Zakat — Almsgiving

Three Types of Nisab for Zakat
Classification of three nisab types with attached rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of nisab in Hanafi fiqh and identify which rulings apply to each.

Core Idea
Not all nisab require growth and a year; the second type triggers four obligations without those conditions.

This passage lays out the Hanafi classification of nisab—the minimum wealth thresholds that trigger various legal obligations and prohibitions. Understanding these three categories is essential for determining when zakat is due, when sacrificial and charity obligations apply, and when begging becomes forbidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first nisab and its conditions
The first nisab requires growth (numuww) and the passing of a lunar year (hawlan al-hawl). It triggers all rulings related to zakat and wealth.
This is the standard nisab for zakat on cash and trade goods.
2
List the four rulings connected to the second nisab
The second nisab does not require growth or the passing of a year, but it triggers four specific rulings: (1) prohibition of taking sadaqah, (2) obligation of sacrifice (qurbani), (3) obligation of sadaqat al-fitr, and (4) obligation to support relatives (nafaqah).
This nisab is often the same amount as the first but without the year condition.
3
Understand the third nisab for begging prohibition
The third nisab is a minimal threshold that makes begging forbidden. According to the Hanafi school, it is having one day's sustenance, or according to some, owning fifty dirhams.
This threshold is lower than the first two and has its own ikhtilaf regarding the exact amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نصاب تین طرح کے ہیں ایک وہ نصاب جس میں نمو شرط ہے اس نصاب کے ساتھ زکوۃ اور مال سے متعلق تمام احکام متعلق ہوتے ہیں۔ دوسرے وہ نصاب جس کے ساتھ چارا حکام متعلق ہوتے ہیں (۱) صدقہ لینے کی حرمت (۲) قربانی کا واجب ہونا ، (۳) صدقہ الفطر کا واجب ہونا ۔ (۴) اور اقارب کا نفقہ ایس نصاب میں نہ نمو شرط ہے نہ تجارت اور نہ حولان حول تیسر انصاب وہ ہے جس سے سوال کرنے کی حرمت ثابت ہوتی ہے یہ وہ ہے جبکہ کسی کے پاس ایک دن کی روزی ہو اور بعض نے کہا کہ پچاس درہم کا مالک ہو تو اس کے لئے سوال کرنا حرام ہے۔
There are three types of nisab: one nisab in which growth (nāw) is a condition; with this nisab, all rulings related to zakat and wealth are connected. Second is the nisab with which four rulings are connected: (1) prohibition of taking sadaqah, (2) obligation of sacrifice, (3) obligation of sadaqat al-fitr, (4) and maintenance of relatives. In this nisab, neither growth nor trade nor the passing of a year is a condition. The third nisab is that from which the prohibition of begging is established. This is when someone has provision for one day, and some have said that if he owns fifty dirhams, then begging is forbidden for him.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the three types of nisab in Hanafi fiqh. The first type is the standard nisab for zakat on wealth, which requires growth (nāw) and the passing of a lunar year (hawlan al-hawl). The second type is a lower nisab that triggers four specific obligations without requiring growth or the passing of a year: it makes receiving zakat forbidden, obligates sacrifice (udhiyah), obligates sadaqat al-fitr, and obligates maintenance of relatives. The third type is a minimal nisab for the prohibition of begging; it is defined as having one day's sustenance or, according to some, owning fifty dirhams. This classification helps determine which legal rules apply to a person's wealth.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisaab): A minimum amount of wealth that triggers certain legal obligations or prohibitions.
نمو (numuww): Growth or potential for increase in wealth, such as profit from trade or increase in livestock.
حولان حول (hawlaan al-hawl): The passing of one lunar year while the nisab is possessed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following rulings is NOT connected to the second type of nisab (the one without growth or passing of year)?
A) Prohibition of taking sadaqah
B) Obligation of zakat on wealth
C) Obligation of sacrifice
D) Obligation of sadaqat al-fitr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes three nisab thresholds: one requiring growth and a year for zakat, one without those for sadaqat al-fitr and other obligations, and a minimal one for the prohibition of begging.

Sadaqat al-Fitr on Oneself: Proof and Ruling
Establishes obligation with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sadaqat al-fitr for oneself, identify the primary proof (hadith of Ibn Umar), and explain why it is wajib rather than fard.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-fitr is wajib on every Muslim sahib al-nisab, proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar.

This passage begins by establishing the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr on every individual. The central proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar, which the Hanafi school interprets as indicating wujub. We will examine the hadith, its textual implications, and how the Hanafi school classifies this obligation based on its usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that one must give sadaqat al-fitr from oneself. Determine the hukm level: wajib. Note that the obligation is on every sahib al-nisab.
The Hanafi school classifies sadaqat al-fitr as wajib, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah ordained zakat al-fitr upon the male and female...' Identify its source (Bukhari and Muslim) and transmission type (ahad).
The hadith is considered ahad by some Hanafi usulis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Arabic word 'farada' (ordained) indicates obligation. However, because the hadith is a single-narrator (ahad) hadith, it yields zann (speculative) certainty. In Hanafi usul, a zanni dalil produces a wujub ruling, not fard (which requires qat'i dalil).
This is why the Hanafi school says wajib, while the Shafi'i school says fard (they consider ahad hadith as qat'i in dalala for obligations).
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers sadaqat al-fitr as fard based on the same hadith, because they hold that ahad hadith can establish fard. The practical difference is minimal, but the epistemological basis differs.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in usul.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: sadaqat al-fitr is wajib on oneself provided one is sahib al-nisab. This is from the zahir al-riwayah and confirmed by later scholars.
No intra-Hanafi dispute on this point.

Source Text

قَالَ يَخْرُجُ لِكَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لِحَدِيثِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ زَكَوةَ الْفِطْرِ عَلَى الذَّكَرِ وَالانْتَى الْحَدِيثَ ترجمہ شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا کہ اس صدقہ کو اپنی طرف سے نکالے کیونکہ ابن عمر کی حدیث ہے کہ فرمایا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے مرد و عورت پر زکوۃ الفطر فرض کیا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ صاحب نصاب پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اپنی جان کا صدقہ ادا کرے دلیل ابن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کی حدیث ہے پوری حدیث یہ ہے فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ زَكوةَ الْفِطْرِ عَلَى الذَّكَرِ و الأنثى وَالْحَرِّ وَالْمَملوك صاعاً مِنْ تَمَر أَوْصَاعاً مِنْ شَعِيرٍ یعنی برحق نبی نے صدقۃ الفطر فرض کیا مرد پر اور عورت پر آزاد پر اور مملوک پر کھجور کا ایک صاع یا جو کا ایک صاع ۔ وَ يَخْرُجُ عَنْ أَوْلَادِهِ الصِّغَارِ لأَنَّ السَّبَبِ رَأْسُ يَمُونُهُ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهَا تُضَافُ إِلَيْهِ يُقَالُ زَكَوةُ الرَّأْسِ وَهِيَ آمَارَةٌ السَّبَيَّةِ وَالْإِضَافَةُ إلَى الْفِطْرِ بِاعْتَبَارِ أَنَّهُ وَقْتُهَا وَلِهَذَا تَتَعَدَّدُ بِتَعَدُّدِ الرَّأْسِ مَعَ اتَّحَادِ الْيَوْمِ وَالْأَصْلُ فِي الْوُجُوبِ رَأْسُهُ وَهُوَ يَمُوتُهُ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِ فَيَلْحَقُ بِه مَا هُوَ فِى مَعَاهُ كَا وَلَادِهِ الصَّغَارِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمُونُهُمْ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِمْ ترجمہ اور نکالے اپنی نابالغ اولاد کی طرف سے کیونکہ صدقہ کا سبب ایسا راس ہے جس کو روز مبینہ دیتا ہے اور اس پر متولی ہے کیونکہ صدقۃ الفطر اس کی طرف منسوب کیا جاتا ہے کہا جاتا ہے زکوۃ الرأس اور یہ اضافت سبب ہونے کی علامت ہے اور فطر کی طرف سے اضافت اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ فطر اس کا وقت ہے اور اسی وجہ سے راُس متعدد ہو جانے سے صدقۃ الفطر متعدد ہو جاتا ہے باوجود یکہ یوم متحد ہے اور وجوب صدقہ میں اصل مالدار کا راس ہے اور وہ اس کو روزینہ دیتا ہے اور اس پر متولی ہے پس اس کے ساتھ ہر وہ راس لاحق کیا جائے گا جو اس کے معنی میں ہو جیسے اس کی نابالغ اولا د اس لئے کہ ددان کو روز بینہ دیتا ہے اور ان پر متولی ہے۔ تشریح - [Al-Quduri] said: He should give it from himself, due to the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah ordained zakat al-fitr upon the male and female.' [The hadith continues:] ... a sa' of dates or a sa' of barley. And he should give on behalf of his minor children because the cause is a head (ra's) that he maintains and has guardianship over. Because it is attributed to him; it is called 'zakat al-ra's'. The attribution to fitr is because it is its time. Therefore it multiplies with the multiplicity of heads despite the unity of the day. The basis of obligation is his head, and he maintains it and has guardianship, so what is like it follows it, such as his minor children, because he maintains them and has guardianship over them.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding sadaqat al-fitr. It begins by stating the obligation on oneself, citing the famous hadith of Ibn Umar. Then it extends the obligation to minor children. The commentary explains the reasoning: the cause (sabab) of obligation is the 'head' (ra's) that one maintains (mu'nah) and has guardianship (wilayah) over. The term 'zakat al-ra's' indicates this. An objection is raised: why is fitr a cause if it is added to fitr? Answer: fitr is the time, not the cause. Another objection: if the cause is the head, why is it repeated annually? Answer: because maintenance (mu'nah) is repeated over time. A final objection: if the cause is the head, why is one not only obligated for oneself but also for children? Answer: because the cause applies to every head that he maintains and has guardianship over. Thus, the father is obligated for his minor children provided he himself is a sahib al-nisab.

Key Terms
رأس (ra's): The person himself/herself; each individual head for whom sadaqat al-fitr is obligated.
مؤنت (mu'nah): Maintenance, expenditure for living expenses.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship, authority over someone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school classify sadaqat al-fitr as wajib rather than fard?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because the hadith of Ibn Umar is ahad and gives zann
C) Because it is only recommended
D) Because the Prophet did not specify the amount

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-fitr is wajib on oneself due to the hadith of Ibn Umar, classified as wajib because the evidence is zanni.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Sadaqat al-Fitr for Minor Children: The Sabab of Mu'nah and Wilayah
Explains the sabab for obligation on behalf of minors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi reasoning that sadaqat al-fitr is wajib on behalf of one's minor children based on the sabab of maintenance (mu'nah) and guardianship (wilayah).

Core Idea
The cause of obligation is the 'head' one maintains and guards; thus, it extends to minor children.

This passage explains why the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr extends to one's minor children. The key is understanding the cause (sabab): it is attached to every 'head' (ra's) that a person maintains and has guardianship over. The author systematically addresses potential objections to this reasoning, clarifying the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the extension
The passage states that one must give sadaqat al-fitr for one's minor children. Note that this is in addition to oneself.
Minor children are those who have not reached puberty.
2
Understand the sabab
The sabab (cause) of obligation is the 'head' (ra's) that one provides maintenance (mu'nah) for and has guardianship (wilayah) over. This is supported by the term 'zakat al-ra's'.
The attribution to fitr (fitr) is only the time, not the cause.
3
Analyze the proof from attribution
The phrase 'zakat al-ra's' shows that the obligation is linked to the head, not to the day. The attribution to fitr indicates timing. This is proven because the obligation multiplies with multiple heads even on the same day.
If fitr were the cause, it would be one payment per person per day, but the multiple head argument shows it's per head.
4
Examine the objections and responses
Three objections are raised: (1) Why is fitr mentioned? Answer: time not cause. (2) If head is cause, why isn't it only once in a lifetime? Answer: mu'nah repeats. (3) If head is cause, why obligation for others? Answer: because the cause applies to each head under one's mu'nah and wilayah.
These objections strengthen the reasoning by clarifying misconceptions.
5
Apply the rule
The rule is: any individual (head) that one maintains and has guardianship over, sadaqat al-fitr is wajib upon the maintainer/guardian. This includes minor children and slaves (as mentioned in the hadith).
For adult dependents who are not under guardianship (like a wife who owns nisab), the rule does not apply.

قَالَ يَخْرُجُ لِكَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لِحَدِيثِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ زَكَوةَ الْفِطْرِ عَلَى الذَّكَرِ وَالانْتَى الْحَدِيثَ ترجمہ شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا کہ اس صدقہ کو اپنی طرف سے نکالے کیونکہ ابن عمر کی حدیث ہے کہ فرمایا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے مرد و عورت پر زکوۃ الفطر فرض کیا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ صاحب نصاب پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اپنی جان کا صدقہ ادا کرے دلیل ابن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کی حدیث ہے پوری حدیث یہ ہے فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ زَكوةَ الْفِطْرِ عَلَى الذَّكَرِ و الأنثى وَالْحَرِّ وَالْمَملوك صاعاً مِنْ تَمَر أَوْصَاعاً مِنْ شَعِيرٍ یعنی برحق نبی نے صدقۃ الفطر فرض کیا مرد پر اور عورت پر آزاد پر اور مملوک پر کھجور کا ایک صاع یا جو کا ایک صاع ۔ وَ يَخْرُجُ عَنْ أَوْلَادِهِ الصِّغَارِ لأَنَّ السَّبَبِ رَأْسُ يَمُونُهُ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهَا تُضَافُ إِلَيْهِ يُقَالُ زَكَوةُ الرَّأْسِ وَهِيَ آمَارَةٌ السَّبَيَّةِ وَالْإِضَافَةُ إلَى الْفِطْرِ بِاعْتَبَارِ أَنَّهُ وَقْتُهَا وَلِهَذَا تَتَعَدَّدُ بِتَعَدُّدِ الرَّأْسِ مَعَ اتَّحَادِ الْيَوْمِ وَالْأَصْلُ فِي الْوُجُوبِ رَأْسُهُ وَهُوَ يَمُوتُهُ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِ فَيَلْحَقُ بِه مَا هُوَ فِى مَعَاهُ كَا وَلَادِهِ الصَّغَارِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمُونُهُمْ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِمْ ترجمہ اور نکالے اپنی نابالغ اولاد کی طرف سے کیونکہ صدقہ کا سبب ایسا راس ہے جس کو روز مبینہ دیتا ہے اور اس پر متولی ہے کیونکہ صدقۃ الفطر اس کی طرف منسوب کیا جاتا ہے کہا جاتا ہے زکوۃ الرأس اور یہ اضافت سبب ہونے کی علامت ہے اور فطر کی طرف سے اضافت اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ فطر اس کا وقت ہے اور اسی وجہ سے راُس متعدد ہو جانے سے صدقۃ الفطر متعدد ہو جاتا ہے باوجود یکہ یوم متحد ہے اور وجوب صدقہ میں اصل مالدار کا راس ہے اور وہ اس کو روزینہ دیتا ہے اور اس پر متولی ہے پس اس کے ساتھ ہر وہ راس لاحق کیا جائے گا جو اس کے معنی میں ہو جیسے اس کی نابالغ اولا د اس لئے کہ ددان کو روز بینہ دیتا ہے اور ان پر متولی ہے۔ تشریح - مسئلہ - مقدار نصاب کا مالک اپنی نا بالغ اولاد کی طرف سے بھی صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کا سبب ایسا راس اور ایسی ذات ہے جس پر آدمی خرچ کرتا ہے اور اس پر متولی ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر کور اس کی طرف مضاف کر کے زکوۃ الرآس کہا جاتا ہے اور شئی کی طرف اضافت اس کے سبب ہونے کی علامت ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کا سبب رأس اور ذات ہے لیکن اگر کوئی اعتراض کرے کہ اضافت تو فطر کی جانب بھی کی جاتی ہے چنانچہ صدقۃ الفطر کہا جاتا ہے لہذا اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ فطر بھی صدقہ واجب ہونے کا سبب ہے حالانکہ تمہارے نزدیک ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فطر کی جانب اضافت اس لئے نہیں کہ فطر اس کا سبب ہے بلکہ اس لئے ہے کہ فطر اس کا وقت ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ راُس اور ذوات کے متعدد ہونے سے صدقات متعدد ہو جاتے ہیں حالانکہ یوم فطر ایک ہی ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ راس ہی سبب ہے اور سب کے متعدد ہونے سے مسبب متعدد ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر کوئی یہ سوال کرے کہ رائس اور ذات اگر وجوب صدقہ کا سبب ہے تو ایک آدمی پر پوری زندگی میں ایک ہی صدقہ واجب ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ پوری زندگی میں راس ایک ہی رہتا ہے ہر سال واجب نہ ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ آپ ہر سال صدقہ واجب کرتے ہیں جواب ہر اس مطلقا وجوب صدقہ کا سبب نہیں ہے بلکہ وصف مونت کے ساتھ موصوف ہو کر سبب ہے اور مونت زمانہ کے گذرنے سے مکرر ہو جاتی ہے پس وصف مونت مکرر ہونے سے راس حکما متکرر کے مانند ہو گیا پس جب رأس ) سبب ( مکر رہو گیا تو صدقۃ الفطر بھی مکر رہو جائے گا فلا اشکال۔ اور اگر کوئی یہ سوال کرے کہ وجوب صدقہ کا سبب اگر راس ہے تو صاحب نصاب پر خود اپنا صدقہ واجب ہونا چاہئے نہ کہ اولا وصغار اور ممالیک کا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر کے وجوب میں اصل تو مالک نصاب کا راس ہے کیونکہ وہ اس پر خرچ کرتا ہے اور اس کا متولی ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ وجوب صدقہ کا سبب راس یعنی ذات کا خرچ برداشت کرنا۔ اور اس پر متولی ہونا ہے۔ اب جس جگہ مؤنت ولایت پائی جائے گی وہی مالدار کے ساتھ لاحق ہوگا مثلا اولا دصغار کہ باپ ہی ان کی مؤنت برداشت کرتا ہے اور باپ ہی ان پر متولی ہوتا ہے اس لئے اولاد صغار کا صدقۃ الفطر بھی باپ پر واجب ہوگا بشرطیکہ باپ مالک نصاب ہو۔
[Al-Quduri] said: He should give it from himself, due to the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah ordained zakat al-fitr upon the male and female.' [The hadith continues:] ... a sa' of dates or a sa' of barley. And he should give on behalf of his minor children because the cause is a head (ra's) that he maintains and has guardianship over. Because it is attributed to him; it is called 'zakat al-ra's'. The attribution to fitr is because it is its time. Therefore it multiplies with the multiplicity of heads despite the unity of the day. The basis of obligation is his head, and he maintains it and has guardianship, so what is like it follows it, such as his minor children, because he maintains them and has guardianship over them.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding sadaqat al-fitr. It begins by stating the obligation on oneself, citing the famous hadith of Ibn Umar. Then it extends the obligation to minor children. The commentary explains the reasoning: the cause (sabab) of obligation is the 'head' (ra's) that one maintains (mu'nah) and has guardianship (wilayah) over. The term 'zakat al-ra's' indicates this. An objection is raised: why is fitr a cause if it is added to fitr? Answer: fitr is the time, not the cause. Another objection: if the cause is the head, why is it repeated annually? Answer: because maintenance (mu'nah) is repeated over time. A final objection: if the cause is the head, why is one not only obligated for oneself but also for children? Answer: because the cause applies to every head that he maintains and has guardianship over. Thus, the father is obligated for his minor children provided he himself is a sahib al-nisab.

Key Terms
رأس (ra's): The person himself/herself; each individual head for whom sadaqat al-fitr is obligated.
مؤنت (mu'nah): Maintenance, expenditure for living expenses.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship, authority over someone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary cause (sabab) for the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr for minors according to the Hanafi school?
A) The day of Fitr
B) The minor's own nisab
C) The guardian's maintenance (mu'nah) and guardianship (wilayah) over the minor
D) The minor's fasting in Ramadan

Key Takeaway
The obligation for minor children stems from the same cause: maintenance and guardianship over the child's 'head' (ra's).

Sadaqat al-Fitr for Slaves and Dispute on Minor's Wealth
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sadaqat al-fitr for minors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sadaqat al-fitr for slaves and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on paying from a minor's wealth, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For a minor with wealth, sadaqat al-fitr is paid from his own wealth according to the two shaykhs, not the father's.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two related issues: the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr for slaves, and the disputed question of who pays for a minor child when the child possesses wealth. The passage clarifies that the master pays for his slaves (if they are for service), but for a minor, the answer depends on which Hanafi authority you follow. We will unpack the reasoning behind each position and identify the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for slaves
The text states that sadaqat al-fitr for slaves (mamaleek) is wajib on the master. Note the condition: the slaves must be for service, not trade. This is a clear ruling with a condition.
If slaves are for trade, zakat applies instead.
2
Identify the dispute on minor's wealth
The passage then moves to minor children (sighar). It states: if the minor has no wealth, the father pays. But if the minor has wealth, there is a difference between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
State each position and its proof
The two shaykhs hold that payment is from the child's own wealth. Imam Muhammad holds that it is from the father's wealth. The text gives Imam Muhammad's reasoning: 'because the law made it like maintenance (mu'nah), similar to nafaqah'.
The two shaykhs' proof is not explicitly stated but implied: sadaqat al-fitr is an ibadah that can be discharged from the minor's property, unlike nafaqah which is the father's duty regardless.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a minor has 100 dinars, according to the two shaykhs, the father pays from that 100 dinars, preserving his own money. According to Imam Muhammad, the father must pay from his own pocket, and the child's wealth remains untouched.
This affects the father's financial planning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates the relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs. Most Hanafi fatwa works follow this, although Imam Muhammad's view is also recognised as a legitimate variant.
The term 'indahima' (with them) signals preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَمَالِيكِهِ لِقِيَامِ الْمُؤْنَةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانُوا لِلْخِدَمَةِ وَلَامَالَ  ِللصَّغَارِ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُمْ مَالُ يُؤَدِى مِنْ مَالِهِمْ عِندَ أبي حَنِيقَةً وَ أبِى يُوسُفَ خِلافا لمُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّ الشَّرعَ أَجْرَاهُ مَجْرَى المَونَةِ فَاشية النفقة ترجمہ اور اپنے مملوکوں کی طرف سے صدقہ نکالے کیونکہ مونت اور ولایت قائم ہے اور یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ خدمت کے لئے ہوں اور اولادصغار کا خود کچھ مال نہ ہو۔ اور اگر اولادصغار کے پاس مال ہو تو ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ان کے مال سے ادا کیا جائے امام محمد کا اختلاف سے کیونکہ شریعت نے اس صدقہ کو مؤنت کے قائم مقام کیا ہے لہذا یہ نفقہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ ممالیک یعنی غلام مدبر ، ام ولد کا صدقہ اس کے مولیٰ پر واجب ہے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کا خرچ بھی مولی برداشت کرتا ہے اور ان پر ولایت بھی مولی کو حاصل ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ممالیک کا صدقہ مولی پر اس وقت واجب ہے جبکہ وہ خدمت کے لئے ہوں کیونکہ اگر وہ تجارت کے لئے ہوں تو زکوۃ واجب ہے نہ کہ صدقۃ الفطر اور اولادصغار کا صدقہ باپ پر اس وقت واجب ہے جبکہ اولاد صغار کے پاس مال قطعا موجود نہ ہواور اگر اولاد صغار کے پاس مال موجود ہو تو شیخین کے نزدیک انہیں کے مال سے ان کا صدقہ ادا کیا جائے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اولاد صغار کے مال سے صدقہ ادا نہ کرے بلکہ باپ خود اپنے مال سے ادا کرے حتی کہ اگر باپ نے اولاد
And on behalf of his slaves, because maintenance and guardianship exist. This is when they are for service and the minor children have no wealth. If they have wealth, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is paid from their wealth, contrary to Muhammad, because the law made it run in the course of maintenance, similar to spending (nafaqah).
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the payment of sadaqat al-fitr for minor children who possess wealth. The text first establishes the rule for slaves: the master is obligated for his slaves (including mudabbar and umm walad) provided they are for service (not trade). Then it states that the same condition applies to minor children: if they have no wealth, the father pays. But if they have wealth, there is a difference. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf say it should be paid from the minor's own wealth. Imam Muhammad disagrees; he argues that sadaqat al-fitr is akin to maintenance (nafaqah) and therefore should be paid by the guardian (father), not from the child's wealth. Al-Hidayah notes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) for minors with wealth, though Imam Muhammad's view is also considered.

Key Terms
ممالیک (mamaleek): Slaves, including mudabbar (whose emancipation is deferred) and umm walad (slave mother of her master's child).
مؤنت (mu'nah): Maintenance; the principle that sadaqat al-fitr is treated like maintenance expenses.
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, if a minor child possesses wealth, from where is his sadaqat al-fitr paid?
A) From the father's wealth
B) From the child's own wealth
C) From the mother's wealth
D) It is not obligatory for the minor

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sadaqat al-fitr for a minor with wealth is paid from the child's own wealth, based on the preferred view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

The Cause of Sadaqat al-Fitr: Person and Maintenance
Talil analysis of the sabab of Sadaqat al-Fitr, answering objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sabab of Sadaqat al-Fitr and explain why it is wajib annually and on the guardian for dependents.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr repeats yearly because its cause is the person qualified by maintenance, which renews annually.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah delves into the legal cause (sabab) that makes Sadaqat al-Fitr wajib. The author establishes that the person (ra's) is the primary locus of obligation, but it becomes an effective cause only when combined with the attribute of maintenance (maw'nat). He then answers three logical objections to clarify why the cause leads to annual repetition and why the guardian must pay for dependents. Understanding this cause is key to applying the ruling correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab
Locate where the passage states that the cause for Sadaqat al-Fitr being wajib is the head/self (ra's/dhat). Note that the name 'Zakat al-Ra's' indicates this.
The author argues that adding 'ra's' shows it is the cause, not the time (fitr).
2
Analyze the first objection (Fitr as cause)
Consider the objection that 'Sadaqat al-Fitr' might imply fitr is the cause. The answer: fitr is the time, not the cause. Multiplicity of persons causes multiplicity of sadaqat, not the single day.
This refutes the Shafi'i view that the day is the cause.
3
Analyze the second objection (annual repetition)
Why is it wajib every year and not once in a lifetime? The answer: the cause is not the person alone, but the person qualified by maintenance, which recurs annually with the passage of time.
Maintenance (maw'nat) is a renewable attribute.
4
Analyze the third objection (guardian's obligation for dependents)
Why does the guardian pay for minor children and slaves? Because the cause of obligation is the person who bears maintenance and has guardianship (wilaya). Thus, the father must pay for his dependents.
Condition: the guardian must be an owner of nisab.

كتاب التركوة کر کے زکوۃ الرآس کہا جاتا ہے اور شئی کی طرف اضافت اس کے سبب ہونے کی علامت ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کا سبب رأس اور ذات ہے لیکن اگر کوئی اعتراض کرے کہ اضافت تو فطر کی جانب بھی کی جاتی ہے چنانچہ صدقۃ الفطر کہا جاتا ہے لہذا اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ فطر بھی صدقہ واجب ہونے کا سبب ہے حالانکہ تمہارے نزدیک ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فطر کی جانب اضافت اس لئے نہیں کہ فطر اس کا سبب ہے بلکہ اس لئے ہے کہ فطر اس کا وقت ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ راُس اور ذوات کے متعدد ہونے سے صدقات متعدد ہو جاتے ہیں حالانکہ یوم فطر ایک ہی ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ راس ہی سبب ہے اور سب کے متعدد ہونے سے مسبب متعدد ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر کوئی یہ سوال کرے کہ رائس اور ذات اگر وجوب صدقہ کا سبب ہے تو ایک آدمی پر پوری زندگی میں ایک ہی صدقہ واجب ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ پوری زندگی میں راس ایک ہی رہتا ہے ہر سال واجب نہ ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ آپ ہر سال صدقہ واجب کرتے ہیں جواب ہر اس مطلقا وجوب صدقہ کا سبب نہیں ہے بلکہ وصف مونت کے ساتھ موصوف ہو کر سبب ہے اور مونت زمانہ کے گذرنے سے مکرر ہو جاتی ہے پس وصف مونت مکرر ہونے سے راس حکما متکرر کے مانند ہو گیا پس جب رأس ) سبب ) مکر رہو گیا تو صدقۃ الفطر بھی مکر رہو جائے گا فلا اشکال۔
 اور اگر کوئی یہ سوال کرے کہ وجوب صدقہ کا سبب اگر راس ہے تو صاحب نصاب پر خود اپنا صدقہ واجب ہونا چاہئے نہ کہ اولا وصغار اور ممالیک کا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر کے وجوب میں اصل تو مالک نصاب کا راس ہے کیونکہ وہ اس پر خرچ کرتا ہے اور اس کا متولی ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ وجوب صدقہ کا سبب راس یعنی ذات کا خرچ برداشت کرنا۔ اور اس پر متولی ہونا ہے۔ اب جس جگہ مؤنت ولایت پائی جائے گی وہی مالدار کے ساتھ لاحق ہوگا مثلا اولاد صغار کہ باپ ہی ان کی مؤنت برداشت کرتا ہے اور باپ ہی ان پر متولی ہوتا ہے اس لئے اولاد صغار کا صدقۃ الفطر بھی باپ پر واجب ہوگا بشرطیکہ باپ مالک نصاب ہو۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary volume three. The book of Zakat. It is called Zakat al-Ra's (head zakat), and the addition to a thing indicates that it is the cause. So it became known that the cause for Sadaqat al-Fitr being wajib is the head (ra's) and the self (dhat). But if someone objects: 'Addition is also made to Fitr, as it is called Sadaqat al-Fitr, so this means that Fitr is also a cause for the obligation of Sadaqah, but you do not hold that.' The answer is: The addition to Fitr is not because Fitr is the cause, but because Fitr is its time. For this reason, when the heads and selves are multiple, the sadaqat become multiple, even though the day of Fitr is one. So it is known that the head is the cause, and the multiplicity of the cause causes the multiplicity of the effect. If someone asks: 'If the head and self are the cause of the obligation of Sadaqah, then a person should be obligated only once in a lifetime, because the head remains one throughout life; it should not be wajib every year, but you make it wajib every year.' The answer: The head is not the cause of the obligation absolutely; rather it becomes the cause by being qualified with the attribute of maintenance (maw'nat), and maintenance is repeated by the passage of time. So by the repetition of the attribute of maintenance, the head becomes as if repeated. Thus, when the cause (head) becomes repeated, Sadaqat al-Fitr also becomes repeated, so no problem. And if someone asks: 'If the cause of obligation is the head, then the owner of nisab should pay his own sadaqah, not that of his minor children and slaves.' The answer: In the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr, the basis is the head of the owner of nisab, because he spends on them and is their guardian. So it is established that the cause of obligation is the head, i.e., bearing the expenses and being the guardian. So wherever maintenance and guardianship are found, they will attach to the wealthy person. For example, minor children: the father bears their maintenance and is their guardian, so Sadaqat al-Fitr for minor children is also wajib upon the father, provided that the father is an owner of nisab.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a detailed talil (cause analysis) regarding Sadaqat al-Fitr. The author establishes that the cause (sabab) of wajib for Sadaqat al-Fitr is the person (ra's/dhat) combined with maintenance (maw'nat). He first refutes an objection that 'Fitr' (breaking the fast) might be the cause because the name includes 'Fitr'. He clarifies that fitr is just the time, not the cause. Then he addresses why it repeats yearly: the person alone is not the cause; it is the person plus the attribute of maintenance, which recurs with the passing of each year. Finally, he explains why the obligation falls on the head of the household for dependents: because the cause is maintenance and guardianship (wilaya). Thus, the father pays for his minor children because he bears their maintenance and guardianship. This is a foundational discussion for the specific rulings that follow.

Key Terms
رأس (ra's): The person or self; the individual for whom Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib.
مونت (maw'nat): Maintenance or expenses; the condition that, when combined with the person, creates the cause for Sadaqat al-Fitr.
ولایت (wilaya): Guardianship or authority over another; required along with maintenance for the obligation to fall on the guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the sabab (cause) for the wajib of Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) The day of Fitr (Eid)
B) The person (ra's) alone
C) The person combined with the attribute of maintenance (maw'nat)
D) The birth of a child

Key Takeaway
The cause of Sadaqat al-Fitr is the person qualified by maintenance, leading to annual repetition and obligation on the guardian for dependents.

Sadaqat al-Fitr for Slaves and Minors: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the source of payment for Sadaqat al-Fitr of minor children with wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Sadaqat al-Fitr on behalf of slaves and minor children, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding whether to pay from the minor's wealth or the guardian's wealth, along with the proofs of each side.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr is like maintenance: if the minor has wealth, it is paid from that wealth, per Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

This passage from al-Hidayah deals with Sadaqat al-Fitr for dependents. The general rule is that the guardian pays for slaves and minors. However, a dispute arises when the minor child possesses wealth: should the father pay from the child's wealth or his own? The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold one view, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds another. Understanding their proofs will sharpen your skill in evaluating intra-madhhab tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is Sadaqat al-Fitr for dependents (slaves and minor children). The general ruling is that it is wajib upon the guardian (master/father) when the dependent has no wealth.
This ruling applies only if the slaves are for service, not trade.
2
Distinguish slaves for service vs. trade
For slaves used in trade, Zakat al-Mal is wajib on the slave's value, not Sadaqat al-Fitr. For service slaves, Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib on the master due to maintenance and guardianship.
This distinction is specific to the Hanafi school.
3
State the default ruling for minors without wealth
If a minor child has no wealth, the father must pay Sadaqat al-Fitr from his own money. This is uncontested.
4
Present the dispute regarding minors with wealth
When the minor has sufficient wealth, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that the father should pay from the child's wealth. Imam Muhammad holds that the father must pay from his own wealth and is liable if he pays from the child's wealth.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Analyse the proofs and determine the mufta bihi
Imam Muhammad argues Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat — not obligatory on a minor's wealth — and is an act of worship. The two shaykhs argue it is treated as maintenance (nafaqah) by the Law, so it follows the rules of nafaqah: if the minor has wealth, obligation is on that wealth. Later scholars prefer the view of the two shaykhs, making it mufta bihi.
The analogy to nafaqah is the stronger talil according to the majority of Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَمَالِيكِهِ لِقِيَامِ الْمُؤْنَةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانُوا لِلْخِدَمَةِ وَلَامَالَ ِللصَّغَارِ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُمْ مَالُ يُؤَدِى مِنْ مَالِهِمْ عِندَ أبي حَنِيقَةً وَ أبِى يُوسُفَ خِلافا لمُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّ الشَّرعَ أَجۡرَاهُ مَجۡرَى المَونَةِ فَاشيَة النَّفَقَةِ
ترجمہ اور اپنے مملوکوں کی طرف سے صدقہ نکالے کیونکہ مونت اور ولایت قائم ہے اور یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ خدمت کے لئے ہوں اور اولادصغار کا خود کچھ مال نہ ہو۔ اور اگر اولادصغار کے پاس مال ہو تو ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ان کے مال سے ادا کیا جائے امام محمد کا اختلاف سے کیونکہ شریعت نے اس صدقہ کو مؤنت کے قائم مقام کیا ہے لہذا یہ نفقہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ ممالیک یعنی غلام مدبر ، ام ولد کا صدقہ اس کے مولیٰ پر واجب ہے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کا خرچ بھی مولی برداشت کرتا ہے اور ان پر ولایت بھی مولی کو حاصل ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ممالیک کا صدقہ مولی پر اس وقت واجب ہے جبکہ وہ خدمت کے لئے ہوں کیونکہ اگر وہ تجارت کے لئے ہوں تو زکوۃ واجب ہے نہ کہ صدقۃ الفطر اور اولادصغار کا صدقہ باپ پر اس وقت واجب ہے جبکہ اولاد صغار کے پاس مال قطعا موجود نہ ہواور اگر اولاد صغار کے پاس مال موجود ہو تو شیخین کے نزدیک انہیں کے مال سے ان کا صدقہ ادا کیا جائے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اولاد صغار کے مال سے صدقہ ادا نہ کرے بلکہ باپ خود اپنے مال سے ادا کرے حتی کہ اگر باپ نے اولاد صغار کے مال سے ادا کر دیا تو باپ اس کا ضامن ہو گا۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر شریعت میں زکوۃ ہے جیسا کہ مال کی زکوۃ اور صغیر کے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی لہذا صدقۃ الفطر بھی اس کے مال میں واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر عبادت ہے اور صغیر وجوب عبادت کا اہل نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کے مال میں صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر شرعا مونت کے قائم مقام ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ آدمی پر اس کے غیر کی جانب سے صدقہ واجب کیا جاتا ہے پس صدقۃ الفطر نفقہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور صغیر کے پاس اگر مال ہو تو اس کا نفقہ اسی کے مال میں واجب ہوتا ہے پس اسی طرح اس کا صدقہ بھی اس کے مال میں واجب ہوگا بشرطیکہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہو۔
And from his slaves [he pays] due to the establishment of maintenance and guardianship. This applies when they are for service and the minors have no wealth. If they have wealth, it is paid from their wealth according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, because the Law has treated it in the place of maintenance, so it resembles obligatory maintenance. Translation: And he should give Sadaqah for his slaves because maintenance and guardianship are established. This ruling applies when they are for service and minor children have no wealth. And if minor children have property, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it should be paid from their property, with disagreement from Imam Muhammad, because the Law has made this Sadaqah a substitute for maintenance, so it resembles obligatory maintenance. Explanation: The Sadaqah for slaves—such as a mudabbar, umm walad—is wajib upon the master, and the proof is that the master bears their expenses and has guardianship over them. The author of al-Hidayah states that the Sadaqah for slaves is wajib upon the master when they are for service, because if they are for trade, zakat is wajib, not Sadaqat al-Fitr. And the Sadaqah for minor children is wajib upon the father when the minor children have absolutely no wealth. And if minor children have wealth, then according to the two shaykhs, their Sadaqah should be paid from their own wealth, whereas Imam Muhammad holds that the Sadaqah should not be paid from the minor children's wealth; rather the father should pay from his own property, to the extent that if the father pays from the minor children's wealth, the father becomes a guarantor. Imam Muhammad's proof is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is zakat in the Law, just like zakat on property, and zakat is not wajib on the wealth of a minor, so Sadaqat al-Fitr also will not be wajib on his wealth. A second proof is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is an act of worship, and a minor is not capable of the obligation of worship, so Sadaqah is not wajib on his wealth. The proof of the two shaykhs is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is made a substitute for maintenance by the Law, which is why it is made wajib upon a person on behalf of another. Thus, Sadaqat al-Fitr resembles maintenance, and if a minor has wealth, his maintenance is wajib from his own wealth, so similarly his Sadaqah will be wajib from his wealth, provided he has wealth.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the payment of Sadaqat al-Fitr for slaves and minor children. The author first states the general rule: a master pays for his slaves (whether mudabbar or umm walad) because he bears their maintenance and has full guardianship, but only if the slaves are for service (not trade). For minor children, the father pays if they have no wealth. If the minor children have wealth, then Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that the father should pay from the child's wealth. Imam Muhammad disagrees, arguing that Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat, which is not obligatory on a minor's wealth, and that it is an act of worship for which a minor is not accountable. The two shaykhs counter that Sadaqat al-Fitr is treated as a maintenance expense (nafaqah) by the Law, so it follows the same ruling as nafaqah: if the minor has wealth, it is taken from that wealth. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the view of the two shaykhs, as maintenance is a stronger analogy.

Key Terms
ممالیک (mamalik): Slaves owned by a master, including mudabbar (slave promised freedom after master's death) and umm walad (slave mother of master's child).
اولاد صغار (awlad sighar): Minor children who are under the guardianship of the father.
مؤنت (maw'nat): Maintenance; the basis for obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr on the guardian for dependents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a minor child has wealth, where should Sadaqat al-Fitr be paid from?
A) The father's own wealth
B) The minor's wealth
C) The state treasury
D) It is not wajib at all

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr for dependents is wajib on the guardian, but when the minor has wealth, the relied-upon view is to pay from that wealth, treating it as maintenance.

Adult Children: Father Not Obligated to Pay Sadaqat al-Fitr
Stating the rule for adult children's Sadaqat al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a father is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for adult children and explain when voluntary payment is valid by istihsan.

Core Idea
A father is not obligated to pay for adult children, but if he pays voluntarily, it is valid by istihsan due to customary permission.

This passage clarifies the scope of a father's obligation to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his children. While minor children fall under his guardianship, adult children do not. However, if a father voluntarily pays on behalf of his adult child, the payment is considered valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because customarily the child would consent. This ruling highlights the interplay between obligation (wujub) and validity (sihha) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a father paying Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children. The ruling is that it is not obligatory for the father. Determine the exact hukm level.
The passage states the father is not required to pay, but if he does, it is valid.
2
Understand the legal cause
The absence of obligation is due to lack of guardianship (wilaya) over adult children. Guardianship is necessary for compulsion in financial obligations.
Minor children are under the father's guardianship, so he is obligated.
3
Examine the exception by istihsan
Although not obligatory, if the father pays voluntarily without explicit permission, it fulfills the child's duty. This is allowed by istihsan because permission is customarily assumed.
Istihsan overrides strict analogy here to facilitate the act of worship.
4
Contrast with minor children
For minor children, the father is obligated to pay because he has guardianship. This contrast helps define the boundary of the rule.
The passage only mentions adult children; the minor rule is implied.
5
Apply to a real scenario
Consider a father with a 25-year-old son living at home, unemployed. The father is not required to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for him. However, if the father pays voluntarily, the son's obligation is discharged.
This shows the practical difference between obligation and validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا عَنْ أَوْلَادِهِ الْكِبَارِ وَإِن كَانُوا فِى عَالِهِ لِإِنْعِدَامِ الْوِلَايَةِ وَلَوْاَدُّى عَنْهُمْ أوْ عَنْ زَوْجَتِه بِغَيْرِ أمْرِ هِم أَجَزَاهُم استِحْسَانًا لِتَبُوتِ الْإِذْنَ عَادَةً
ترجمہ اور نہ ادا کرے اپنی بالغ اولاد کی طرف سے اگر چہ وہ اس کے عیال میں ہوں کیونکہ ولایت معدوم ہے اور اگر ان کی طرف سے
And not from his adult children, even if they are in his household, due to the absence of guardianship. And if he pays on their behalf or on behalf of his wife without their command, it is valid for them by istihsan because permission is customary established. Translation: And he should not pay from his adult children, even if they are his dependents, because guardianship is absent. And if he pays on their behalf or on behalf of his wife without their command, it is valid by istihsan because permission is customarily established.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a father is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children (i.e., those who have reached puberty), even if they live in his household and he supports them. The reason is that guardianship (wilaya) over adult children is absent; a father cannot compel them. However, if the father voluntarily pays on their behalf without their explicit permission, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because customarily the children would consent to such payment. This is a subtle point: the obligation is removed, but the act is valid if done. The passage also mentions that the same applies to paying for the wife without her command, though that was already covered in the previous lesson. The last part of the Urdu text is cut off in the OCR, but the Arabic provides the complete ruling.

Key Terms
اولاد كبار (awlad kibar): Adult children who have reached puberty, even if they still live with and are supported by the father.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a secondary source of law that allows a departure from strict analogy for reasons of custom or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a father pays Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult child without the child's explicit permission, what is the ruling?
A) It is invalid because permission is required
B) It is valid by istihsan because customary permission exists
C) It is wajib on the father anyway
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
A father is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for adult children, but voluntary payment is valid by istihsan due to customary permission.

Sadaqat al-Fitr from a Minor's Wealth: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Sadaqat al-Fitr from minor's wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn regarding Sadaqat al-Fitr from a minor's wealth and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib from a minor's wealth because it resembles maintenance, not zakat.

This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school. Imam Muhammad argues that Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat and thus not wajib on minors, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) argue it is like nafaqah and therefore wajib if the minor has wealth. The relied-upon position follows the Shaykhayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
State the exact legal question: Is Sadaqat al-Fitr wajib from the wealth of a minor child who has not reached puberty?
2
State Imam Muhammad's Position
Imam Muhammad holds that Sadaqat al-Fitr is NOT wajib from a minor's wealth. Note his two proofs: (1) It is like zakat, and zakat is not wajib on minors; (2) It is worship, and minors are not capable of worship obligations.
These proofs rely on analogy and the nature of worship.
3
State the Shaykhayn's Position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that Sadaqat al-Fitr IS wajib from a minor's wealth if he has means. Their proof: Sadaqat al-Fitr is like maintenance (nafaqah), which is wajib from the minor's own wealth when available.
They base this on the function of Sadaqat al-Fitr as a substitute for maintenance.
4
Analyze the Analogies
Compare the two analogies: zakat vs. nafaqah. Which one better captures the nature of Sadaqat al-Fitr? The Shaykhayn point to the fact that a person can pay on behalf of another, similar to nafaqah.
The opening sentence about the father being guarantor hints that payment from minor's wealth is not automatic without liability.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi View
Later Hanafi scholarship (e.g., Al-Hidayah) prefers the Shaykhayn's view. Thus the operative ruling is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib from a minor's wealth if the minor has sufficient means.
The practical consequence: the guardian must pay from the minor's wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صغار کے مال سے ادا کر دیا تو باپ اس کا ضامن ہو گا۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر شریعت میں زکوۃ ہے جیسا کہ مال کی زکوۃ اور صغیر کے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی لہذا صدقۃ الفطر بھی اس کے مال میں واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر عبادت ہے اور صغیر وجوب عبادت کا اہل نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کے مال میں صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر شرعا مونت کے قائم مقام ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ آدمی پر اس کے غیر کی جانب سے صدقہ واجب کیا جاتا ہے پس صدقۃ الفطر نفقہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور صغیر کے پاس اگر مال ہو تو اس کا نفقہ اسی کے مال میں واجب ہوتا ہے پس اسی طرح اس کا صدقہ بھی اس کے مال میں واجب ہوگا بشرطیکہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہو۔
If he paid from the wealth of minors, the father will be guarantor for it. The proof of Imam Muhammad is that Sadaqat al-Fitr in Shariah is zakat, like zakat on wealth, and zakat is not wajib on the wealth of a minor, so Sadaqat al-Fitr will also not be wajib on his wealth. The second proof is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is an act of worship, and a minor is not capable of obligation of worship, so Sadaqah will not be wajib on his wealth. The proof of the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that Sadaqat al-Fitr in Shariah stands in the place of maintenance (moonat). This is why a person is obligated to pay Sadaqah on behalf of someone else. Thus Sadaqat al-Fitr resembles nafaqah. If a minor has wealth, his nafaqah is wajib from his wealth. Similarly, his Sadaqah will be wajib from his wealth, provided he has wealth.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Sadaqat al-Fitr from a minor's wealth. Imam Muhammad argues that Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat; zakat is not wajib on a minor's wealth, so Sadaqat al-Fitr is also not wajib. He also argues that it is an act of worship, and minors are not qualified for worship obligations. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) counter that Sadaqat al-Fitr is like maintenance (nafaqah). Since a minor's nafaqah is taken from his own wealth when available, Sadaqat al-Fitr should similarly be taken from his wealth. The passage does not specify which view is mufta bihi, but later Hanafi works adopt the Shaykhayn's view. The opening sentence implies that if a father pays Sadaqat al-Fitr from the minor's wealth without proper justification, he guarantees it, indicating that payment from minor's wealth is not automatically valid without the minor's liability.

Key Terms
صغار (sighar): Minor children who have not reached puberty
مونت (moonat): Maintenance expenses, especially nafaqah
شيخين (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn, why is Sadaqat al-Fitr wajib on the wealth of a minor child?
A) Because it is an act of worship and minors are obligated
B) Because it is like zakat on wealth
C) Because it is in place of maintenance (nafaqah)
D) Because the father has guardianship

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib from a minor's wealth because it is considered maintenance for which the minor's wealth is liable.

Husband Not Obliged for Wife's Sadaqat al-Fitr
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a husband's obligation for his wife's Sadaqat al-Fitr and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
A husband is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his wife because his guardianship and maintenance are incomplete.

This lesson examines a specific inter-madhhab dispute: whether a husband must pay Sadaqat al-Fitr (Fitrana) on behalf of his wife. The Hanafi school rules that he is not obligated, based on the deficiency of both guardianship (wilayah) and maintenance (moonah). We will analyze the reasoning, the Shafi'i objection citing a hadith, and the Hanafi response that interprets 'maintenance' as complete maintenance, which the husband does not provide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the husband's obligation to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his wife. The Hanafi ruling is that it is not wajib.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof is not a direct text but an inference: Sadaqat al-Fitr requires complete wilayah and complete moonah. The husband's wilayah is restricted to marital rights (not a general guardianship), and his moonah only covers basic necessities (not medical treatment or other expenses). Hence both are deficient.
This is a form of istidlal by absence of a condition.
3
Identify the Shafi'i dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith: 'Pay Sadaqah on behalf of those whom you maintain' (ادوا عمن تمونون). Since the husband maintains the wife, he must pay her Sadaqah.
This is a direct command from the Prophet ﷺ.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the hadith refers to absolute maintenance (moonah mutlaqah), which implies complete maintenance. However, the husband's maintenance is not complete (e.g., he is not obliged to pay for medical treatment). Therefore, the condition for obligation is not met.
The Hanafi response uses a linguistic argument: 'absolute' implies 'complete'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, the wife must pay her own Fitrana if she possesses the nisab. In the Shafi'i school, the husband is obliged regardless of the wife's wealth.
This affects fiqh practice in financial planning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُؤَدِّى عَنْ زَوْجَتِهِ لِقُصُورِ الْوِلَايَةِ وَالْمُؤْنَةِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَلِيْهَا فِى غَيْرِ حُقُوقِ النِّكَاحِ وَلَا يَمُونُهَا فِي غَيْرِ الرَّوَانِبِ كَالْمُدَاوَاةِ ترجمہ اور مالک نصابے اپنی بیوی کی طرف سے ادا نہ کرے کیونکہ ولایت اور مؤنت دونوں ناقص ہیں اس لئے شوہر حقوق نکاح کے علاوہ میں اس پر ولایت نہیں رکھتا اور شوہر ثابت شدہ امور کے علاوہ میں اس کے مونت برداشت نہیں کرتا جیسے دوا کرنا۔ تشریح مسئلہ مالدار شوہر پر اس کی بیوی کا صدقہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ بیوی پر شو ہر کی ولایت بھی ناقص ہے اور مونت بھی ناقص ہے ولایت تو اس لئے ناقص ہے کہ شوہر کو بیوی پر امور نکاح کے علاوہ میں کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے بلکہ فقط امور نکاح میں ولایت حاصل ہے تو شوہر کو بیوی پر کامل ولایت حاصل نہ ہوئی اور مؤنت اس لئے ناقص ہے کہ شوہر بیوی کے انہیں مصارف کو برداشت کرتا ہے جو شرعا ثابت ہیں مثلا نان نفقہ سکنی اور اس کے علاوہ میں مونت برداشت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے مثلاً بیوی اگر بیمار ہو جائے تو اس کا علاج معالجہ شوہر پر واجب نہیں۔ پس جب ولایت اور مونت دونوں ناقص ہیں تو شوہر پر بیوی کا صدقہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب ولایت کا ملہ اور مونت کا ملہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک بیوی کا صدقہ شوہر پر واجب ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ اد وا عَمَّنْ تَمُونُوں یعنی تم جن کی مونت برداشت کرتے ہو ان کی طرف سے صدقہ ادا کرو اور شوہر بیوی کی مونت برداشت کرتا ہے لہذا بیوی کا صدقہ شوہر پر واجب ہوگا لیکن ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں مؤنت مطلقہ کا ذکر ہے۔ مطلق جب بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے کامل مراد ہوتا ہے اور مونت کاملہ شوہر پر ہوتی نہیں اس لئے اس پر بیوی کا صدقہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
And he (the husband) shall not pay on behalf of his wife due to the deficiency of guardianship (wilayah) and maintenance (moonah). Indeed, he does not have authority over her in matters other than marital rights, and he does not bear her maintenance in non-fixed matters like medical treatment. Translation: And a wealthy husband should not pay on behalf of his wife because both guardianship and maintenance are deficient. Therefore, the husband has no guardianship over her outside marital rights, and he does not bear her maintenance outside established matters like bread, food, and housing. Explanation: The husband is not obligated to pay Sadaqah for his wife because his guardianship over her is deficient (he only has authority in marital matters) and his maintenance obligation is deficient (only covering food, clothing, housing, not medical treatment). Since both are deficient, the husband is not obligated for her Sadaqat al-Fitr, because the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr arises from complete guardianship and complete maintenance. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the husband is obligated for his wife's Sadaqah because the Prophet ﷺ said, 'Pay Sadaqah on behalf of those whom you maintain.' Since the husband maintains the wife, he must pay her Sadaqah. But our response is that the hadith mentions absolute maintenance (moonah mutlaqah). When absolute is used, it implies complete maintenance, and complete maintenance is not incumbent upon the husband; therefore, he is not obligated for her Sadaqah.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that a husband is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his wife. The reasoning is that both guardianship and maintenance are incomplete. Guardianship: the husband has authority only in marital matters, not other affairs. Maintenance: the husband is only obligated to provide basic necessities (food, clothing, housing), not incidental expenses like medical treatment. Since Sadaqat al-Fitr requires complete guardianship and complete maintenance, the husband's deficient status makes him non-liable. The passage then addresses the Shafi'i objection citing a hadith. The Hanafi response argues that the hadith's word 'tamunoon' implies complete maintenance (moonah kamilah), which the husband does not have over the wife, so the analogy fails. This is an inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi school's position is defended.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship or authority; in this context, the husband's legal authority over the wife.
مؤنت (moonah): Maintenance obligation; in this context, the financial support the husband provides to the wife.
مونت مطلق (moonah mutlaqah): Absolute or complete maintenance that includes all expenses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the husband's guardianship and maintenance are incomplete
C) Because Sadaqat al-Fitr is only for oneself
D) Because the wife is not required to pay Sadaqah

Key Takeaway
A husband's obligation to pay his wife's Sadaqat al-Fitr is not wajib because complete guardianship and complete maintenance—conditions for such obligation—are lacking.

Father Not Obliged for Adult Children's Sadaqat al-Fitr
Ruling that father is not obligated for adult children's fitrana, with istihsan ruling if he pays without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father's obligation to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children and explain the role of istihsan in validating a payment made without explicit permission.

Core Idea
A father is not obliged to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children, but if he pays without permission it is valid by istihsan due to customary permission.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario in Sadaqat al-Fitr: who bears the obligation for adult children? The text clarifies that a father's guardianship (wilayah) ceases when children reach adulthood, so he is not required to pay on their behalf. However, if he voluntarily does so without their explicit command, the payment is still considered valid through istihsan (juristic preference) because customarily, such payments are understood to be permitted. This lesson will unpack the reasoning behind the rule and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine the act and who is obligated. The passage rules that a father is not required to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children.
2
Analyze the underlying cause (illat)
The text states the cause is 'absence of guardianship' (intima' al-wilayah). Explain why adulthood severs guardianship.
Guardianship over children ends at adulthood (bulugh) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Examine the exception
If the father pays without explicit permission, it is still valid by istihsan. Contrast this with the default rule.
Istihsan overrides the general rule due to custom.
4
Understand the custom-based permission
The text says permission is established by custom (al-idhn al-'aadi). Explain how customary permission functions in Hanafi fiqh.
Custom is considered like a textual mandate in certain matters.
5
Apply to a similar scenario
Consider the husband paying for his wife – the same principle applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا عَنْ أَوْلَادِهِ الْكِبَارِ وَإِن كَانُوا فِى عَالِهِ لِإِنْعِدَامِ الْوِلَايَةِ وَلَوْاَدُّى عَنْهُمْ أوْ عَنْ زَوْجَتِه بِغَيْرِ أمْرِ هِم أَجَزَاهُم استِحْسَانًا لِتَبُوتِ الْإِذْنَ عَادَةً ترجمہ اور نہ ادا کرے اپنی بالغ اولاد کی طرف سے اگر چہ وہ اس کے عیال میں ہوں کیونکہ ولایت معدوم ہے اور اگر ان کی طرف سے یا اپنی بیوی کی طرف سے بغیر ان کے حکم کے ادا کیا تو استحسانا ان کی طرف سے ادا ہو گیا کیونکہ اجازت عادہ ثابت ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ باپ پر بالغ اولاد کا صدقہ واجب نہیں ہوتا اگر چہ اولاد کبار اس کے عیال میں داخل ہوں کیونکہ باپ کو بالغ اولاد پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے لیکن اگر باپ نے بالغ اولاد کی طرف سے ادا کر دیا یا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کی طرف سے ادا کر دیا اور یہ ادا ئیگی بغیر ان کے حکم کے پائی گئی تو بھی استحسانا صدقہ ادا ہو گیا کیونکہ اجازت عادہ ثابت ہے اور جو چیز عادہ ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ ایسی ہے جو نص اور صراحت کے ساتھ ثابت ہو۔
And (the father shall) not (pay) on behalf of his adult children, even if they are under his care, due to the absence of guardianship. And if he pays on their behalf or on behalf of his wife without their command, it suffices them by istihsan, because permission is established by custom. Translation: And he should not pay on behalf of his adult children, even if they are under his care, because guardianship is absent. And if he pays on their behalf or on behalf of his wife without their permission, it suffices them by istihsan because permission is established by custom. Explanation: The father is not obligated to pay Sadaqah for his adult children, even if they live in his household, because the father has no guardianship over adult children. But if the father pays on behalf of his adult children, or the husband pays on behalf of his wife, without their command, it is still valid by istihsan because permission is established by custom, and what is established by custom is like what is established by text and explicit statement.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage first establishes that a father is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children because he has no guardianship over them (adults are independent). However, if he voluntarily pays for them without their explicit permission, it is still considered valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because custom dictates that such payments are typically permitted. The same ruling applies to a husband paying for his wife. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that customary permission (al-idhn al-'aadi) has legal force similar to explicit permission. The passage does not address whether the father can recover the expense; it simply states the payment avails and is acceptable.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; in this case, validating the payment based on customary permission.
اذن عادة (idhn 'aadah): Permission established by custom; i.e., it is customary to assume permission in such transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The father's guardianship over the child
B) The child's obligation to pay
C) Customary permission (istihsan)
D) The father's wealth

Key Takeaway
A father's payment of Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children is not obligatory but is valid and discharges their obligation if done, thanks to the Hanafi reliance on custom as a source of permission.

Sadaqat al-Fitr for Mukatab, Mudabbar, Umm Walad, and Trade Slaves
Rulings on fitrana for mukatab, mudabbar, umm walad, and trade slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Sadaqat al-Fitr for each category of slave and explain the reasoning behind the difference, including the Shafi'i dispute.

Core Idea
The master's obligation for fitrana depends on complete guardianship and avoiding duplication with zakat on trade slaves.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced aspect of Sadaqat al-Fitr: who is obligated to pay for different categories of slaves? The master's liability hinges on his degree of guardianship (wilayah) and the principle of avoiding duplication of annual obligations. A key disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i highlights the methodological difference in how Hanafi usul handles conflicting obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four categories mentioned: mukatab, mudabbar, umm walad, and trade slaves (mamalik li al-tijarah). For each, note the ruling on who pays Sadaqat al-Fitr.
The passage also mentions the mukatab himself is not obligated due to poverty.
2
Understand the basis of obligation
In Hanafi fiqh, Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib on the master for slaves he owns and maintains, provided he has complete guardianship (wilayah kamilah). Incomplete wilayah (as with mukatab) removes the obligation.
Guardianship is tied to ownership and control over the slave's affairs.
3
Analyze the trade slaves ruling
For trade slaves, the master has full ownership, but paying fitrana would create duplication with zakat on trade goods. The Hanafi school argues that both fitrana and zakat are obligations on the master, so applying both to the same property in one year is impermissible duplication.
This is the point of ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i.
4
Examine the Shafi'i counterargument
Imam al-Shafi'i places the obligation of fitrana on the slave himself (even though the master pays on his behalf), while zakat is on the master. Thus no duplication as the subject differs.
The Hanafi response rejects this as they consider both obligations on the master.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a master with a mukatab, a mudabbar, and a trade slave, determine the fitrana obligations. The master pays for mudabbar and umm walad only.
This step consolidates the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَخْرُجُ عَنْ مُكَاتِبِهِ لَعَدَمِ الوِلَايَةِ وَلَا الْمُكَاتَبُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لَفَقْرِهِ وَ فِى الْمُدَبَّرِ وَأُمِّ الْوَلَدِ وِلَايَةُ المَولى ثَابِتَةَ فَيُخْرِجُ عَنْهَا وَلَا يُخْرِجُ عَنْ مَمَالِيكِهِ لِلتِّجَارَةِ خِلَاقًا لِلشَّافِعِى فَإِنَّ عِنْدَهُ وُجُوبُهَا عَلَى الْعَبْدِ وَوُجُوبُ الزَّكوة عَلَى الْمَوْلى فَلَا تُنَافِيْهِ وَعِندَنَا وُجُوبُهَا عَلَى الْمَولى بسَبيهِ كَالزَّكوة فَيُؤدى إلى البنى ترجمہ اور نہ نکالے اپنے مکاتب کی طرف سے کیونکہ ولایت نہیں ہے اور نہ مکاتب خود اپنی طرف سے نکالے کیونکہ مکاتب فقیر ہے اور مدبر اور ام ولد میں مولیٰ کی ولایت پوری ثابت ہے اس سے مولیٰ ان دونوں کی طرف سے نکالے گا۔ اور مولیٰ اپنے تجارتی مملوکوں کی طرف سے نہ نکالے گا۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب غلام پر ہوتا ہے اور زکوۃ کا وجوب مولیٰ پر ہوتا ہے پس کوئی منافات نہیں ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب اپنے سبب کی وجہ سے مولیٰ پر ہوتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ پس یہ تکرار کا سبب بنے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ مولیٰ پر مکاتب کا صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ مکاتب کے یدا اور تصرفات کے اعتبار سے آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے مولی کو اس پر کامل ولایت نہیں ہے حالانکہ وجوب صدقہ کا سبب ہی کامل ولا یت ہے اور مکاتب پر خود بھی اپنی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ مکاتب چونکہ بدل کتابت ادا کرنے کا محتاج ہے اس لئے جو کچھ مال اس کے پاس ہے وہ سب مولی کا مملوک ہے اور جب وہ مولیٰ کا مملوک ہے تو مکاتب فقیر کا فقیر رہا۔ اور فقیر پر صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے مکاتب پر خود اپنی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا اور رہامد بر اور ام ولد تو چونکہ ان پر مولی کو رقبہ اور یدا دونوں طرح کامل ولایت حاصل ہے اور ان کی مونت بھی مولی برداشت کرتا ہے اس لئے ان کی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر بھی مولیٰ ہی پر واجب ہوگا۔ اور غلام اور باندیاں جو تجارت کے لئے ہوں ان کا صدقہ بھی مولی پر واجب نہ ہوگا اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ تجارت کے غلام اور باندیوں کی طرف سے صدقہ نکالے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہوتا ہے غلام پر اگر چہ اس کی طرف سے ادا مولی کرے گا۔ اور ان کی زکوۃ مولی پر واجب ہوتی ہے پس صدقہ اور زکوۃ دو حق میں دو مختلف محل میں ثابت ہیں یعنی صدقہ غلام پر ثابت ہے اور زکوۃ مولیٰ پر ثابت ہے لہذا ان دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں ہے اور جب ماہت نہیں تو دونوں کا جمع ہونا جائز ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ غلام کے صدقہ کا وجوب مولیٰ پر ہوتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ کا وجوب مولی پر ہوتا ہے پس اگر تجارت کے غلاموں کا صدقہ مولیٰ پر واجب کیا گیا تو ان غلاموں کے اندر ایک سال میں دو مرتبہ فریضسالی واجب کرنا لازم آئے گا ایک بصورت صدقۃ الفطر دوم بصورت زکوۃ حالانکہ ایک۔
And he (the master) shall not pay on behalf of his mukatab because of absence of guardianship, and the mukatab shall not pay on behalf of himself because of his poverty. For the mudabbar and umm walad, the guardianship of the master is established, so he will pay on their behalf. And he shall not pay on behalf of his trade slaves, contrary to al-Shafi'i. For in his view, its obligation is upon the slave, and the obligation of zakat is upon the master, so there is no contradiction. And in our view, its obligation is upon the master due to its cause like zakat, so it would lead to duplication. Translation: And he should not pay on behalf of his mukatab because there is no guardianship, and the mukatab should not pay on behalf of himself because he is poor. For the mudabbar and umm walad, the master's guardianship is complete, so he will pay on their behalf. And the master will not pay on behalf of his trade slaves, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Because according to al-Shafi'i, the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is upon the slave, and the obligation of zakat is upon the master, so there is no contradiction. But according to us, the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is upon the master due to its cause like zakat, so it would lead to duplication. Explanation: The master is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his mukatab because the master's guardianship over the mukatab is incomplete (the mukatab is partially free). The mukatab himself is also not obligated to pay because he is considered poor (his wealth is owned by the master for the kitabah). For the mudabbar and umm walad, the master has full guardianship and provides for them, so he must pay. For trade slaves, the master is not obligated because if he were, then the slave would have two obligations in one year: Sadaqat al-Fitr and zakat (on trade goods), leading to repetition. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is on the slave himself (even if the master pays), while zakat is on the master, so no conflict. But the Hanafi response is that both obligations fall on the master, causing duplication.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage covers the Sadaqat al-Fitr obligations for various categories of slaves. For a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission), the master does not have complete guardianship (because the mukatab is in the process of freedom), so the master is not obligated. The mukatab himself is also not obligated because he is considered poor (his earnings go to the kitabah payment). For a mudabbar (slave whose freedom is deferred to after the master's death) and an umm walad (slave mother of the master's child), the master has full ownership and guardianship, and he provides their maintenance, so he is obligated to pay their fitrana. For trade slaves (slaves used for business), the master is not obligated, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi reasoning is that if the master were obligated, it would result in two annual obligations on the same property: Sadaqat al-Fitr and zakat (since the trade goods are subject to zakat). This would be duplication. Al-Shafi'i avoids this by placing the Sadaqat al-Fitr obligation on the slave himself (even though the master pays), so the two obligations target different subjects. The Hanafi school rejects this and maintains that both obligations are on the master, leading to conflict.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract of manumission (kitabah) to purchase his freedom by installments.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is promised upon the master's death.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child to her master; the child is free, and she becomes free upon master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a master not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his trade slaves?
A) Because trade slaves are not owned by the master
B) Because it would cause duplication with zakat on trade goods
C) Because trade slaves are deemed rich
D) Because the master has no guardianship over them

Key Takeaway
The master's obligation for Sadaqat al-Fitr depends on complete guardianship; for trade slaves, it is waived to prevent duplication with zakat.

Paying Sadaqat al-Fitr for Adult Children and Wife: Customary Permission
Explains ruling on paying fitr for adult children and wife based on customary permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying Sadaqat al-Fitr for adult children and wife without permission and explain the role of custom (adah) as a legal basis.

Core Idea
Customary permission suffices; a well-established custom has the force of an explicit text.

In the Hanafi school, payment of Sadaqat al-Fitr on behalf of another normally requires the beneficiary's permission. But what happens when a father pays for his adult son or a husband pays for his wife without their explicit command? This lesson explores the Hanafi position that such payment is valid by istihsan because custom (adah) establishes implicit permission. The passage from the Hidayah commentary explains this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
First, note that a father is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children, even if they live with him, because he loses guardianship over them at adulthood. Similarly, a husband is not obligated for his wife, though he often pays.
2
Recognize the istihsan exception
If the father or husband actually pays without express permission, the payment is valid by istihsan due to established custom. Understand 'istihsan' as juristic preference that overrides strict qiyas.
3
Understand the custom-as-text principle
The author states that something established by custom (adah) is treated like a text (nass) in legal effect. This is a key Hanafi usul principle that custom can serve as a basis for rulings.
This principle is reflected in the Hanafi legal maxim: 'al-adatu muhakkamah' (custom is authoritative).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكوة یا اپنی بیوی کی طرف سے بغیر ان کے حکم کے ادا کیا تو استحسانا ان کی طرف سے ادا ہو گیا کیونکہ اجازت عادہ ثابت ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ باپ پر بالغ اولاد کا صدقہ واجب نہیں ہوتا اگر چہ اولاد کبار اس کے عیال میں داخل ہوں کیونکہ باپ کو بالغ اولاد پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے لیکن اگر باپ نے بالغ اولاد کی طرف سے ادا کر دیا یا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کی طرف سے ادا کر دیا اور یہ ادا ئیگی بغیر ان کے حکم کے پائی گئی تو بھی استحسانا صدقہ ادا ہو گیا کیونکہ اجازت عادہ ثابت ہے اور جو چیز عادہ ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ ایسی ہے جو نص اور صراحت کے ساتھ ثابت ہو۔
Kitab al-Zakat: Or if he paid on behalf of his wife without her command, then by istihsan it is paid on her behalf because permission is established by custom. Explanation: The issue: A father is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children, even if the adult children are within his household, because the father has no guardianship over adult children. But if the father paid on behalf of his adult children, or a husband paid on behalf of his wife, and this payment occurred without their command, then by istihsan the sadaqah is valid because permission is established by custom, and something established by custom is like that which is established by text and explicit statement.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter of Zakat. It addresses the permissibility of paying Sadaqat al-Fitr on behalf of adult children and a wife without their explicit permission. The default ruling is that a father is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult children because he has no guardianship over them once they reach adulthood. Similarly, a husband is not obligated to pay for his wife, though he ordinarily does due to the marital relationship. However, if a father or husband actually pays the sadaqah on their behalf without their express command, the payment is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because the custom (‘adah) is that such payment is implicitly permitted. The author notes that custom, when well-established, takes the same legal force as an explicit text (nass). This is a Hanafi principle that custom can serve as a basis for legal rulings in the absence of explicit evidence.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference based on custom and necessity, overriding strict qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a father pays Sadaqat al-Fitr for his adult son without the son's permission, what is the ruling?
A) The payment is invalid and the son must pay again.
B) The payment is valid because customary permission is established.
C) The father is obligated to pay because the son is in his household.
D) The payment is valid only if the son explicitly authorized it beforehand.

Key Takeaway
Customary permission can validate payment of Sadaqat al-Fitr on behalf of adult children and wife, as per Hanafi istihsan.
