Fitr for Mukatab, Mudabbar, and Umm Walad
States rulings for fitr on three slave categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Sadaqat al-Fitr for a mukatab, mudabbar, and umm walad, and explain the role of guardianship and poverty in determining the obligation.

Core Idea
Master pays fitr for mudabbar and umm walad, but not for mukatab—guardianship is key.

This lesson examines the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr for three categories of slaves: the mukatab (contract slave), mudabbar (death-deferred freedom), and umm walad (mother of master's child). The rulings are based on the master's level of guardianship (wilayah) and the slave's financial capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three slave categories
Recognize mukatab, mudabbar, and umm walad. Each has a distinct legal status in terms of ownership and guardianship.
The mukatab is partially free; the mudabbar and umm walad remain fully owned during the master's lifetime.
2
Understand the role of wilayah
The obligation to pay fitr on behalf of another requires full guardianship (wilayah) over that person. Determine whether the master has complete wilayah over each category.
Full wilayah means the master has both property rights (raqabah) and physical control (yad), and bears maintenance.
3
Derive the ruling for each category
Apply the condition: if full wilayah exists, the master must pay; if not, no obligation. For the mukatab, also consider the slave's own obligation—he is poor, so fitr is not due from him either.
The mukatab's earnings go toward his kitabah, so he is considered poor (faqir) for fitr purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکاتب، مدبر، ام ولد کا صدقہ فطر آقا پر نہیں
وَلَا يَخْرُجُ عَنْ مُكَاتِبِهِ لَعَدَمِ الوِلَايَةِ وَلَا الْمُكَاتَبُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لَفَقْرِهِ وَ فِى الْمُدَبَّرِ وَأُمِّ الْوَلَدِ وِلَايَةُ المَولى ثَابِتَةَ فَيُخْرِجُ عَنْهَا وَلَا يُخْرِجُ عَنْ مَمَالِيكِهِ لِلتِّجَارَةِ خِلَاقًا لِلشَّافِعِى فَإِنَّ عِنْدَهُ وُجُوبُهَا عَلَى الْعَبْدِ وَوُجُوبُ الزَّكوة عَلَى الْمَوْلى فَلَا تُنَافِيْهِ وَعِندَنَا وُجُوبُهَا عَلَى الْمَولى بسَبيهِ كَالزَّكوة فَيُؤدى إلى البنى
ترجمہ اور نہ نکالے اپنے مکاتب کی طرف سے کیونکہ ولایت نہیں ہے اور نہ مکاتب خود اپنی طرف سے نکالے کیونکہ مکاتب فقیر ہے اور مدبر اور ام ولد میں مولیٰ کی ولایت پوری ثابت ہے اس سے مولیٰ ان دونوں کی طرف سے نکالے گا۔ اور مولیٰ اپنے تجارتی مملوکوں کی طرف سے نہ نکالے گا۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب غلام پر ہوتا ہے اور زکوۃ کا وجوب مولیٰ پر ہوتا ہے پس کوئی منافات نہیں ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب اپنے سبب کی وجہ سے مولیٰ پر ہوتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ پس یہ تکرار کا سبب بنے گا۔

تشریح مسئلہ مولیٰ پر مکاتب کا صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ مکاتب کے یدا اور تصرفات کے اعتبار سے آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے مولی کو اس پر کامل ولایت نہیں ہے حالانکہ وجوب صدقہ کا سبب ہی کامل ولا یت ہے اور مکاتب پر خود بھی اپنی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ مکاتب چونکہ بدل کتابت ادا کرنے کا محتاج ہے اس لئے جو کچھ مال اس کے پاس ہے وہ سب مولی کا مملوک ہے اور جب وہ مولیٰ کا مملوک ہے تو مکاتب فقیر کا فقیر رہا۔ اور فقیر پر صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے مکاتب پر خود اپنی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا اور رہامد بر اور ام ولد تو چونکہ ان پر مولی کو رقبہ اور یدا دونوں طرح کامل ولایت حاصل ہے اور ان کی مونت بھی مولی برداشت کرتا ہے اس لئے ان کی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر بھی مولیٰ ہی پر واجب ہوگا۔ اور غلام اور باندیاں جو تجارت کے لئے ہوں ان کا صدقہ بھی مولی پر واجب نہ ہوگا اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ تجارت کے غلام اور باندیوں کی طرف سے صدقہ نکالے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہوتا ہے غلام پر اگر چہ اس کی طرف سے ادا مولی کرے گا۔ اور ان کی زکوۃ مولی پر واجب ہوتی ہے پس صدقہ اور زکوۃ دو حق میں دو مختلف محل میں ثابت ہیں یعنی صدقہ غلام پر ثابت ہے اور زکوۃ مولیٰ پر ثابت ہے لہذا ان دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں ہے اور جب ماہت نہیں تو دونوں کا جمع ہونا جائز ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ غلام کے صدقہ کا وجوب مولیٰ پر ہوتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ کا وجوب مولی پر ہوتا ہے پس اگر تجارت کے غلاموں کا صدقہ مولیٰ پر واجب کیا گیا تو ان غلاموں کے اندر ایک سال میں دو مرتبہ فریضسالی واجب کرنا لازم آئے گا ایک بصورت صدقۃ الفطر دوم بصورت زکوۃ حالانکہ ایک
۔
سال میں دو مرتبہ مالی فریضہ واجب کرنا جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ حدیث رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ثنى فِي الصَّدفة منی ٹا، کے کسرہ اور الف مقصورہ کے ساتھ ہے یعنی سال میں دو مرتبہ صدقہ نہ لیا جائے۔
Translation of Arabic: And he does not pay on behalf of his mukatab due to lack of guardianship, nor does the mukatab pay on his own behalf due to his poverty. And concerning the mudabbar and the umm walad, the master’s guardianship is fully established, so he pays on their behalf. And he does not pay on behalf of his trade slaves, contrary to al-Shafi’i, because in his view the obligation of fitr is upon the slave, and the obligation of zakat is upon the master, so there is no conflict. And in our view, the obligation of fitr is upon the master due to its cause, like zakat, so it would lead to repetition. Urdu translation: And he does not pay on behalf of his mukatab because there is no guardianship, nor does the mukatab pay on his own behalf because he is poor. And for the mudabbar and umm walad, the master’s guardianship is fully established, so the master will pay on their behalf. And the master will not pay on behalf of his trade slaves. There is a difference with Imam Shafi’i because according to him, the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is upon the slave, and the obligation of zakat is upon the master, so there is no conflict. And in our view, the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is upon the master due to its own cause, like zakat, so this would cause repetition. Explanation of the issue: The master is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his mukatab because the master does not have full guardianship over him due to the mukatab’s freedom in terms of his hand and transactions, while the cause of obligation of sadaqah is full guardianship. And the mukatab himself is not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr on his own behalf because he needs to pay his kitabah, and whatever wealth he has is all owned by the master, so he remains poor, and the poor are not obligated to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr. As for the mudabbar and umm walad, since the master has full guardianship over them in terms of property and hand, and he bears their maintenance, therefore the Sadaqat al-Fitr on their behalf is obligatory upon the master. And for slaves and slave-girls that are for trade, their sadaqah is not obligatory upon the master. Imam Shafi’i said that one should pay sadaqah on behalf of trade slaves because according to him, Sadaqat al-Fitr is obligatory upon the slave, even though the master will pay on his behalf. And their zakat is obligatory upon the master. So sadaqah and zakat are two rights established in two different places: sadaqah is established upon the slave, and zakat upon the master, so there is no conflict between them. And when there is no conflict, it is permissible for both to be combined. And in our view, since the obligation of the slave’s sadaqah is upon the master like the obligation of zakat, if the sadaqah of trade slaves is made obligatory upon the master, then it would necessitate making a financial obligation twice in one year upon these slaves: once in the form of Sadaqat al-Fitr and second in the form of zakat, whereas it is not permissible to impose a financial obligation twice in one year, as in the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'La tunna al-sadaqah' i.e., sadaqah is not taken twice in a year.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning Sadaqat al-Fitr for various categories of slaves. The Hanafi position: the master is not required to pay fitr for a mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) because the master lacks full guardianship (wilayah), and the mukatab is not required to pay because he is deemed poor (faqir) since his earnings must go toward his kitabah. For a mudabbar (slave freed upon master's death) and umm walad (slave mother of master's child), the master does pay due to full guardianship and maintenance burden. For trade slaves (mamalik al-tijarah), the master does not pay fitr according to the Hanafis, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. The Shafi'i view: fitr is obligatory upon the slave himself, with the master as paying agent, while zakat is upon the master, so no conflict arises. The Hanafi response: if fitr were also on the master for trade slaves, it would lead to two financial obligations (fitr and zakat) on the same slave's head in one year, which is prohibited by the hadith 'La tunna al-sadaqah' (sadaqah is not taken twice). Therefore, to avoid this repetition, the Hanafis rule that fitr is not obligatory upon the master for trade slaves. The hadith is cited as proof.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master to earn his freedom by paying a sum.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose manumission is deferred until after the master's death.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to her master's child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does the master not pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his mukatab?
A) Because the mukatab is a free man
B) Because the master lacks full guardianship over him
C) Because the mukatab is wealthy enough to pay himself
D) Because fitr is not obligatory on any slave

Key Takeaway
The master's obligation to pay fitr for a slave depends on having full guardianship; he pays for mudabbar and umm walad, but not for the mukatab.

Zakat — Almsgiving

The Dispute Over Fitr for Trade Slaves
States the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on fitr for trade slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on Sadaqat al-Fitr for trade slaves, state the Hanafi proof, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hanafis: no fitr on master for trade slaves to avoid double obligation; Shafi'is: fitr on slave, zakat on master, no conflict.

This lesson presents a classical inter-madhhab dispute regarding Sadaqat al-Fitr for slaves acquired for trade. The Hanafi school argues that obligating the master to pay fitr would result in two financial duties (fitr and zakat) on the same slave in one year, which is prohibited. The Shafi'i school counters that fitr and zakat attach to different persons, so they can coexist.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its basis
The master does not pay fitr for trade slaves. The reason: the obligation of fitr is upon the master (like zakat), so requiring both fitr and zakat would mean two financial obligations on the same slave in one year, which is disallowed by hadith.
Trade slaves are commercial assets; their zakat is paid by the master as part of trade zakat.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the master must pay fitr for trade slaves. His reasoning: fitr is obligatory upon the slave himself (even if the master pays on his behalf), while zakat is upon the master. They are two separate obligations on two different subjects, so no conflict arises.
In the Shafi'i school, the slave is the primary obligor for fitr, and the master acts as his payer.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument
The Hanafi response is that fitr is not on the slave but on the master due to the cause of obligation (sabab). Since both fitr and zakat would be on the master for the same slave, repetition occurs. The hadith 'La tunna al-sadaqah' prohibits taking sadaqah twice in one year.
The Hanafis view the sabab of fitr as the master's ownership and maintenance, similar to zakat.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi school, the master does not pay fitr for trade slaves; under the Shafi'i school, he does. This affects the master's total fitr payment.
The dispute is purely legal; both schools consider their position valid.

Source Text

تشریح مسئلہ مولیٰ پر مکاتب کا صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ مکاتب کے یدا اور تصرفات کے اعتبار سے آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے مولی کو اس پر کامل ولایت نہیں ہے حالانکہ وجوب صدقہ کا سبب ہی کامل ولا یت ہے اور مکاتب پر خود بھی اپنی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ مکاتب چونکہ بدل کتابت ادا کرنے کا محتاج ہے اس لئے جو کچھ مال اس کے پاس ہے وہ سب مولی کا مملوک ہے اور جب وہ مولیٰ کا مملوک ہے تو مکاتب فقیر کا فقیر رہا۔ اور فقیر پر صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے مکاتب پر خود اپنی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا اور رہامد بر اور ام ولد تو چونکہ ان پر مولی کو رقبہ اور یدا دونوں طرح کامل ولایت حاصل ہے اور ان کی مونت بھی مولی برداشت کرتا ہے اس لئے ان کی طرف سے صدقۃ الفطر بھی مولیٰ ہی پر واجب ہوگا۔ اور غلام اور باندیاں جو تجارت کے لئے ہوں ان کا صدقہ بھی مولی پر واجب نہ ہوگا اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ تجارت کے غلام اور باندیوں کی طرف سے صدقہ نکالے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہوتا ہے غلام پر اگر چہ اس کی طرف سے ادا مولی کرے گا۔ اور ان کی زکوۃ مولی پر واجب ہوتی ہے پس صدقہ اور زکوۃ دو حق میں دو مختلف محل میں ثابت ہیں یعنی صدقہ غلام پر ثابت ہے اور زکوۃ مولیٰ پر ثابت ہے لہذا ان دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں ہے اور جب ماہت نہیں تو دونوں کا جمع ہونا جائز ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ غلام کے صدقہ کا وجوب مولیٰ پر ہوتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ کا وجوب مولی پر ہوتا ہے پس اگر تجارت کے غلاموں کا صدقہ مولیٰ پر واجب کیا گیا تو ان غلاموں کے اندر ایک سال میں دو مرتبہ فریضسالی واجب کرنا لازم آئے گا ایک بصورت صدقۃ الفطر دوم بصورت زکوۃ حالانکہ ایک

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning Sadaqat al-Fitr for various categories of slaves. ثنى فِي الصَّدفة (thunna fi al-sadaqah): Part of a hadith meaning 'sadaqah is not taken twice'.

Prohibition of Taking Sadaqah Twice in One Year
States prohibition based on hadith 'لا ثنى في الصدقة'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking sadaqah twice in one year and identify the hadith that proves this prohibition.

Core Idea
Once zakat is paid on wealth, it cannot be taken again in the same year.

This lesson examines a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: it is impermissible to impose a financial obligation (like zakat) twice on the same wealth in a single year. The proof is a prophetic hadith that serves as primary textual evidence. Understanding this principle helps avoid double taxation in zakat calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is taking sadaqah (or zakat) twice on the same wealth in one year. The ruling is that it is prohibited (haram).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH): 'لا ثنى في الصدقة' (there is no double payment in sadaqah).
The Arabic in the source is slightly corrupted but the meaning is established.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The negation 'لا' in the hadith indicates absolute prohibition. The word 'ثنى' means double or second. Thus, the hadith clearly forbids levying sadaqah twice on the same wealth.
This is a direct dalil naqli (textual evidence).
4
Note the consensus
This ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the schools. There is no intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكوة سال میں دو مرتبہ مالی فریضہ واجب کرنا جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ حدیث رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ثنى فِي الصَّدفة منی ٹا، کے کسرہ اور الف مقصورہ کے ساتھ ہے یعنی سال میں دو مرتبہ صدقہ نہ لیا جائے۔
The book of Zakat. It is not permissible to make a financial obligation wajib twice in a year, as in the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (PBUH): 'ثنى فِي الصَّدفة منی ٹا' with kasra and alif maqsura, meaning: sadaqah should not be taken twice in a year.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling that it is not permissible to impose a financial obligation (like zakat or sadaqah) twice on the same wealth within a single year. The proof is a hadith of the Prophet (PBUH). Although the OCR corrupted the exact wording, the known hadith is 'لا ثنى في الصدقة' (There is no double payment in sadaqah). This is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh: once zakat is paid on wealth, it cannot be taken again in the same lunar year. The hadith serves as a primary textual evidence (dalil naqli) and establishes the prohibition at the level of haram (impermissible).

Key Terms
ثنى (thani): Meaning 'double' or 'second'—referring to taking sadaqah twice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Qiyas on zakat
D) The Quranic verse on zakat

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'لا ثنى في الصدقة' establishes that the same wealth cannot be subject to zakat or sadaqah twice within one lunar year.

Fitrah for Jointly Owned Slaves: The Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Fitrah for multiple jointly-owned slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Fitrah for jointly owned slaves and explain the intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
No Fitrah for a single jointly-owned slave by consensus; for multiple slaves, the ruling depends on the permissibility of dividing slaves.

This lesson explores the ruling of Sadaqat al-Fitr for slaves owned jointly by two partners. While there is consensus on the single slave, a well-known dispute arises when multiple slaves are jointly owned. Understanding this dispute requires grasping the underlying principle of complete ownership and authority (wilayah).

Guided Path
1
State the consensus ruling for a single jointly-owned slave
Identify the ruling that applies by agreement of all three Imams: no Fitrah is due on either partner because both have deficient wilayah and mu'nah.
This is a clear foundational point.
2
Identify the point of disagreement for multiple jointly-owned slaves
Recognise that when there are multiple slaves, Abu Hanifa maintains no Fitrah, while the Sahibayn say Fitrah is due for the complete heads resulting from combining shares.
The ikhtilaf only concerns multiple slaves, not a single slave.
3
Explain Abu Hanifa's reasoning based on the impermissibility of dividing slaves
Abu Hanifa does not permit division (qasmah) of slaves among co-owners, so each partner remains a fractional owner in every slave. Thus no one has complete ownership, and Fitrah is not wajib.
The key principle: complete ownership (raqabah) is necessary for Fitrah.
4
Explain the Sahibayn's reasoning based on the permissibility of division
The Sahibayn allow division, so each partner can own complete slaves by combining his fractional shares. For the complete heads, Fitrah is wajib; for leftover fractions, it is not.
Understand the example of five slaves: each partner gets 2.5 complete heads, so Fitrah for 2 each.
5
Analyze the third view claiming consensus on no Fitrah for multiple slaves
Some scholars report that all three Imams agree that no Fitrah is due for multiple slaves because shares cannot be combined before division. This view is presented as a consensus (ijma) and may be the mufta bihi.
This view reconciles the positions by stating that the disagreement is only apparent; the practical ruling is the same.

Source Text

مشترک غلام کا صدقہ فطر دونوں آقاؤں پر نہیں
وَالْعَبْدُ بَيْنَ شَرِيكَيْنِ لَا فِطْرَةَ عَلى وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا لِقُصُورِ الوِلَايَةِ وَالْمُؤْنَةِ فِى كُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهَا وَكَذَا الْعَبْد بَينَ اثْنَيْنِ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا عَلى كُلّ مِنْهَا مَا يَخُصُّهُ مِنَ الرُّؤُوسِ دُونَ الْأَشْقَاصِ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُرَى قَسَمَةَ الرَّقِيقِ وَهُمَا يَرَيَانِهَا وَقِيلَ هُوَ يا لإجماع لأنَّهُ لَا يَجْتَمِعُ النَّصِيبُ قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ فَلَم تتم الرقبة لِكُلّ واحد منهما ترجمہ اور جو غلام دو شریکوں کے درمیان ہو، ان دونوں میں سے کسی پر صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ ولایت اور مونت دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے حق میں ناقص ہے اور یونہی چند علام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہوں، یہ حکم ) امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر اس کا صدقہ واجب ہوگا جو راسوں میں سے اس کے واسطے مخصوص ہو، نہ کہ ٹکڑوں میں سے یہ اختلاف اس بات پر مبنی ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ رقیق کی تقسیم اور ہوارہ کو جائز قرار نہیں دیتے اور صاحبین اس کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں اور کہا گیا کہ یہ حکم بالا جماع ہے کیونکہ تقسیم سے پہلے حصص جمع نہیں ہو سکتے ہیں پس ہر شریک کے واسطے ان میں سے کوئی رقبہ پورا نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو تو بالاتفاق دونوں میں سے کسی پر اس غلام کا صدقۃ الفطر واجب نہ ہو گا کیونکہ دونوں کی ولایت بھی ناقص ہے اور مونت بھی ناقص ہے اور یہ بات گذر چکی ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کا سبب ولایت کا ملہ اور مونت کا ملہ ہے۔ پس جب سبب نہیں پایا گیا تو صدقۃ الفطر بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر چند غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہوں تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شریکین میں سے کسی پر کسی غلام کا صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ہر شریک کے حصے ملا کر جتنی راس کامل ہو جائیں ان کا صدقہ ان پر واجب ہوگا اور جو کامل راس نہ ہو بلکہ لڑا ر ہے اس کا واجب نہ ہوگا مثلاً پانچ غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہیں تو ہر شریک کے حصہ میں پانچ نصف آئے اور پانچ نصف کے دو غلام کامل اور نصف ہوئے پس شریلین میں سے ہر ایک پر دو دو غلام کا صدقہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور نصف نصف کا صدقہ دونوں پر واجب نہ ہوگا۔
بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک رقیق اور غلام کی تقسیم اور ہوارہ جائز نہیں ہے اور صاحبین اس کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں لیپس امام صاحب کے نزدیک چونکہ تقسیم جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے شریکین میں سے ہر ایک ہر غلام کے اندر حصہ دار ہوگا اور جب ہر غلام میں ہر ایک کا حصہ ہوا تو دونوں میں سے کوئی کسی عبد کامل اور راُس کامل کا مالک نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب پورے غلام کا کوئی مالک نہیں تو شریکین میں سے کسی کی دلایت اور مونت کامل نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب کسی غلام پر کسی کی ولایت اور مونت کامل نہیں تو کسی پر صدقۃ الفطر بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ غلام کی تقسیم جائز ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک ہر ایک عبد کامل کا مالک ہو سکتا ہے پس ہر ایک غلام کے ٹکڑے ملا کر جتنی راس کامل ہوں گی ان کا صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہو جائے گا اور جونکڑا رہ جائے گا۔ اس کا صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا جیسے مثال گذر چکی ہے اور بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ چند غلاموں کے دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہونے کی صورت میں شریکین میں سے کسی پر صدقہ الفطر کا واجب نہ ہونا ائمہ ثلاثہ (امام صاحب، صاحبین ) کے نزدیک متفق علیہ ہے کیونکہ تقسیم سے پہلے حصص یکجا نہیں ہوسکتے پس ہر شریک کے واسطے کوئی رقبہ پورا نہ ہو گا اور جب کسی کے واسطے کوئی رقبہ پورا نہیں ہوا تو صدقۃ الفطر بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Fitrah for a jointly owned slave is not upon either master. And a slave between two partners: no Fitrah is due on either of them due to the deficiency of authority (wilayah) and maintenance (mu'nah) for each of them. Similarly, [multiple] slaves between two persons: according to Abu Hanifa, the same ruling; and they (the two) said: upon each of them is the Fitrah for the heads that fall to his share, not for the fractions. This is built upon the fact that he does not consider division (qasmah) of slaves permissible, while they consider it permissible. And it was said: this ruling is by consensus, because the shares cannot be combined before division, so no complete slave (raqabah) is established for any of them. Translation: And a slave between two partners: no Fitrah is obligatory on either of them because wilayah and mu'nah are deficient for each. Similarly, if several slaves are jointly owned between two persons, this ruling is according to Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: upon each of them is the Fitrah for the heads that are specific to his share, not for the fractions. This difference is based on the fact that Abu Hanifa does not consider division (qasmah) of slaves permissible, while the Sahibayn consider it permissible. And it was said that this ruling is by consensus because shares cannot be combined before division, so no complete slave exists for any partner. Explanation: The issue is that if one slave is jointly owned by two persons, by consensus no Fitrah is due on either because both wilayah and mu'nah are deficient. And it has passed that the cause for Fitrah being wajib is complete wilayah and complete mu'nah. So when the cause is not found, Fitrah is not wajib. And if several slaves are jointly owned by two persons, according to Abu Hanifa no Fitrah is due on any partner for any slave. And according to the Sahibayn, after combining each partner's shares, the Fitrah is due for the complete heads that result, not for the leftover fraction. For example, five slaves jointly owned by two persons: each partner's share is five halves, and from five halves, two complete slaves and one half result; so each partner pays Fitrah for two slaves, and no Fitrah for the half. The basis of difference is that Abu Hanifa does not permit division of slaves, while the Sahibayn permit it. So according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), since division is not permitted, each partner has a share in every slave, and neither has complete ownership of any slave. Thus, no one has complete wilayah and mu'nah over any slave, so no Fitrah is due. According to the Sahibayn, since division is permitted, each partner can become owner of complete slaves by combining his shares, so Fitrah is due for the complete heads, not for the leftover fraction, as in the example. And some scholars said that in the case of several slaves jointly owned, the fact that no Fitrah is due on any partner is agreed upon by the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) because shares cannot be combined before division, so no complete slave is established for any partner, and thus no Fitrah is due.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of Sadaqat al-Fitr for a slave jointly owned by two partners. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn). The passage first states the ruling for a single jointly-owned slave: by consensus, no Fitrah is due on either partner because both have deficient wilayah (authority) and mu'nah (maintenance). Then it addresses multiple jointly-owned slaves: according to Abu Hanifa, no Fitrah is due; according to the Sahibayn, Fitrah is due for the complete heads (ra's) that arise from combining each partner's shares, but not for fractions. The basis of this difference is that Imam Abu Hanifa does not consider division (qasmah) of slaves permissible, so each partner remains a co-owner in every slave, preventing complete ownership. The Sahibayn consider division permissible, thus allowing each partner to own complete slaves from combined shares. The passage also mentions a third view that for multiple slaves, there is consensus among the three Imams that no Fitrah is due, because shares cannot be combined before actual division. This is the relied-upon position according to some scholars. The detailed explanation with the example of five slaves illustrates the practical application of the Sahibayn's view.

Key Terms
رقبہ (raqabah): Here it means a complete slave as an individual entity, as opposed to a fraction (shiqs).
قسمہ رقیق (qasmah al-raqiq): The division of slaves among co-owners, allocating individual slaves to each partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding Fitrah for multiple jointly-owned slaves?
A) Whether the slaves are Muslim or non-Muslim
B) Whether the partners are Muslims or not
C) Whether division (qasmah) of slaves is permissible
D) Whether the Fitrah is paid in cash or kind

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Fitrah for jointly owned slaves hinges on complete ownership, which depends on the permissibility of dividing slaves.

Fitrah for a Non-Muslim Slave is Upon the Muslim Master
States ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Fitrah for a non-Muslim slave, cite the textual and rational proofs, explain the Shafi'i position, and identify the practical consequence of the disagreement.

Core Idea
A Muslim master must pay Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave because the cause of obligation (ownership and maintenance) is complete and the master is qualified.

This lesson examines the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr for a non-Muslim slave owned by a Muslim. The Hanafi school holds that the master must pay, while the Shafi'i school disagrees. We will explore the proofs from hadith and legal reasoning, and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the Muslim master must pay Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave. Note that this is a wajib obligation.
The ruling applies regardless of the slave's religion; the key is the master's ownership and maintenance.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (and also Malik and Ahmad) hold that Fitrah is not due for a non-Muslim slave. Understand their reasoning: the obligation is on the slave himself, and a non-Muslim is not qualified for worship.
The opposing school places the obligation on the slave, even though the master often pays it.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i argument: Fitrah is an act of worship, so it requires the person being paid for to be a Muslim. Since the slave is non-Muslim, no obligation arises.
They may interpret the hadith 'Pay for every slave' as referring only to Muslim slaves.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Consider the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith explicitly mentions non-Muslims (Jews, Christians, Magians). Moreover, the cause of obligation (complete wilayah and mu'nah) is on the master, so the slave's qualification is irrelevant.
The Hanafis argue that the obligation is on the master, not the slave. The master is qualified, and the cause is present.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, the master pays; in the Shafi'i school, no payment is made. This affects whether the master must include his non-Muslim slave in his Fitrah calculation.
The difference has real financial implications for the Muslim master.

دی کا فر غلام کا صدقہ فطر مسلم آقا پر ہے
وَيُؤدّى المُسْلِمُ الْفِطْرَةَ عَنْ عَبْدِهِ الْكَافِرِ لِإِطْلَاقِ مَارَوَيْنَاهُ وَلِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ فِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عَبَاسٍ أَدُّوا عَنْ كُلّ حُرَ وَعَبْدِ يَهُودِي أَوْ نَصْرَانِي أَوْ مَجُوسِي الْحَدِيثِ. وَلِأَنَّ السَّبَبَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ وَالْمَوْلَى مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَفِيهِ خِلافُ الشَّافِعِي لِأَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عِنْدَهُ عَلَى الْعَبْدِ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَلَوْ كَانَ عَلَى الْعَكْسِ فَلَا وُجُوبَ بِالْإِنْفَاقُ
ترجمہ اور مسلمان اپنے کا فرغلام کی طرف سے فطرہ ادا کرے گا اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے اور حدیث ابن عباس میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان ہے کہ صدقہ ادا کر و ہر آزاد اور غلام یہودی یا نصرانی یا مجوسی کی طرف سے اور اس لئے کہ سبب تحقق ہو گیا اور مولی اس کا اہل ہے اور اس میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک صدقہ کا وجوب غلام پر ہے اور کافر غلام اس کا اہل نہیں ہے اور اگر مسئلہ بر عکس ہو تو بالا تفاق وجوب نہیں ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسلمان مالک نصاب اگر کافر غلام کا مالک ہو تو اس پر کا فر غلام کا صدقۃ الفطر بھی واجب ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک کا فرغلام کی طرف سے مسلمان مولی صدقہ ادا نہ کرے یہی قول امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اول باب میں ثعلبہ بن عمر کی حدیث ادواعَنْ كُلّ حُرو عبد (الحدیث ) مطلق ہے جو عبد مسلم اور عبد کا فر دونوں کو شامل ہے۔ دوسری دلیل این عباس کی حدیث ہے علامہ ابن الہمام نے دار قطنی کے حوالہ سے یہ حدیث اس طرح ذکر کی ہے قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ادو اصدقة الفطر عَنْ كُلَّ صَغِيرِ وَكَبير ذكر وانثى يهودى اَوْ نَصْرَانِي حر او مملوک نِصف صاع من براو صَاعاً مِنْ تَمَرٍ أو شعير، تیسری دلیل ہو ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کا سبب پایا گیا کیونکہ مسلمان مولی کو کافر غلام نیر ولایت کا ملہ بھی حاصل ہے اور اس کی مکمل طور پر مونت بھی برداشت کرتا ہے اور مولی وجوب صدقہ کا اہل بھی ہے اگر چہ غلام کا فر ہونے کی وجہ سے اہل نہیں ہے پس جب سبب وجوب بھی پایا گیا اور مولی کے اندر اہلیت بھی موجود ہے تو مولی پر کا فرغلام کی طرف سے صدقہ واجب ہو جائے گا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر چونکہ غلام پر واجب ہوتا ہے اگر چہ ادا مولی کرتا ہے اور کا فر غلام اس لائق نہیں کہ اس پر صدقہ الفطر جیسی عبادت واجب کی جائے اس لئے کافر غلام کا صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر مسئلہ برعکس ہو یعنی غلام مسلمان ہو اور مولی کا فر ہو تو بالا تفاق صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ ہمارے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ مولی کا فر ہونے کی وجہ سے نہ وجوب صدقہ کا اہل ہے اور نہ ادا صدقہ کا اور مام شافعی کے نزدیک وجوب اگر چہ غلام پر ہوتا ہے لیکن ادا مولی کو کرنا پڑتا ہے اور مولیٰ کا فر ہونے کی وجہ سے ادائے عبادت کا اہل نہیں ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بالکل صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Fitrah for a non-Muslim slave is upon the Muslim master. And the Muslim performs the Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave due to the generality of what we have narrated, and due to his statement (PBUH) in the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Pay for every free person and slave, Jew, Christian, or Magian'—the hadith. And because the cause (sabab) is established and the master is qualified (ahl) for it. And there is the disagreement of al-Shafi'i because, according to him, the obligation is upon the slave, and he (the non-Muslim slave) is not qualified. If it were the opposite (i.e., the slave is Muslim and the master is non-Muslim), then there is no obligation by consensus. Translation: And a Muslim will pay Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave due to the generality of the hadith we narrated, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas in which the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Pay sadaqah for every free and slave, Jew, Christian, or Magian.' And because the cause has been realized and the master is qualified for it. And in this, there is the disagreement of Imam al-Shafi'i because, according to him, the obligation is upon the slave, and a non-Muslim slave is not qualified. If the case were the opposite (i.e., the slave is Muslim and the master is non-Muslim), then by consensus there is no obligation. Explanation: The issue is that if a Muslim who owns the nisab possesses a non-Muslim slave, then Fitrah for that non-Muslim slave is also wajib upon him. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the Muslim master does not pay Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave; this is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Our proof is: First, in the first chapter, the hadith of Tha'labah ibn 'Umr (may Allah be pleased with him) 'Pay for every free and slave' is general, including both Muslim and non-Muslim slaves. Second, the hadith of Ibn Abbas, which 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam narrated from al-Daraqutni: 'The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: Pay the sadaqat al-fitr for every young and old, male and female, Jew, Christian, or Magian, free or slave: half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley.' Third, the cause for Fitrah being wajib is established because the Muslim master has complete wilayah over the non-Muslim slave and fully bears his maintenance, and the master is qualified for the obligation (of worship) even if the slave is not qualified due to disbelief. So when the cause of obligation is present and the master has qualification, then the master must pay Fitrah for the non-Muslim slave. According to al-Shafi'i, since Fitrah is wajib upon the slave (even though the master pays it), and a non-Muslim slave is not fit for an act of worship like Fitrah, therefore Fitrah is not wajib. If the case were the opposite—i.e., the slave is Muslim and the master is non-Muslim—then by consensus no Fitrah is wajib. According to us, because the non-Muslim master is neither qualified for wajub (the obligation) nor for ada' (performance) of the worship. According to al-Shafi'i, although the obligation is upon the slave, the master must pay it, and since the master is non-Muslim, he is not qualified to perform the worship, so no Fitrah is wajib in that case.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of Sadaqat al-Fitr for a non-Muslim slave owned by a Muslim. It is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i (and also Maliki and Hanbali) schools. The Hanafi position is that the Muslim master must pay Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave. The proof consists of two hadiths: (1) the general hadith of Tha'labah ibn 'Umr, 'Pay for every free and slave,' which is general and includes non-Muslim slaves; (2) the specific hadith of Ibn Abbas, narrated by al-Daraqutni, which explicitly mentions Jews, Christians, and Magians. Additionally, the Hanafis argue by reasoning (qiyas): the cause (sabab) for Fitrah being wajib is complete wilayah and mu'nah, which the master has over his slave regardless of the slave's religion. The master himself is qualified for the obligation (he is a Muslim). Therefore, the obligation is upon the master. The Shafi'i school holds that the obligation is upon the slave himself (even though the master performs it), and a non-Muslim is not qualified for worship obligations, so no Fitrah is due. The passage also mentions the reverse case (Muslim slave, non-Muslim master): by consensus, no Fitrah is due, but for different reasons in each school. The commentary further elaborates that the Hanafi view is supported by the generality of the hadith and the existence of the cause.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause for the obligation of Fitrah: complete wilayah (ownership/guardianship) and mu'nah (maintenance) over the slave.
اہلیت (ahliyyah): Legal capacity to be obligated for worship; a Muslim master has it, a non-Muslim slave does not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling that a Muslim must pay Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave?
A) The consensus of the Companions
B) The hadith of Ibn Abbas explicitly mentioning Jews, Christians, and Magians
C) The principle that all slaves are obligated
D) The analogy with zakah on wealth

Key Takeaway
The Muslim master must pay Fitrah for his non-Muslim slave because the cause of obligation (ownership and maintenance) is complete and the master is qualified, even if the slave is not.

Fitrah for a Slave Sold with Option (Khiyar)
Begins ruling on fitrah for slave sold with khiyar; cites Zufar and Shafi'i; Hanafi proof cut off.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three opinions on who pays fitrah for a slave when a sale is subject to khiyar, and identify the incomplete Hanafi proof.

Core Idea
Fitrah liability during khiyar turns on whether authority (wilayah) or ownership (milk) controls — a disputed issue.

This lesson parses a passage from al-Hidayah on fitrah for a slave sold with an option (khiyar) still pending on the day of Fitr. The matn gives the default Hanafi ruling, but the proof is cut off. We will examine the views of Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and al-Shafi‘i to understand the legal debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
A slave is sold with khiyar (option of cancellation). The day of Fitr arrives while the option is still active. On whom is the obligation to pay fitrah?
2
Recognize the matn's ruling
The text states: 'فَفِطْرَتُهُ عَلَى مَنْ يَصِيرُ لَهُ' — the fitrah is upon the one to whom the slave ultimately becomes (i.e., the eventual owner after the option period).
This is the default Hanafi position, but its proof is missing from this manuscript.
3
Understand Zufar's position
Zufar holds that fitrah is upon the one who holds the option (khiyar) because that person has authority (wilayah) over the slave during the option period.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar, so this is an intra-madhhab difference.
4
Understand al-Shafi'i's position
Al-Shafi'i argues that fitrah is upon the one who owns the slave (the seller, since ownership has not yet transferred) by analogy to nafaqah (maintenance).
This is an inter-madhhab difference.
5
Note the incomplete Hanafi proof
The passage ends with 'وَلَنَا أَنَّ' (And we say that…), but the rest is missing. The full Hanafi argument must be sought from a complete source.
Do not assume the missing proof; this lesson only covers the stated positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشتری پر خریدے ہوئے غلام کا صدقہ فطر لازم ہے
قَالَ وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا وَاَحَدُهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ فَفِطْرَتُهُ عَلَى مَنْ يَصِيرُ لَهُ مَعْنَاهُ أَنه إِذَا مَرَّيَوْمُ الْفِطْرِ وَالْحَيَارُ بَاقِ وَ قَالَ زُفَرُ عَلى مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ لأنَّ الوِلايَةَ لَهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعَى عَلَى مَنْ لَهُ الْمِلْكُ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ وَطَائِفَهِ كَالنَّفَقَةِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ
Fitrah for a purchased slave is obligatory on the buyer. He said: And whoever sells a slave while one of them has the option, then his Fitrah is upon the one to whom he becomes (i.e., the slave becomes). Meaning that when the day of Fitr passes while the option is still pending, and Zufar said: upon the one who has the option, because the authority (wilayah) is for him. And al-Shafi'i said: upon the one who has ownership, because it is from his dependents like maintenance. And we (Hanafis) say that...
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage introduces the ruling on Fitrah for a slave that has been sold but an option (khiyar) is still pending for either the seller or the buyer. The matn states that the Fitrah is upon the one to whom the slave ultimately belongs (i.e., if the sale is finalized, the buyer; if the sale is rescinded, the seller). If the day of Fitr occurs while the option is still active, Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) says the Fitrah is upon the one who holds the option because he has the authority (wilayah) over the slave. Al-Shafi'i says it is upon the one who holds the ownership (the seller, because ownership has not transferred) similar to nafaqah. The Hanafi position begins with 'ولنا أنَّ' (And we say that...) but the text cuts off, so the complete ruling and proof are not available. This passage is incomplete and requires the full text from a complete edition.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to cancel a sale within a specified period.
فطرة (fitrah): Alms given at the end of Ramadan (sadaqat al-fitr), wajib upon every free Muslim who has enough wealth for himself and his dependents.
ولاية (wilayah): Authority or guardianship; in this context, the power of control over the slave during the option period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Upon the buyer
B) Upon the seller
C) Upon the one with the option
D) Upon the slave

Key Takeaway
Fitrah liability for a slave in a khiyar sale is disputed: the matn says upon ultimate owner, Zufar says upon option holder, Shafi‘i says upon seller.

Fitr for a Kafir Slave: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling with proof and Shafi'i disagreement on fitr for kafir slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fitr for a kafir slave, cite the primary proof, and explain why the obligation is on the master rather than the slave.

Core Idea
The Muslim master pays fitr for his kafir slave because guardianship, not worship eligibility, triggers the obligation.

This lesson examines a specific inter-madhhab dispute: whether a Muslim master must pay sadaqat al-fitr on behalf of his kafir slave. The Hanafi school rules that it is wajib, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. Understanding the basis of each position reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes the relationship of guardianship (wilayah) over the worship capacity of the dependent.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the Muslim master must pay fitr for his kafir slave. This is the established Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi dispute exists on this point.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (along with Malik and Ahmad) holds that fitr is not wajib for a kafir slave. Their reasoning: the obligation is on the slave himself, and a kafir cannot be obligated for worship.
The source also mentions consensus on the reverse case (Muslim slave, kafir master) – no obligation.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: fitr is an act of worship, and a kafir is not eligible for worship obligations. Therefore, the master should not pay on his behalf.
This argument assumes the obligation rests on the slave.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the obligation is on the master due to his wila' (guardianship) and maintenance responsibility, not on the slave. The master's eligibility (being Muslim and having the means) suffices.
The Hanafi school cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the absolute hadith as textual proofs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi master pays fitr for his kafir slave; a Shafi'i master does not. This affects the master's Ramadan obligations.
The thamarah is clear and directly impacts practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُؤدّى المُسْلِمُ الْفِطْرَةَ عَنْ عَبْدِهِ الْكَافِرِ لِإِطْلَاقِ مَارَوَيْنَاهُ وَلِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ فِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عَبَاسٍ أَدُّوا عَنْ كُلّ حُرَ وَعَبْدِ يَهُودِي أَوْ نَصْرَانِي أَوْ مَجُوسِي الْحَدِيثِ. وَلِأَنَّ السَّبَبَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ وَالْمَوْلَى مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَفِيهِ خِلافُ الشَّافِعِي لِأَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عِنْدَهُ عَلَى الْعَبْدِ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَلَوْ كَانَ عَلَى الْعَكْسِ فَلَا وُجُوبَ بِالْإِنْفَاقُ

ترجمہ اور مسلمان اپنے کا فرغلام کی طرف سے فطرہ ادا کرے گا اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے اور حدیث ابن عباس میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان ہے کہ صدقہ ادا کر و ہر آزاد اور غلام یہودی یا نصرانی یا مجوسی کی طرف سے اور اس لئے کہ سبب تحقق ہو گیا اور مولی اس کا اہل ہے اور اس میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک صدقہ کا وجوب غلام پر ہے اور کافر غلام اس کا اہل نہیں ہے اور اگر مسئلہ بر عکس ہو تو بالا تفاق وجوب نہیں ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسلمان مالک نصاب اگر کافر غلام کا مالک ہو تو اس پر کا فر غلام کا صدقۃ الفطر بھی واجب ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک کا فرغلام کی طرف سے مسلمان مولی صدقہ ادا نہ کرے یہی قول امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اول باب میں ثعلبہ بن عمر کی حدیث ادواعَنْ كُلّ حُرو عبد (الحدیث ) مطلق ہے جو عبد مسلم اور عبد کا فر دونوں کو شامل ہے۔ دوسری دلیل این عباس کی حدیث ہے علامہ ابن الہمام نے دار قطنی کے حوالہ سے یہ حدیث اس طرح ذکر کی ہے قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ادو اصدقة الفطر عَنْ كُلَّ صَغِيرِ وَكبير ذكر وانثى يهودى اَوْ نَصْرَانِي حر او مملوک نِصف صاع من براو صَاعاً مِنْ تَمَرٍ أو شعير ، تیسری دلیل ہو ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کا سبب پایا گیا کیونکہ مسلمان مولی کو کافر غلام نیر ولایت کا ملہ بھی حاصل ہے اور اس کی مکمل طور پر مونت بھی برداشت کرتا ہے اور مولی وجوب صدقہ کا اہل بھی ہے اگر چہ غلام کا فر ہونے کی وجہ سے اہل نہیں ہے پس جب سبب وجوب بھی پایا گیا اور مولی کے اندر اہلیت بھی موجود ہے تو مولی پر کا فرغلام کی طرف سے صدقہ واجب ہو جائے گا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر چونکہ غلام پر واجب ہوتا ہے اگر چہ ادا مولی کرتا ہے اور کا فر غلام اس لائق نہیں کہ اس پر صدقہ الفطر جیسی عبادت واجب کی جائے اس لئے کافر غلام کا صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر مسئلہ برعکس ہو یعنی غلام مسلمان ہو اور مولی کا فر ہو تو بالا تفاق صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ ہمارے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ مولی کا فر ہونے کی وجہ سے نہ وجوب صدقہ کا اہل ہے اور نہ ادا صدقہ کا اور مام شافعی کے نزدیک وجوب اگر چہ غلام پر ہوتا ہے لیکن ادا مولی کو کرنا پڑتا ہے اور مولیٰ کا فر ہونے کی وجہ سے ادائے عبادت کا اہل نہیں ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بالکل صدقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
And the Muslim pays the fitr on behalf of his kafir slave due to the absolute nature of what we have narrated, and due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Pay on behalf of every free person and slave, Jew, Christian or Zoroastrian' – the hadith. And because the cause has materialized and the master is qualified. In this is the disagreement of al-Shafi'i because according to him the obligation is on the slave and he is not qualified. And if the situation were reversed, there is no obligation by agreement.

Translation: And the Muslim will pay fitr on behalf of his kafir slave due to the absolute nature of this hadith which we have narrated, and in the hadith of Ibn Abbas, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Pay charity on behalf of every free person and slave, Jew, Christian or Zoroastrian.' And because the cause has materialized and the master is qualified. In this is the disagreement of Imam Shafi'i, because according to him the obligation of charity is on the slave, and a kafir slave is not qualified. And if the situation is reversed, then by agreement there is no obligation.

Explanation: The issue is that if a Muslim who is a possessor of nisab owns a kafir slave, then the fitr of the kafir slave is wajib upon him. According to Imam Shafi'i, the Muslim master should not pay fitr on behalf of the kafir slave. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Our proof is that in the first chapter, the hadith of Tha'laba ibn 'Umar: 'Pay on behalf of every free person and slave' (the hadith) is absolute, including Muslim slave and kafir slave. The second proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas; 'Allama Ibn al-Humam narrated from al-Daraqutni that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Pay the sadaqat al-fitr on behalf of every young and old, male and female, Jew or Christian, free or slave, half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley.' The third proof is that the cause of the obligation of fitr has existed because the Muslim master has the right of wila' over the kafir slave and bears his expenses fully, and the master is qualified for the obligation of charity although the slave, due to being kafir, is not qualified. So when the cause of obligation exists and the master has the eligibility, then the fitr becomes wajib on the master on behalf of the kafir slave. According to Imam Shafi'i, since fitr is wajib on the slave even if the master pays, and a kafir slave is not worthy of having an act of worship like fitr wajib upon him, therefore fitr for a kafir slave is not wajib. And if the situation is reversed, i.e., the slave is Muslim and the master is kafir, then by agreement fitr is not wajib. According to us, because the master, being kafir, is not qualified for the obligation of charity nor for its payment. According to Imam Shafi'i, although the obligation is on the slave, the master must pay, and the master being kafir is not qualified to perform an act of worship, so in that case fitr is not wajib at all.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its proofs and the disagreement of Imam Shafi'i. The Hanafi ruling is that a Muslim master must pay sadaqat al-fitr on behalf of his kafir slave. The author gives three proofs: first, the absolute hadith from the beginning of the book; second, the specific hadith of Ibn Abbas reported by al-Daraqutni; third, a rational argument that the cause of obligation (the presence of a dependent) and the master's eligibility both exist. The Shafi'i position holds that the obligation is on the slave himself, and a kafir is not qualified for worship, so the master should not pay. The Hanafi response is that the obligation is on the master due to his right of wila' (guardianship) and his responsibility for maintenance, not on the slave. The passage also notes the consensus on the reverse case: if the slave is Muslim and the master kafir, fitr is not wajib. This is a clear example of how the Hanafi school distinguishes between the one on whom the obligation rests and the one who performs the worship.

Key Terms
فطرة (fitrah): Sadaqat al-fitr, the charity given at the end of Ramadan.
عبد (abd): A male slave owned by a master.
مولی (mawla): The master/owner of a slave.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship or authority over a dependent, including a slave.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; the legal requirement to perform an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The kafir slave himself
B) The Muslim master
C) The Muslim master only if the slave is Muslim
D) No one, because fitr is not wajib for slaves

Key Takeaway
A Muslim master must pay fitr for his kafir slave because the obligation arises from guardianship, not the slave's capacity for worship.

Fitr for a Slave Sold with an Option (Khiyar)
Ruling with three views on fitr for a slave sold with khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on fitr for a slave sold with khiyar, explain the distinction from nafaqah, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf among the three views.

Core Idea
Ownership suspended during khiyar: fitr follows the final owner, not the option holder.

This lesson examines a three-way ikhtilaf on who bears the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr for a slave when a conditional option (khiyar) is pending on the day of Eid. The Hanafi school argues that ownership is suspended (milk mawquf), so the obligation is also suspended until the option is resolved. You will learn to distinguish this from nafaqah (maintenance), which is immediate, and understand the practical consequence of each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling from the text: fitr is on the one for whom the slave ultimately becomes (the final owner after the option is exercised).
This is the view of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
Identify the opposing views
Name the two other positions: Zufar (on the holder of the option) and al-Shafi'i (on the buyer immediately). Note their respective proofs.
Zufar's basis is wilaya; Shafi'i's basis is ownership and analogy to nafaqah.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Explain Zufar's reasoning (wilaya gives authority over the slave) and Shafi'i's reasoning (ownership is established at contract, so fitr is like nafaqah).
Shafi'i uses qiyas to nafaqah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes fitr from nafaqah: nafaqah is an immediate need and cannot be suspended, whereas fitr can be delayed. Therefore, fitr follows the suspended ownership.
Key distinction: al-hajah al-najizah (immediate need) vs. fitr which can be paid later.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical difference: if the option is exercised to cancel, the obligation falls on the seller (Hanafi), the option holder (Zufar), or the buyer (Shafi'i).
This shows how the same scenario yields different rulings.

Source Text

قَالَ وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا وَاَحَدُهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ فَفِطْرَتُهُ عَلَى مَنْ يَصِيرُ لَهُ مَعْنَاهُ أَنه إِذَا مَرَّيَوْمُ الْفِطْرِ وَالْحَيَارُ بَاقِ وَ قَالَ زُفَرُ عَلى مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ لأنَّ الوِلايَةَ لَهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعَى عَلَى مَنْ لَهُ الْمِلْكُ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ وَطَائِفَهِ كَالنَّفَقَةِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْمِلْكَ مُوْقُوفٌ لأنَّهُ لَوْ رُدُّيَعُودُ إِلى مِلْكِ الْبَائِعِ وَلَوْ اَجِيُزَ يَثْبُتُ الْمِلْكُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي مِنْ وَقْتِ الْعَقْدِ فَيَتَوَقَّفُ مَا يَبْتَنِي عَلَيْهِ بِخِلَافِ النَّفَقَةِ لأنَّهَا لِلْحَاجَةِ النَّاجِزَةِ فَلا تَقْبَلُ التَّوَقُفَ وَ زَكوةُ التِّجَارَةِ عَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ

ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے غلام فروخت کیا اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو خیار ہے تو اس کا فطرہ اس پر واجب ہوگا جس کے لئے وہ ہو جائے گا اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جب فطرہ کا دن گذرا اور خیار باقی ہے اور امام زفر نے کہا کہ اس پر واجب ہے جس کے لئے خیار ہے کیونکہ ولایت اس کو حاصل ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا اس پر واجب ہے جسکے لئے ملک حاصل ہے کیونکہ وجوب فطرہ ملک کے وظائف میں سے ہے جیسے نفقہ ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ملک موقوف ہے اس لئے کہ اگر بیع ر کی گئی تو وہ بالغ کی ملک میں لوٹ آئے گی اور اگر اجازت دی گئی تو ملک مشتری کے لئے عقد کے وقت سے ثابت ہو جائیگی پس جو چیز ملک پر مبنی ہے وہ بھی موقوف رہے گی برخلاف نفقہ کے کیونکہ نفقه فوری ضرورت ہے لہذا وہ تو قف کو قبول نہیں کرے گا اور تجارتی زکوۃ بھی اسی اختلاف پر ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنا غلام فروخت کر دیا اور بائع یا مشتری نے اپنے لئے تین دن کا خیار شرط لے لیا تو صدقہ الفطر اس پر واجب ہوگا جس کا یہ غلام ہو جائے گا یعنی اگر بیع پوری ہوگئی تو صدقہ مشتری پر واجب ہوگا اور اگر ٹوٹ گئی تو صدقہ بائع پر واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عید کا دن گذر گیا لیکن خیارا بھی باقی ہے تو ایسی صورت میں صدقہ اس پر واجب ہوگا جس کا وہ غلام ہو جائے گا یعنی اگر بیع ہوگئی تو مشتری ادا کرے گا اور اگر صاحب خیار نے بیچ تو ڑ دی تو بائع پر واجب ہوگا۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ یہ غلام خدمت کے لئے تھا اور مشتری نے بھی خدمت ہی کے لئے خریدا ہے کیونکہ تجارتی غلام میں کسی پر صدقہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اور امام زفر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ جس کے لئے خیار ہے صدقہ اسی پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ صدقۃ الفطر کا سبب ولایت کا ملہ ہے اور ولایت کا ملہ اسی کو حاصل ہے جسکے لئے خیار ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ اگر اس نے بیج کو جائز قرار دیا تو بیع پوری ہو جائے گی اور اگر جائز نہ کیا تو فسخ ہو جائے گی پس جب ولایت كامل من له الخیار کو حاصل ہے تو صدقہ بھی اسی پر واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اس غلام کا صدقہ اس پر واجب ہو گا جس کے لئے ملک ثابت ہے اور ملک ثابت ہوتی ہے مشتری کے لئے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک خیار شرط مشتری کے واسطے ملک ثابت ہونے کو منع نہیں کرتا پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک غلام کا صدقۃ الفطر مشتری پر واجب ہو گا خواہ خیار شرط کسی کے لئے ہو۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر ملک کے وظائف میں سے ہے اس لئے مالک پر واجب ہوگا۔ اور خیار شرط کی صورت میں ملک ثابت ہوتی ہے مشتری کے لئے جیسا کہ امام شافعی کا مذہب ہے اس لئے صدقۃ الفطر مشتری پر واجب ہوگا جیسا کہ مدت خیار میں غلام کا نفقہ مالک مشتری پر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر ملک کا وظیفہ ہے لیکن یہاں ملک موقوف ہے اس لئے کہ من له الخیار نے اگر اپنے خیار کے تحت بیع کو رد کر دیا تو بائع کی ملک لوٹ آئے گی اور اگر جائز کر دیا تو عقد کے وقت سے مشتری کے لئے ملک ثابت ہو جائے گی اور قاعدہ ہے کہ شئی موقوف پر اگر کوئی چیز بنی ہوتو وہ بھی موقوف رہے گی پس ثابت ہوا کہ ملک موقوف جس کے لئے ثابت ہوگی صدقۃ الفطر بھی اس پر واجب ہوگا بر خلاف نفقہ کے کہ نفقہ اگر چہ ملک پر مبنی ہے لیکن وہ فوری ضرورت کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ تو قف کو قبول نہیں کرے گا بلکہ نفقہ کے بارے میں فوری فیصلہ کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور صدقۃ الفطر ایسا نہیں ہے کہ دو چار روز بعد بھی ادا کیا جا سکتا ہے پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے صدقۃ الفطر کو فقہ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تجارتی غلاموں کی زکوۃ میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے مثلاً کسی کے پاس تجارتی غلام میں اس نے بشرط خیار
He said: And whoever sells a slave while one of them has an option (khiyar), then his fitr is upon the one for whom it becomes. Meaning that when the day of fitr passes and the option remains, Zufar said: upon the one who has the option because the wilaya is his. Al-Shafi'i said: upon the one who has ownership because it is from the functions of ownership like maintenance. Our argument is that ownership is suspended, because if the sale is rescinded, it returns to the seller's ownership; if it is ratified, ownership is established for the buyer from the time of contract. So whatever is based on ownership is also suspended, unlike maintenance because it is an immediate need, so it does not accept suspension. And the zakat of trade is upon this dispute.

Translation: And the person who sold a slave and one of them has an option, then his fitr is wajib on the one for whom it becomes. Its meaning is that when the day of fitr passes and the option remains, Imam Zufar said: it is wajib on the one who has the option because wilaya is in his hand. Imam Shafi'i said: it is wajib on the one who has ownership because the obligation of fitr is from the functions of ownership, like maintenance. And our argument is that ownership is suspended, because if the sale is rescinded, it returns to the seller's ownership; if permission is given, ownership is established for the buyer from the time of the contract. So whatever is based on ownership will also be suspended. Unlike maintenance, because it is an immediate need, so it does not accept suspension. And the zakat of trade is also upon this dispute.

Explanation: The scenario is that if someone sold his slave and the seller or buyer stipulated an option of three days for himself, then sadaqat al-fitr is wajib on the one to whom this slave will belong. If the sale is completed, fitr is wajib on the buyer; if it is broken, fitr is wajib on the seller. The author of al-Hidayah (may Allah have mercy on him) says that its meaning is: the day of Eid passes while the option is still remaining, then in such a case fitr is wajib on the one to whom the slave will belong. That is, if the sale goes through, the buyer pays; if the person having the option rescinds the sale, then it is wajib on the seller. Note that this slave was for service and the buyer also bought him for service, because for a trade slave fitr is not wajib on anyone. The madhhab of Imam Zufar is that fitr is wajib on the one who has the option because the cause of fitr is the possession of wila', and the possession of wila' is with the one who has the option, because if he ratifies the sale, the sale is completed, and if he does not, it is annulled. So when complete wila' is with the one having the option, fitr is wajib on him. The madhhab of Imam Shafi'i is that fitr of this slave is wajib on the one for whom ownership is established, and ownership is established for the buyer because according to them a conditional option does not prevent ownership from being established for the buyer. So the result is that according to Imam Shafi'i, fitr of the slave is wajib on the buyer regardless of who has the conditional option. The argument of Imam Shafi'i is that fitr is from the functions of ownership, so it is wajib on the owner. And in the case of a conditional option, ownership is established for the buyer as per his madhhab, so fitr is wajib on the buyer, just as during the option period the maintenance of the slave is wajib on the owner-buyer. Our argument is that we concede that fitr is a function of ownership, but here ownership is suspended because if the one having the option rescinds the sale, ownership returns to the seller; if he ratifies it, ownership is established for the buyer from the time of the contract. And the rule is that anything built upon a suspended thing is also suspended. So it is established that fitr will be wajib on the one to whom the suspended ownership becomes established, unlike maintenance. Although maintenance is based on ownership, it is established due to immediate need, so it does not accept suspension; rather, an immediate decision about maintenance is necessary. And fitr is not like that; it can be paid a few days later. So because of this difference, it is not correct to analogize fitr to maintenance. The author of al-Hidayah says that the same dispute applies to the zakat of trade slaves.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on sadaqat al-fitr for a slave sold with a conditional option (khiyar al-shart). The matn states that fitr is on the one for whom the slave ultimately becomes, meaning it is suspended until the option is exercised. Three views are given: Imam Zufar says fitr is on the one holding the option due to wilaya; Imam Shafi'i says it is on the buyer because ownership is established at the time of contract; and the Hanafi view (shared by Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) is that ownership is suspended, so fitr follows the final owner. The key difference from nafaqah (maintenance) is that nafaqah is an immediate need and cannot be postponed, while fitr can be delayed. Therefore, fitr is suspended, unlike maintenance. The passage also notes that this dispute applies to zakat on trade goods held under such an option.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): Option or choice in a contract, allowing one party to rescind or confirm within a specified period.
ملک موقوف (milk mawquf): Suspended ownership; ownership that is not finalized until a condition (like exercising an option) is fulfilled.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship or authority; here, the authority over the slave that determines who benefits from his service.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance, daily expenses for a dependent (like food, clothing, shelter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, on whom does sadaqat al-fitr become wajib for a slave sold with a conditional option (khiyar) when the option is still pending?
A) The seller
B) The buyer
C) The person holding the option (man lahu al-khiyar)
D) The one to whom the slave ultimately belongs after the option is resolved

Key Takeaway
For a slave sold with khiyar, fitr is suspended until the final ownership is determined; it is not immediate like nafaqah.

Sadaqat al-Fitr for a Slave Sold with Khiyar: The Dispute Among Imams
Inter-madhhab dispute over fitr obligation during khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who must pay sadaqat al-fitr for a slave sold with khiyar, explain why ownership is suspended, and distinguish fitr from nafaqah in the context of khiyar.

Core Idea
Ownership suspended means fitr awaits final owner; fitr can wait, nafaqah cannot.

When a slave is sold with a condition of option (khiyar), ownership is not finalized until the option period ends. This creates a dispute: on whom does sadaqat al-fitr become obligatory if the day of fitr passes during the option period? The Hanafi school, Imam Zufar, and Imam al-Shafi'i each argue different positions, hinging on the nature of suspended ownership (milk mawquf) and whether fitr can be delayed like nafaqah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
A slave is sold with a condition of option (khiyar) for either party. The day of Eid al-Fitr arrives during the option period. The question is: who is obligated to pay sadaqat al-fitr for that slave? The Hanafi school says we wait to see if the sale is finalized or rescinded. Imam Zufar says the one with khiyar must pay. Imam Shafi'i says the buyer must pay immediately.
The slave is for service, not trade; trade slaves have different rules.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that the obligation depends on final ownership. If the sale is ratified, the buyer pays; if rescinded, the seller pays. The reason is that during khiyar, ownership is suspended (milk mawquf). Any obligation based on ownership is also suspended until ownership is finalized. Fitr is not an immediate need, so it can be delayed.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Present Imam Zufar's alternative
Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) holds that the obligation falls on the one who has the khiyar (the option holder). His reasoning: sadaqat al-fitr is caused by complete authority (wilayah kamilah), and the option holder has that authority because he can decide whether to finalize the sale. Therefore, he should pay.
Zufar's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school.
4
Present Imam al-Shafi'i's alternative
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the obligation is on the buyer from the moment of the contract. In his school, khiyar does not suspend ownership; ownership transfers immediately to the buyer. Therefore, fitr, being a function of ownership, is due from the buyer. He analogizes fitr to nafaqah (maintenance), which is also due from the owner during the option period.
Shafi'i uses the nafaqah analogy to support his view.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response to the nafaqah analogy
The Hanafis reject the analogy to nafaqah. Nafaqah is for an immediate need (hajah najizah) and cannot be postponed, so it is due from the buyer even during khiyar. Fitr, however, can be paid a few days later, so it can wait until ownership is resolved. Thus, the analogy is invalid. The ruling for fitr follows the principle of suspended ownership.
This distinction between immediate and deferrable obligations is a key feature of Hanafi usul.

امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اس غلام کا صدقہ اس پر واجب ہو گا جس کے لئے ملک ثابت ہے اور ملک ثابت ہوتی ہے مشتری کے لئے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک خیار شرط مشتری کے واسطے ملک ثابت ہونے کو منع نہیں کرتا پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک غلام کا صدقۃ الفطر مشتری پر واجب ہو گا خواہ خیار شرط کسی کے لئے ہو۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر ملک کے وظائف میں سے ہے اس لئے مالک پر واجب ہوگا۔ اور خیار شرط کی صورت میں ملک ثابت ہوتی ہے مشتری کے لئے جیسا کہ امام شافعی کا مذہب ہے اس لئے صدقۃ الفطر مشتری پر واجب ہوگا جیسا کہ مدت خیار میں غلام کا نفقہ مالک مشتری پر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر ملک کا وظیفہ ہے لیکن یہاں ملک موقوف ہے اس لئے کہ من له الخیار نے اگر اپنے خیار کے تحت بیع کو رد کر دیا تو بائع کی ملک لوٹ آئے گی اور اگر جائز کر دیا تو عقد کے وقت سے مشتری کے لئے ملک ثابت ہو جائے گی اور قاعدہ ہے کہ شئی موقوف پر اگر کوئی چیز بنی ہو تو وہ بھی موقوف رہے گی پس ثابت ہوا کہ ملک موقوف جس کے لئے ثابت ہوگی صدقۃ الفطر بھی اس پر واجب ہوگا بر خلاف نفقہ کے کہ نفقہ اگر چہ ملک پر مبنی ہے لیکن وہ فوری ضرورت کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ تو قف کو قبول نہیں کرے گا بلکہ نفقہ کے بارے میں فوری فیصلہ کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور صدقۃ الفطر ایسا نہیں ہے کہ دو چار روز بعد بھی ادا کیا جا سکتا ہے پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے صدقۃ الفطر کو نفقہ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تجارتی غلاموں کی زکوۃ میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے مثلاً کسی کے پاس تجارتی غلام تھے اس نے بشرط خیار ان کو فروخت کر دیا اور مدت خیار میں سال پورا ہو گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک زکوۃ اس پر واجب ہوگی جو ان غلاموں کا مالک ہو جائے گا اور امام زفر کے نزدیک اس پر واجب ہوگی جس کے لئے خیار ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس پر واجب ہوگی جس کے لئے اس وقت ملک ثابت ہے یعنی مشتری پر واجب ہوگی۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Ownership is suspended because if the sale is rescinded, it returns to the seller's ownership, and if it is ratified, ownership is established for the buyer from the time of the contract. Thus what is built upon it is also suspended. Unlike maintenance (nafaqah), because it is for an immediate need, so it does not accept suspension. And zakat of trade is also upon this disagreement. Translation: And the person who sold a slave and one of the two has an option, then the fitr is obligatory upon the one for whom the slave becomes, meaning when the day of fitr passes and the option remains. Imam Zufar said it is obligatory upon the one who has the option because he has authority (wilayah). Imam Shafi'i said it is obligatory upon the one who has ownership because the obligation of fitr is from the functions of ownership, like maintenance. And our proof is that ownership is suspended because if the sale is rescinded it returns to the seller's ownership, and if ratified it is established for the buyer from the contract time. Thus whatever is based on ownership is also suspended, unlike maintenance because it is an immediate need, so it does not accept suspension. And zakat of trade is also upon this disagreement. Explanation: The case is that if someone sold his slave and the seller or buyer stipulated an option of three days for himself, then sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory upon the one for whom the slave becomes. If the sale is completed, it is upon the buyer; if rescinded, upon the seller. As for Imam Zufar's madhhab: it is obligatory upon the one who has the option because the cause of sadaqat al-fitr is complete authority, and complete authority belongs to the one with the option. As for Imam Shafi'i's madhhab: it is upon the one for whom ownership is established, and ownership is established for the buyer because in his view the option does not prevent ownership. So according to Shafi'i, fitr is upon the buyer regardless of who has the option. Shafi'i's proof: sadaqat al-fitr is from the functions of ownership, so it is obligatory upon the owner. And with khiyar, ownership is for the buyer, so fitr is upon the buyer, just like maintenance during the option period. Our proof: we agree that fitr is a function of ownership, but here ownership is suspended. If the one with the option rescinds, ownership returns to seller; if ratifies, it is established for buyer from contract time. The rule is that what is built upon a suspended thing is also suspended. Thus fitr is obligatory upon whoever ultimately owns. Unlike maintenance, which is for immediate need and does not accept suspension, fitr can be paid a few days later, so analogy to maintenance is incorrect. The author says the same dispute applies to zakat of trade slaves.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whom sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory upon for a slave sold with a condition of option (khiyar). The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that the obligation depends on who becomes the final owner of the slave after the option period. If the sale is ratified, the buyer pays; if rescinded, the seller pays. This is because ownership is suspended (milk mawquf) during the option period. Imam Zufar holds that it is obligatory on the one who has the option (khiyar) because he has complete authority (wilayah) over the transaction. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is obligatory on the buyer from the beginning because he is the owner during the option period in his view. The Hanafi reasoning distinguishes sadaqat al-fitr from maintenance (nafaqah), which is an immediate need and cannot be suspended. The same dispute extends to zakat of trade slaves. The passage emphasizes that the slave in question is for service, not for trade, as trade slaves do not incur sadaqat al-fitr.

Key Terms
ملک موقوف (milk mawquf): Suspended ownership – ownership that is not finalized until a condition (like khiyar) is resolved.
خیار (khiyar): Option to rescind or ratify a sale, typically for three days.
صدقۃ الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan per person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Shafi'i, who is obligated to pay sadaqat al-fitr for a slave sold with khiyar?
A) The seller, because the sale is not yet finalized.
B) The buyer, because ownership transfers immediately upon contract.
C) The one who has the khiyar (option), because of authority.
D) The obligation is suspended until the sale is finalized.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sadaqat al-fitr for a slave sold with khiyar is suspended until ownership is finalized, distinguishing it from nafaqah which is an immediate need.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Measure of Sadaqat al-Fitr: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute over sa' measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the required measure of sadaqat al-fitr for wheat, dates, and raisins, and explain the proof-based difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Half a sa' of wheat suffices; Shafi'i requires full sa' from all foods.

This lesson examines a well-known inter-madhhab dispute regarding the quantity of sadaqat al-fitr. While the obligation itself is unanimous, the measure—half sa' versus full sa'—varies by food type and school. You will learn the Hanafi position, its internal variants, and how the school defends it against the Shafi'i proof from the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the baseline Hanafi ruling: half sa' of wheat, flour, sawiq, and raisins; full sa' of dates and barley. Note the internal ikhtilaf on raisins.
Sahibayn consider raisins like barley (full sa'); primary narration puts it with wheat (half sa').
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a full sa' is required from all items. His proof is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, who described Companion practice during the Prophet's time as giving one sa' of each food.
The Hanafis do not reject the hadith; they interpret it differently.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the hadith can be understood as describing voluntary extra giving, not the obligatory minimum. Their own proof is the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and a group of Companions, which establishes half sa' for wheat.
The caliphs' practice is given legal weight as 'amal al-khulafa' al-rashidin.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi may give half a sa' of wheat, while a Shafi'i must give a full sa' of any staple food. This affects the amount due, especially when calculating value.
Both schools allow giving value (cash), but the minimum measure differs.
5
Note the mufta bihi and precaution
The relied-upon Hanafi position is half sa' of wheat or equivalent. However, giving a full sa' is considered mustahab (recommended) to leave disagreement. Also note the preference for cash (dirhams) over flour over wheat, as per Abu Yusuf's narration.
Giving cash is more beneficial to the poor and quicker.

وَالأَوَّلُ رِوَايَةُ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ مِنْ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ صَاعٌ لِحَدِيثِ أَبِي سَعِيدِ الْخُدْرِي قَالَ كُنَّا نَخْرُجُ ذَلِكَ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه
