قَالَ وَ الصَّاعُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ ثَمَانِيَةٌ أَرْطَالِ بِالْعَراقِي وَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ خَمْسَةُ أرْطَالٍ وَثُلُتُ طل وهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِى لِقَوْلِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ صَاعُنَا أَصْغَرُ الصَّيْعَانِ وَلَنَا مَارُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَانَ يَتَوَضَّأَ بِالْمُدِ رِطَلَيْنِ وَيَغْسِلُ بِالصَّاعِ ثَمَانِيَةَ أرْطَالٍ وهَكَذَا كَانَ صَاعُ عُمَرَ وَهُوَ اصْغَرُ مِنَ الْهَا شَمِى وَكَانُوا يَسْتَعْمِلُونَ الْهَا شَمِى
ترجمہ فرمایا کہ طرفین کے نزدیک صاع آٹھ رطل عراقی کا ہوتا ہے اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ پانچ رطل اور تہائی رطل کا ہوتا ہے اور یہی قول امام شافعی کا ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہمارا صاع سب صاعوں میں چھوٹا ہے اور ہماری دلیل وہ ہے جو مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم ایک مددور طل سے وضو کرتے تھے اور ایک صاع آٹھ رطل سے غسل کرتے تھے اور ایسا ہی حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ کا صاع تھا اور یہ صاع ہاشمی صاع سے چھوٹا ہوتا ہے اور لوگ ہاشمی صاع استعمال کیا کرتے تھے۔
تشریح صاع کے بارے میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے چنانچہ طرفین نے فرمایا کہ صاع وہ ہے جس میں عراقی آٹھ رطل وزن کے برابر گندم و غیرہ کوئی چیز سما سکے یعنی صاع عراقی آٹھ رطل کا ہوتا ہے اور ایک صاع میں چار مد ہوتے ہیں اور ایک رحل ہیں استاد کا ہوتا ہے اور ایک استار ساڑھے چھ درہم وزن کے برابر ہوتا ہے گویا ایک رطل ایک سو تیں درہم وزن کا ہوتا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ ایک صاع پانچ طل اور تہائی رطل کا ہوتا ہے یہی قول امام شافعی، امام مالک، امام احمد کا ہے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ حدیث ب صاعنا اصغر الصيعان یعنی ہمارا صاع سب صاعوں سے چھوٹا ہوتا ہے اور ظاہر ہی کہ پانچ رطل اور تہائی کا صاع به نسبت آٹھ رطل والے صاع کے چھوٹا ہوتا ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ صاح پانچ رطل اور تہائی رطل کا ہوتا ہے نیز ابن حبان نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ عنہ سے روایت کیا ہے أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قِيلَ لَهُ يَارَسُولَ اللهِ صَاعُنَا أَصْغَرُ الصِّبْيعَانِ وَمُدَّنا اكْبَرُ الأَمْدَادِ فَقَالَ اللَّهُمَّ بَارِك لَنَا فِى صَاعِنَا وَبَارِك لَنَا فِي قَلِينَا وَكَثِيرِنَا وَاجْعَل لَّنَا مَعَ الْبَرَكَةِ بر گتین یعنی خدا کے رسول سے عرض کیا گیا کہ یا رسول اللہ ہمارا صاع سب کے صاعوں سے چھوٹا ہے اور ہما را مد سب مدوں سے بڑ تو آپے نے دعا فرمائی کہ اے اللہ ! ہمارے صاع میں برکت فرما اور ہمارے قلیل اور کثیر میں برکت فرما اور ہمارے لئے ایک ایک برکت کے ساتھ دو۔ دو برکت پیدا فرما۔ ابن حبان کہتے ہیں کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کے صاع کے سب سے چھوٹا ہونے کا انکار نہیں کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ مدینہ منورہ کا صاع سب سے چھوٹا صاع ہے علامہ ابن الہمام نے حسن بن ولید قریشی کی روایت بیان کی ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف جب حج سے واپس ہو کر ہمارے یہاں آئے اور کہا کہ میں چاہتا ہوں کہ تمہارے اوپر علم کا ایک دروازہ کھولدوں جس نے مجھ کو بڑی فکر میں ڈال دیا تھا بس میں نے اس کا تتبع کیا تو میں مدینہ منورہ گیا اور میں نے باغ کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تو لوگوں نے کہا کہ ہمارا یہ صار رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا صاع ہے میں نے کہا کہ تمہارے پاس اس کی کیا دلیل ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا صاع ہے انہوں نے کہا کہ ہم
(The author) said: And the sa' according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad is eight Iraqi ratls. And Abu Yusuf said: five and one-third ratls, and this is the statement of al-Shafi'i, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Our sa' is the smallest of the two sa's.' And our proof is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform wudu with one mudd (two ratls) and ghusl with one sa' (eight ratls). And similarly was the sa' of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and it is smaller than the Hashimi sa', and they used to use the Hashimi sa'.
Translation: He said that according to the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad), the sa' is eight Iraqi ratls. And Abu Yusuf said that it is five and one-third ratls, and this is the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Our sa' is the smallest of the sa's.' And our proof is what is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to perform wudu with one mudd (two ratls) and ghusl with one sa' (eight ratls), and similarly was the sa' of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and this sa' is smaller than the Hashimi sa', and people used to use the Hashimi sa'.
Explanation: There is a disagreement among scholars about the sa'. So the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) said that the sa' is that in which eight Iraqi ratls by weight of wheat etc. can fit, i.e., the Iraqi sa' is eight ratls. And one sa' contains four mudd. And one ratl is twelve uqiyah, and one uqiyah is equal to six and a half dirhams in weight, so one ratl is one hundred and thirty dirhams in weight. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that one sa' is five and one-third ratls. This is also the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is this hadith: 'Our sa' is the smallest of the sa's.' And it is apparent that the sa' of five and one-third ratls is smaller than the sa' of eight ratls. Therefore we said that the sa' is five and one-third ratls. Also Ibn Hibban narrated from Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked: 'O Messenger of Allah, our sa' is the smallest of the sa's and our mudd is the largest of the mudds.' So he said: 'O Allah, bless us in our sa' and bless us in our little and our much, and make for us with every blessing two blessings.' Ibn Hibban says that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not deny their statement that their sa' is the smallest, so it is known that the sa' of Madinah is the smallest sa'. Allamah Ibn al-Humam narrated from Hasan ibn Walid al-Qurashi that Imam Abu Yusuf, when he returned from Hajj and came to us, said: 'I want to open for you a door of knowledge that had caused me great worry. I investigated it and went to Madinah. I asked about the garden, and the people said: This is the sa' of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). I said: What proof do you have that it is the sa' of the Messenger? They said: We...' (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the size of the sa' used for Sadaqat al-Fitr. The two main Hanafi authorities, Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, hold that the sa' equals eight Iraqi ratls, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who used a sa' of eight ratls for ghusl and a mudd of two ratls for wudu, as well as the sa' of Umar. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the sa' is five and one-third ratls, citing the hadith that 'our sa' is the smallest of the sa's' and a narration from Ibn Hibban where the Prophet did not deny that the Madinan sa' was the smallest. The commentary explains the conversion: one ratl equals 130 dirhams. Additionally, the passage includes a report from Abu Yusuf himself, who after investigation in Madinah confirmed the smaller sa'. The reader learns the basis for the Hanafi preferred position (eight ratls) and the alternative view. The dispute has practical implications for the exact amount of food or money one must give for Sadaqat al-Fitr.

Key Terms
صاع (ṣāʿ): A unit of volume/weight for measuring food grains; size disputed.
رطل عراقي (raṭl ʿirāqī): Iraqi ratl = 130 dirhams (approx. 406.25 grams).
هاشمي (hāshimī): A larger sa' used by the Banu Hashim; the Prophet's sa' was smaller than this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view of the Hanafi school on the size of the sa' for Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) Five and one-third ratls
B) Eight ratls
C) Ten ratls
D) Four ratls

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the sa' is eight Iraqi ratls, based on the Prophet's own practice, not on ambiguous verbal hadith.

The Weight of the Sa': Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sa' weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position (8 Iraqi ratls) on the weight of the sa', explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and evaluate the proofs for each position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi sa' is 8 ratls—Abu Yusuf's 5 1/3 is marjuh despite his empirical investigation.

In this lesson, we delve into a famous intra-Hanafi dispute: the weight of the sa' (a volumetric measure used for sadaqat al-fitr). While Abu Hanifa and Muhammad held that the sa' is eight Iraqi ratls, Abu Yusuf—after travelling to Madinah and directly measuring the Prophet's sa'—adopted a smaller measure of five and one-third ratls, aligning with the majority of other schools. We will examine the textual and empirical proofs on both sides and understand why the majority Hanafi view remains mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the two views: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: 8 ratls. Abu Yusuf: 5 1/3 ratls. Note that the latter matches the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools.
The term 'ratl' is the Iraqi ratl (130 dirhams).
2
Examine the proofs for each side
For Abu Hanifa/Muhammad: the hadith of the Prophet's wudu with 2 ratls and ghusl with 8 ratls, and the practice of Umar. For Abu Yusuf: the hadith 'Our sa' is the smallest of measures' and the empirical measurement by a group of Madinan descendants.
Abu Yusuf also cited the Ibn Hibban narration where the Prophet did not deny the smallness.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf's proof
The Hanafi response argues that 'our sa' is the smallest' refers to the Hashimi sa' (32 ratls), not an absolute statement. The 8-ratl sa' is indeed smaller than the Hashimi. The Prophet's own practice confirms 8 ratls.
The text emphasises that the hadith of wudu/ghusl is a stronger, action-based proof.
4
Determine the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
The thamarah al-khilaf: the amount of grain for fitrah differs significantly. The mufta bihi is 8 ratls, but precaution may favour a larger amount to ensure fulfilment.
The author then gives three calculation methods, with the largest being most precautionary.

تشریح صاع کے بارے میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے چنانچہ طرفین نے فرمایا کہ صاع وہ ہے جس میں عراقی آٹھ رطل وزن کے برابر گندم و غیرہ کوئی چیز سما سکے یعنی صاع عراقی آٹھ رطل کا ہوتا ہے اور ایک صاع میں چار مد ہوتے ہیں اور ایک رحل ہیں استاد کا ہوتا ہے اور ایک استار ساڑھے چھ درہم وزن کے برابر ہوتا ہے گویا ایک رطل ایک سو تیں درہم وزن کا ہوتا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ ایک صاع پانچ طل اور تہائی رطل کا ہوتا ہے یہی قول امام شافعی، امام مالک، امام احمد کا ہے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ حدیث ب صاعنا اصغر الصيعان یعنی ہمارا صاع سب صاعوں سے چھوٹا ہوتا ہے اور ظاہر ہی کہ پانچ رطل اور تہائی کا صاع به نسبت آٹھ رطل والے صاع کے چھوٹا ہوتا ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ صاح پانچ رطل اور تہائی رطل کا ہوتا ہے نیز ابن حبان نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ عنہ سے روایت کیا ہے أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قِيلَ لَهُ يَارَسُولَ اللهِ صَاعُنَا أَصْغَرُ الصِّبْيعَانِ وَمُدَّنا اكْبَرُ الأَمْدَادِ فَقَالَ اللَّهُمَّ بَارِك لَنَا فِى صَاعِنَا وَبَارِك لَنَا فِي قَلِينَا وَكَثِيرِنَا وَاجْعَل لَّنَا مَعَ الْبَرَكَةِ بر گتین یعنی خدا کے رسول سے عرض کیا گیا کہ یا رسول اللہ ہمارا صاع سب کے صاعوں سے چھوٹا ہے اور ہما را مد سب مدوں سے بڑ تو آپے نے دعا فرمائی کہ اے اللہ ! ہمارے صاع میں برکت فرما اور ہمارے قلیل اور کثیر میں برکت فرما اور ہمارے لئے ایک ایک برکت کے ساتھ دو۔ دو برکت پیدا فرما۔ ابن حبان کہتے ہیں کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کے صاع کے سب سے چھوٹا ہونے کا انکار نہیں کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ مدینہ منورہ کا صاع سب سے چھوٹا صاع ہے علامہ ابن الہمام نے حسن بن ولید قریشی کی روایت بیان کی ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف جب حج سے واپس ہو کر ہمارے یہاں آئے اور کہا کہ میں چاہتا ہوں کہ تمہارے اوپر علم کا ایک دروازہ کھولدوں جس نے مجھ کو بڑی فکر میں ڈال دیا تھا بس میں نے اس کا تتبع کیا تو میں مدینہ منورہ گیا اور میں نے باغ کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تو لوگوں نے کہا کہ ہمارا یہ صار رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا صاع ہے میں نے کہا کہ تمہارے پاس اس کی کیا دلیل ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا صاع ہے انہوں نے کہا کہ ہم
كُلِّ أَوَّلَ وَقْتٍ آپ کے پاس حجت پیش کریں گے۔ چنانچہ جب صبح ہوئی تو میرے پاس تقریبا پچاس بوڑھے آئے جو انصار ومہاجرین کی اولاد سے تھے ہر ایک کی چادر کے نیچے اس کا ایک صاع تھا اور ہر شخص نے اپنے باپ دادا سے سند بیان کر کے کہا کہ یہ رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا صاع ہے۔ پس جب میں نے ان کو دیکھا تو سب برابر تھے اور میں نے ان کو ناپ کر تو لا تو پانچ رطل اور
ایک تہائی رطل سے کچھ ہی کم نکلا ۔ یہ دیکھ کر میں نے حضرت الاستاد امام اعظم کے قول کو ترک کر دیا۔ ہماری دلیل حضرت انس اور حضرت جابر رضی اللہ تعالی عنہا کی یہ روایت ہے اُنَّه عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَتَوَضَّأَ بِالْمَةٍ رطلَيْن وَيَغْتَسِلُ بِالصَّاعِ ثَمَانِيَةَ أَرْطَال يعنى رسول ہاشمی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ایک مد یعنی دور طل پانی سے وضو کیا کرتے تھے اور ایک صاع یعنی آٹھ رطل پانی سے غسل کیا کرتے تھے اور ایسا ہی حضرت عمر کا صاع تھا بہر حال اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صاع آٹھہ طل کا
ہوتا ہے۔
اور امام ابو یوسف کی طرف سے پیش کردہ روایت صاعُنَا أَصْغَرَ الصَّيْعَانِ میں اصف صاع سے مراد یہ ہے کہ آٹھ طل والا صاع ہاشمی صاع سے چھوٹا ہے کیونکہ ہاشمی صاع بتیس رطل کا ہوتا تھا اور لوگ اس کو استعمال کرتے تھے جبکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم عراقی صاع ( جس میں آٹھ رطل ہوتے ہیں ) استعمال فرماتے تھے تو ہاشمی صاع کے مقابلہ میں کہا گیا کہ صَاعُنَا أَصَغَرُ الصّيعَان
فوائد صاع کا وزن معلوم کرنے کے تین طریقے ہیں: (۱) صاع کا وزن بحساب مثقال ایک مثقال چار ماشہ چار رتی کا ہوتا ہے مشتقال کے حساب سے صاع کا وزن تین ہزار دو سو چالیس ماشے بنتا ہے یعنی دوسوستر تو لہ اس حساب سے تین سیر چھ چھٹانک کا پورا صاع ہوا اور ڈیڑھ سیر تین چھٹا تک کا نصف صاع ہوا۔ (۲) درہم کے اعتبار سے ایک درہم تین ماشہ ایک رتی اور ایک بٹہ پانچ ( لٹھ ) رتی کا ہوتا ہے اس حساب سے ایک صاع دو سو تہتر تولے کا ہوگا۔ اور نصف صاع ایک سو چھتیس تولے چھ ماشے کا ہوتا ہے گو یا انگریزی سیر کے حساب سے پورا صاع تین سیر چھ چھٹا تک تین تولے کے برابر ہوتا ہے اور نصف صاع ڈیڑھ سیر تین چھٹا تک ڈیڑھ تو لے کے برابر ہے۔ (۳) مد کے اعتبار سے ایک مدار سٹھ تولہ تین ماشہ کا ہوتا ہے اس حساب سے ایک صاع دو سو اسی تو لے کچھ ماشہ کا بنتا ہے اور نصف صاع ایک سو چالیس تولے تین ماشے کا ہوتا ہے گویا پورا صاع ساڑھے تین سیر چھ ماشہ کا ہوا اور نصف صاع پونے دوسیر تین ماشہ کا واضح رہے کہ ایک صاع چار مد کا ہوتا ہے۔ ( درس ترندی جلد ۱ (۳۹۵) صاع کا وزن معلوم کرنے کے جو تین طریقے لکھے گئے ہیں ان میں سے جس طریقہ اور حساب کو بھی اختیار کر لیا جائے صدقۃ الفطر ادا ہو جائے گا لیکن چونکہ آخری حساب میں زیادتی ہے اس لئے اس کے مطابق ادا کرنے میں زیادہ احتیاط ہے یعنی پونے دوسیر تین ماشہ گندم یا ساڑھے تین سیر چھ ماشہ جو غیر ہ فطرہ میں ادا کیا جائے۔ جمیل احمد
Book of Zakah. Page 173. Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 3. It is preferable because there is no disagreement about wheat being permissible, and regarding money and price there is disagreement of Imam al-Shafi'i, so choosing the agreed-upon thing is better than choosing the disputed thing. And Allah knows best. Jamil Afi Anhu. The quantity of the Sa'... Statements of the Jurists. He said: The sa' according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is eight ratls by Iraqi measure, and Abu Yusuf said: five and one-third ratls, and that is the statement of al-Shafi'i, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Our sa' is the smallest of the measures.' And our proof is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform wudu with a mudd of two ratls and perform ghusl with a sa' of eight ratls, and likewise was the sa' of Umar, and it is smaller than the Hashimi measure, and they used to use the Hashimi measure. Translation: He said that according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the sa' is eight Iraqi ratls, and Abu Yusuf said it is five and one-third ratls, and this is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Our sa' is the smallest of measures.' And our proof is what is narrated: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to perform wudu with a mudd of two ratls and perform ghusl with a sa' of eight ratls, and likewise was the sa' of Umar, and it is smaller than the Hashimi sa', and people used to use the Hashimi sa'. Explanation: There is disagreement among scholars about the sa'. So the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) said: The sa' is that which can contain something like wheat etc. equal to eight ratls Iraqi weight, i.e., the sa' is eight ratls. And one sa' has four mudds. And one ratl is one uqiyya? and one uqiyya is six and a half dirhams in weight, so one ratl is one hundred thirty dirhams in weight. And Imam Abu Yusuf said: One sa' is five and one-third ratls. This is also the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is the hadith: 'Our sa' is the smallest of measures,' i.e., our sa' is smaller than all measures. And it is apparent that a sa' of five and one-third is smaller than a sa' of eight ratls, therefore we say the sa' is five and one-third ratls. Also Ibn Hibban narrated from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked: 'O Messenger of Allah, our sa' is the smallest of measures and our mudd is the largest of mudds.' He said: 'O Allah, bless our sa' and bless our little and our much, and make for us with blessing two blessings.' Ibn Hibban says that the Prophet did not deny that their sa' is the smallest, so it is known that the sa' of Madinah is the smallest sa'. Allamah Ibn al-Humann narrated from Hasan ibn Walid al-Qurashi that Imam Abu Yusuf, when he returned from Hajj and came to us, said: 'I want to open a door of knowledge for you that caused me great worry. I investigated it and went to Madinah and asked about the garden. People said: This is the sa' of the Messenger of Allah. I asked: What proof do you have that it is the Prophet's sa'? They said: We will present proof at the first time. So when morning came, about fifty old men from the descendants of the Ansar and Muhajirin came to me, each having a sa' under his cloak, and each person narrated from his father and grandfather saying: This is the sa' of the Messenger of Allah. When I saw them, they were all equal. I measured them and found them slightly less than five and one-third ratls. Seeing this, I abandoned the saying of my teacher the Great Imam. Our proof is the narration from Anas and Jabir that the Prophet used to perform wudu with a mudd of two ratls and ghusl with a sa' of eight ratls, and likewise was the sa' of Umar. Anyway, from this hadith it is known that the sa' is eight ratls. And regarding the narration presented by Imam Abu Yusuf 'Our sa' is the smallest of measures,' the meaning is that the sa' of eight ratls is smaller than the Hashimi sa', because the Hashimi sa' was thirty-two ratls and people used it, while the Prophet used the Iraqi sa' (which has eight ratls), so in comparison to the Hashimi sa' it was said 'Our sa' is the smallest of measures.' Benefits: There are three methods to determine the weight of the sa': (1) By mithqal: One mithqal is four mashas and four rattis. By this calculation, the sa' weighs 3240 mashas, i.e., 200 tolas? So a full sa' is three seers and six chhatanks, and half sa' is one and a half seers and three chhatanks. (2) By dirham: One dirham is three mashas, one ratti, and one bat'ha five (lath) rattis. By this calculation, one sa' is 273 tolas, and half sa' is 136 tolas and 6 mashas. In terms of English seer, a full sa' equals three seers, six chhatanks, and three tolas, and half sa' equals one and a half seers, three chhatanks, and one and a half tolas. (3) By mudd: One mudd is 60 tolas and 3 mashas. By this calculation, one sa' is 280 tolas and some mashas, and half sa' is 140 tolas and 3 mashas. So a full sa' is three and a half seers and 6 mashas, and half sa' is one and three-quarters seers and 3 mashas. Note that one sa' is four mudds. (Dars Tirmidhi vol. 1 p.395) Among the three methods given for determining the weight of the sa', whichever method and calculation is adopted, the sadaqat al-fitr will be fulfilled. But since the last calculation has an increase, it is more cautious to pay according to it, i.e., one and three-quarters seers and three mashas of wheat or three and a half seers and six mashas of other items for fitrah. Jamil Ahmad.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the legal measurement of the sa' (a volume measure used in zakat and sadaqat al-fitr) and the well-known intra-Hanafi dispute on its weight. It begins by stating that it is preferable to give in zakat what is agreed upon rather than what is disputed, referring to a previous discussion on wheat versus price. Then it presents the dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that the sa' is eight ratls (Iraqi weight), while Imam Abu Yusuf holds it is five and one-third ratls, which is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i. The proof for Abu Yusuf is the hadith 'Our sa' is the smallest of measures,' implying a smaller sa' is superior. The text then gives the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) counter-proof: the Prophet used two ratls for wudu and eight ratls for ghusl, and this was the standard of Umar. It explains that the hadith about 'smallest' refers to comparison with the larger Hashimi sa' (32 ratls), not an absolute statement. The passage then narrates a story of Imam Abu Yusuf's empirical investigation in Madinah that led him to adopt the smaller sa', but the author upholds the majority Hanafi view. Finally, it provides three calculation methods for the sa' weight in contemporary units, noting that any method fulfills the obligation but the most precautionary is the largest. This lesson is a classic example of Hanafi juridical methodology: weighing textual evidence (hadith), empirical verification, and practical precaution. The authority weight of the main ruling (sa' = 8 ratls) is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad and the standard in the madhhab. Abu Yusuf's view is a divergent opinion (nawadir) that he personally adopted but is not mufta bihi.

Key Terms
صاع (ṣāʿ): A measure of volume used for zakat and sadaqat al-fitr; its weight is disputed between 8 ratls (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad) and 5 1/3 ratls (Abu Yusuf).
رطل (ratl): A unit of weight; the Iraqi ratl equals 130 dirhams (approx. 408 grams in modern estimates).
مد (mudd): A measure equal to one-fourth of a sa' (2 ratls by the majority Hanafi view).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), how many Iraqi ratls are in one sa'?
A) 5 1/3 ratls
B) 8 ratls
C) 10 ratls
D) 32 ratls

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that the sa' is 8 Iraqi ratls, though Abu Yusuf's view (5 1/3 ratls) is a legitimate ikhtilaf; precaution favours the larger measure.

Time of Obligation for Sadaqat al-Fitr: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the time of wajib of fitrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the time of wajib of sadaqat al-fitr and explain the thamarah al-khilaf regarding cases of conversion, birth, and death on the night of Eid.

Core Idea
The obligation of fitrah begins at Fajr of Eid day, not sunset of the last day of Ramadan.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: when exactly does sadaqat al-fitr become wajib? The Hanafi school ties it to the dawn of Eid day, while Imam al-Shafi'i ties it to the sunset of the last day of Ramadan. This difference leads to practical consequences for those who convert, are born, or die on the night between the two views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi view (Fajr of Eid) and the Shafi'i view (sunset of last Ramadan). Note the precise timing.
2
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the two positions to three scenarios: conversion, birth, and death on the night of Eid. Observe how the ruling differs.
The practical consequence is the key to the dispute.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof is linguistic: the name 'fitrah' is derived from 'futur' (breaking the fast), which occurs on Eid day, thus the day of breaking the fast is the locus of obligation.
The source text mentions 'al-idafah li al-ikhtisas' (the attribution for specificity).
4
Recognize the Shafi'i dalil
The Shafi'i view ties the obligation to the completion of Ramadan, which ends at sunset. Thus the obligation is triggered at that moment.
The Shafi'i proof is based on the completion of the month.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
Within the Hanafi school, the position of Abu Hanifa (Fajr of Eid) is the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صدقہ فطر کے وجوب کا وقت
قَالَ وَوُجُوبُ الفِطْرَةِ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ مِن يَوْمِ الْفِطْرِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ بِعُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ فِى الْيَوْم الأخير مِنْ رَمَضَانَ حَتَّى إِنَّ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ أوْ وُلِدَ لَيْلَةَ الْفِطْر تَجِبُ فِطْرَتُهُ عِندَنَا وَ عِندَهُ لا تَجِبُ وَ عَلَى عَكْسِه مَنْ مَاتَ فِيهَا مِن مَّمَالِيْكه أو وَلَدِهِ لَهُ أَنَّهُ يَخْتَصُّ بِالْفِطْرِ وَهذَا وَقتُهُ وَلَنَا أنَ الْإِضَافَةَ لِلاخْتِصَاصِ وَاخْتِصَاصِ الْفِطْرِ
The time of obligation of sadaqat al-fitr. He said: The obligation of fitrah is tied to the break of dawn on the day of Fitr (Eid). Al-Shafi'i said: at sunset on the last day of Ramadan. So that if someone accepts Islam or is born on the night of Fitr, his fitrah is obligatory according to us, but according to him it is not. And conversely, if someone dies among his slaves or his child? He said that it is specific to Fitr, and this is its time. And our proof is that the attribution is for specificity, and the specificity of Fitr...
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This short passage addresses the time when sadaqat al-fitr becomes wajib. According to the Hanafi school (stated by the author), the obligation is connected to the subh sadiq (true dawn) on the day of Eid al-Fitr. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it becomes wajib at sunset on the last day of Ramadan. The practical consequence is clear: if a person accepts Islam or a baby is born on the night of Eid (after sunset but before fajr), the Hanafi school says fitrah is obligatory because the obligation time (fajr) has not yet passed; the Shafi'i says it is not obligatory because sunset of the last day of Ramadan has passed. Conversely, if a slave owner or a parent dies during that night, the Shafi'i might not require fitrah for his dependents? The text is cut off but indicates the Hanafi response that the attribution (of the obligation) to 'Fitr' (Eid day) shows specificity, meaning the obligation relates to the day of Fitr itself, so fajr is the correct trigger. This is a standard inter-madhhab dispute on the exact moment of obligation.

Key Terms
الفطرة (al-fiṭra): Sadaqat al-fitr, the obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan.
وجوب (wujūb): Legal obligation; here it means the time when the obligation becomes incumbent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) At midday on Eid
D) At the time of the Eid prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sadaqat al-fitr becomes wajib at Fajr of Eid day, not at sunset of the last day of Ramadan, and this affects cases of conversion, birth, and death on the night of Eid.

Weight and Measurement of the Sa'
Establishes the weight of the Sa' using hadith and calculations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Sa' as 8 ratls, identify the hadith proof, and calculate the weight using any of the three methods for Sadaqat al-Fitr.

Core Idea
The Sa' is 8 ratls — the Prophet's practice is the definitive legal measure for Zakat and Sadaqat al-Fitr.

The Sa' is a fundamental volume measure in Hanafi fiqh, used for obligations like Sadaqat al-Fitr and Kaffarah. In this lesson, we examine the primary hadith evidence that establishes its weight as 8 ratls. Additionally, we explore the practical calculations derived by later jurists to determine the exact weight in local units. Understanding this measurement ensures your standing of Zakat obligations is accurate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Determine what the passage is ruling on: the weight of the Sa' as a legal measure. Note that it is a sunnah muakkadah based on the Prophet's action.
2
Examine the hadith proof
Read the hadith from Anas and Jabir. Extract the explicit statement that the Prophet used 8 ratls for ghusl. Understand why this establishes the Sa' as 8 ratls.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi clarification
Consider the narration from Abu Yusuf about the 'smallest Sa''. Understand that it distinguishes the 8-ratl Sa' from the larger Hashimi Sa' (32 ratls).
This shows the Hanafi preference for the Iraqi Sa'.
4
Learn the three calculation methods
Review the three methods: by mithqal, dirham, and mudd. Note the resulting weights in tolas, seers, etc.
Each method gives a slightly different weight; all are valid.
5
Apply the precautionary method
Identify which method is most precautionary (the mudd-based one) and understand why it is recommended for Sadaqat al-Fitr.
Precaution ensures the obligation is definitely fulfilled.

Source Text

ہماری دلیل حضرت انس اور حضرت جابر رضی اللہ تعالی عنہا کی یہ روایت ہے اُنَّه عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسَّلَامُ كَانَ يَتَوَضَّأَ بِالْمَةٍ رطلَيْن وَيَغْتَسِلُ بِالصَّاعِ ثَمَانِيَةَ أَرْطَال يعنى رسول ہاشمی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ایک مد یعنی دور طل پانی سے وضو کیا کرتے تھے اور ایک صاع یعنی آٹھ رطل پانی سے غسل کیا کرتے تھے اور ایسا ہی حضرت عمر کا صاع تھا بہر حال اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صاع آٹھہ طل کا ہوتا ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کی طرف سے پیش کردہ روایت صاعُنَا أَصْغَرَ الصَّيْعَانِ میں اصف صاع سے مراد یہ ہے کہ آٹھ طل والا صاع ہاشمی صاع سے چھوٹا ہے کیونکہ ہاشمی صاع بتیس رطل کا ہوتا تھا اور لوگ اس کو استعمال کرتے تھے جبکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم عراقی صاع ( جس میں آٹھ رطل ہوتے ہیں ) استعمال فرماتے تھے تو ہاشمی صاع کے مقابلہ میں کہا گیا کہ صَاعُنَا أَصَغَرُ الصّيعَان فوائد صاع کا وزن معلوم کرنے کے تین طریقے ہیں: (۱) صاع کا وزن بحساب مثقال ایک مثقال چار ماشہ چار رتی کا ہوتا ہے مشتقال کے حساب سے صاع کا وزن تین ہزار دو سو چالیس ماشے بنتا ہے یعنی دوسوستر تو لہ اس حساب سے تین سیر چھ چھٹانک کا پورا صاع ہوا اور ڈیڑھ سیر تین چھٹا تک کا نصف صاع ہوا۔ (۲) درہم کے اعتبار سے ایک درہم تین ماشہ ایک رتی اور ایک بٹہ پانچ ( لٹھ ) رتی کا ہوتا ہے اس حساب سے ایک صاع دو سو تہتر تولے کا ہوگا۔ اور نصف صاع ایک سو چھتیس تولے چھ ماشے کا ہوتا ہے گو یا انگریزی سیر کے حساب سے پورا صاع تین سیر چھ چھٹا تک تین تولے کے برابر ہوتا ہے اور نصف صاع ڈیڑھ سیر تین چھٹا تک ڈیڑھ تو لے کے برابر ہے۔ (۳) مد کے اعتبار سے ایک مدار سٹھ تولہ تین ماشہ کا ہوتا ہے اس حساب سے ایک صاع دو سو اسی تو لے کچھ ماشہ کا بنتا ہے اور نصف صاع ایک سو چالیس تولے تین ماشے کا ہوتا ہے گویا پورا صاع ساڑھے تین سیر چھ ماشہ کا ہوا اور نصف صاع پونے دوسیر تین ماشہ کا واضح رہے کہ ایک صاع چار مد کا ہوتا ہے۔ ( درس ترندی جلد ۱ (۳۹۵) صاع کا وزن معلوم کرنے کے جو تین طریقے لکھے گئے ہیں ان میں سے جس طریقہ اور حساب کو بھی اختیار کر لیا جائے صدقۃ الفطر ادا ہو جائے گا لیکن چونکہ آخری حساب میں زیادتی ہے اس لئے اس کے مطابق ادا کرنے میں زیادہ احتیاط ہے یعنی پونے دوسیر تین ماشہ گندم یا ساڑھے تین سیر چھ ماشہ جو غیر ہ فطرہ میں ادا کیا جائے۔ جمیل احمد
Our proof is the narration of Anas and Jabir, may Allah be pleased with them, that the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) used to perform ablution with one mudd (two ratls) and perform ghusl with one sa' (eight ratls). This hadith indicates that the sa' is eight ratls. The narration from Abu Yusuf, 'our sa' is the smallest of the sa's,' means that the eight-ratl sa' is smaller than the Hashimi sa' (thirty-two ratls). The people used the Hashimi sa', while the Prophet used the Iraqi sa' (eight ratls). Benefits: There are three methods to determine the weight of the sa': (1) By mithqal: one mithqal is 4 mashas and 4 rattis; thus one sa' is 3240 mashas, i.e., 200 tolas; full sa' is 3 seers 6 chhataks; half sa' is 1.5 seers 3 chhataks. (2) By dirham: one dirham is 3 mashas 1 rati and 5/6 rati; one sa' is 273 tolas; half is 136 tolas 6 mashas. In English seer, full sa' equals 3 seers 6 chhataks 3 tolas; half sa' equals 1.5 seers 3 chhataks 1.5 tolas. (3) By mudd: one mudd is 60 tolas 3 mashas; one sa' is 280 tolas and some mashas; half is 140 tolas 3 mashas; full sa' is 3.5 seers 6 mashas; half is 1.75 seers 3 mashas. Note: one sa' is 4 mudds. (Durr-e-Mukhtar vol.1 p.395) Whichever method is chosen, the sadaqat al-fitr will be valid, but the last calculation gives more weight, so it is more precautionary: i.e., give 1.75 seers 3 mashas of wheat or 3.5 seers 6 mashas of other grains.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the measurement of the Sa', a key unit for Zakat and Sadaqat al-Fitr. The author begins by citing a hadith from Anas and Jabir, which the Hanafi school uses to prove that the Prophet's sa' was 8 ratls. This is the standard for the Iraqi sa' used in Iraq and the Hijaz. The narration from Abu Yusuf clarifies that this sa' is smaller than the larger Hashimi sa' (32 ratls) used by some people. The section then provides three practical methods for calculating the weight of the sa' in local units: by mithqal, dirham, and mudd. These are based on later Hanafi jurists' calculations (Durr-e-Mukhtar). The author concludes that any of these methods suffices for Sadaqat al-Fitr, but the last method (by mudd) is more precautionary due to its higher weight, ensuring obligation is fulfilled without doubt.

Key Terms
صاع (Sa'): A volume measure equal to 4 mudds, equivalent to 8 ratls (approx. 2.5 kg of wheat).
مد (Mudd): A volume measure equal to 2 ratls, used for wudu and as one-fourth of a sa'.
رطل (Ratl): A weight measure (approx. 406.25 g). The sa' is 8 ratls.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 4 ratls
B) 8 ratls
C) 12 ratls
D) 32 ratls

Key Takeaway
The Sa' is definitively 8 ratls by the Prophet's practice; all three calculation methods yield valid weights, but the mudd-based method is most precautionary.

The Time of Obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on the time of obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using linguistic reasoning.

Core Idea
The obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr begins at dawn of Eid, not sunset, because 'fitr' means the day of breaking fast.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute concerning the precise moment when Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes wajib. The Hanafi school ties it to the dawn of Eid day, while the Shafi'i school ties it to sunset of the last day of Ramadan. The disagreement has practical consequences for who is liable. Let us examine the proofs and the logical reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its practical ruling
State clearly what the Hanafi school holds: that Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory at the dawn (Fajr) of the day of Eid al-Fitr.
This is the mufta bihi position in the school.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its practical ruling
State the Shafi'i view: the obligation begins at sunset of the last day of Ramadan.
The Shafi'i school relies on a different interpretation of 'fitr'.
3
Examine the Hanafi linguistic proof
Understand the argument from idafa: 'sadaqat al-fitr' means the charity of the day of Fitr. 'Fitr' is the opposite of fasting, and fasting is by day, so fitr is also by day.
The day begins at dawn, not sunset.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Review the Shafi'i proof: the hadith of Ibn Umar and the interpretation of 'fitr' as the act of breaking fast, which begins at sunset.
This leads to a different time of obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Work through the practical examples: conversion, birth, and death on the night of Eid. Conclude which position is relied upon in the Hanafi madhhab and why.
The Hanafi tarjih is based on the linguistic specificity of idafah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَوُجُوبُ الفِطْرَةِ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ مِن يَوْمِ الْفِطْرِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ بِعُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ فِى الْيَوْم الأخير مِنْ رَمَضَانَ حَتَّى إِنَّ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ أوْ وُلِدَ لَيْلَةَ الْفِطْر تَجِبُ فِطْرَتُهُ عِندَنَا وَ عِندَهُ لا تَجِبُ وَ عَلَى عَكْسِه مَنْ مَاتَ فِيهَا مِن مَّمَالِيْكه أو وَلَدِهِ لَهُ أَنَّهُ يَخْتَصُّ بِالْفِطْرِ وَهذَا وَقتُهُ وَلَنَا أنَ الْإِضَافَةَ لِلاخْتِصَاصِ وَاخْتِصَاصِ الْفِطْرِ بِالْيَوْمِ دُونَ اللَّيْلِ تشریح ... ہمارے نزدیک عید الفطر کی صبح صادق سے صدقۃ الفطر کا ادا کرنا واجب ہو جاتا ہے یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ رمضان کے آخری دن آفتاب غروب ہونے کے بعد سے ادا کرنا واجب ہوگا حاصل یہ کہ چاند رات میں شوافع کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر کے وجوب ادا کا وقت غروب آفتاب سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک صبح صادق طلوع ہونے پر شروع ہوگا۔ اختلاف کا ثمرہ اس سے ظاہر ہوگا کہ چاند رات میں صبح صادق سے پہلے اگر کا فرمسلمان ہو گیا یا بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فطرہ واجب ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر چاند رات میں صبح صادق سے پہلے کسی کا کوئی غلام مر گیا یا اس کا بچہ مر گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فطرہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وقت ادا شروع ہونے سے پہلے مر گیا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک وقت ادا شروع ہونے کے بعد مرا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب فطر کے ساتھ مختص ہے کیونکہ ابن عمرؓ نے فرمایا ہے فرض رسول اللہ صلی اللہ عليه وسلم زكوة الفطر اور فطر یعنی افطار کا وقت غروب سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب ادار مضان کے آخری دن کے غروب کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ کہے صدقۃ الفطر میں صدقہ کی اضافت فطر کی طرف اختصاص کے لئے ہے یعنی صدقہ فطر کے ساتھ مختص ہے اور فطر سے مراد صوم کی ضد ہے اور صوم کا تعلق دن سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ رات سے الہذا فطر کا تعلق بھی دن سے ہوگا نہ کہ رات سے اور یہ معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ صدقہ فطر کیسا تھ مخصوص ہے اور فطر سے مراد دن ہے لہذا صدقہ دن کے ساتھ مختص دن صبح صادق سے شروع ہوتا ہے اس لئے صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب ادا چاند رات کی صبح صادق کے ساتھ متعلق ہو گا۔
He said: The obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is connected to the dawn of the day of Fitr. Al-Shafi'i said: It is connected to the sunset of the last day of Ramadan. Thus, whoever embraces Islam or is born on the night of Fitr, his Sadaqat al-Fitr is obligatory according to us, but not according to him. The opposite applies to one whose slave or child dies on that night: according to him it is obligatory, according to us it is not. His (Shafi'i's) proof is that it is dedicated to Fitr, and the time of Fitr (breaking fast) begins at sunset. Our proof is that the addition (idafah) of sadaqah to fitr implies specification, and fitr means the opposite of fasting, which is connected to the day, not the night. Therefore, Sadaqat al-Fitr is connected to the day, which begins at dawn. Commentary: According to us, the obligation starts at true dawn (subh sadiq) on Eid day; this is also the view of Malik. According to Shafi'i, it starts after sunset on the last day of Ramadan. The practical consequence: If a person becomes Muslim or a child is born on the night of Eid before dawn, we say it is obligatory; Shafi'i says no. If a slave or child dies before dawn, we say it is not obligatory; Shafi'i says it is obligatory (because for him the time had started). Shafi'i's evidence: Ibn Umar said the Prophet made Zakat al-Fitr obligatory, and fitr begins at sunset. Our evidence: The word 'fitr' in 'sadaqat al-fitr' indicates it is specific to the day, not the night; the day begins at dawn.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the exact moment when Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory. The matn (original text) states the Hanafi position: obligation is tied to the dawn of Eid day. The Shafi'i position is tied to sunset of the last day of Ramadan. The author then explains the practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf): a person who accepts Islam or a child born on the night of Eid before dawn owes Sadaqat al-Fitr according to the Hanafis (since the obligation time has not yet started for them? Wait careful: The text says 'عندنا تجب' for one who becomes Muslim on that night; that is because for Hanafis the time of obligation starts at Fajr, so after Fajr it becomes wajib. But the example given is before Fajr? Actually: 'من أسلم أو ولد ليلة الفطر' - on the night of Fitr, before Fajr. For Shafi'i, the time starts at sunset, so by that night it's already time, so it would be wajib? The text says opposite: 'عندنا تجب و عنده لا تجب' because for Shafi'i the time hasn't started? Let me re-read: 'حَتَّى إِنَّ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ أوْ وُلِدَ لَيْلَةَ الْفِطْر تَجِبُ فِطْرَتُهُ عِندَنَا وَ عِندَهُ لا تَجِبُ وَ عَلَى عَكْسِه مَنْ مَاتَ فِيهَا مِن مَّمَالِيْكه أو وَلَدِهِ'. This is the standard rule: For a person who enters Islam or a child born on the night of Eid, the Hanafi say it is wajib because the time of obligation (Fajr) is still in the future; but for Shafi'i, the time started at sunset of the previous day, so the person was not Muslim/alive at that time, so no obligation. Conversely, for a slave or child who dies on that night, Hanafi says not wajib (because they died before Fajr), Shafi'i says wajib (because they were alive when the time began at sunset). So the roles are reversed. The author then explains the reasoning: Shafi'i ties fitr to breaking the fast (iftar) which begins at sunset; Hanafi ties fitr to the day of Eid itself, arguing that 'fitr' means the opposite of fasting, and fasting is done during the day, so fitr pertains to the day, which starts at dawn.

Key Terms
فطرہ (Fitra): Sadaqat al-Fitr, the obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan.
اضافت (Idafah): Grammatical construct (idafa) in 'sadaqat al-fitr' which implies specification of the charity to the day of Fitr.
فِطر (Fitr): The day of breaking the fast, i.e., Eid al-Fitr; also the act of breaking fast (iftar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, at what moment does Sadaqat al-Fitr become obligatory?
A) At sunset on the last day of Ramadan
B) At dawn (Fajr) on the day of Eid
C) At the time of Eid prayer
D) At the sighting of the new moon of Shawwal

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory at dawn of Eid day according to the Hanafi school, based on the construct 'sadaqat al-fitr' specifying the day of Fitr.

Mustahabb Time for Sadaqat al-Fitr
States the preferred time to give Sadaqat al-Fitr before Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mustahabb time for giving Sadaqat al-Fitr and explain the rationale behind it.

Core Idea
The best time to give Sadaqat al-Fitr is before the Eid prayer, following the Prophet's practice and to enable the poor to pray without distraction.

This passage from Al-Hidayah teaches us the preferred timing for fulfilling the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr. While the obligation can be fulfilled anytime before the Eid prayer, the Prophet's example and the underlying purpose guide us to give early. Understanding this ruling deepens our appreciation of the wisdom behind the acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Sadaqat al-Fitr. What is the ruling? Mustahabb (recommended) to give before the Eid prayer.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Prophet's practice: he used to give before going out to the musalla.
The hadith of Ibn Umar is referenced.
3
Understand the wisdom
The command to make the poor self-sufficient (ighna') so they are not distracted from prayer by begging. This wisdom is achieved by giving early.
4
Distinguish from obligation
Giving after the prayer is still valid, but the mustahabb time is before.
Mustahabb does not mean obligatory.

وَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ أنْ يُخْرِجَ النَّاسُ الْفِطْرَةَ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ قَبْلَ الْخُرُوجِ إِلَى الْمُصْلى لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَانَ يُخْرِجُ قَبْلَ أن يَخْرجَ وَلِأَنَّ الأَمَرَ بِالْإِغْنَاء كَى لَا يَتَشَاعَلُ الْفَقِيرِ بِالْمَسْأَلَةِ عَنِ الصَّلوةِ وَ ذُلِكَ بِالتَّقْدِيم ترجمہ اور مستحب یہ ہے کہ لوگ عید الفطر کے دن عید گاہ کی طرف نکلنے سے پہلے فطرہ ادا کر دیں کیونکہ حضور نکلنے سے پہلے نکال دیا کرتے تھے اور اس لئے کہ مستغنی کر دینے کا حکم اس مقصد سے ہے کہ فقیر سوال کرنے کی وجہ سے نماز سے مشغول نہ ہو جائے اور یہ مقصد صدقہ کو پہلے دینے سے حاصل ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنے میں مستحب عمل یہ ہے کہ لوگ عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے ادا کریں ۔ دلیل حدیث ابن عمر ہے حدیث یہ
It is mustahabb for people to give the Sadaqat al-Fitr on the day of Fitr before going out to the musalla (prayer ground), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to give it before going out, and because the command to make the poor independent (of asking) is so that the poor are not distracted from prayer by begging, and that is achieved by giving early. Translation: It is recommended that people give the Fitra on Eid day before leaving for the Eid prayer, because the Prophet used to give it before leaving, and because the purpose of making the self-sufficient is that the poor should not be occupied with asking and miss the prayer, and this purpose is achieved by giving early. Commentary: The recommended action in giving Sadaqat al-Fitr is that people should give it before going to the Eid prayer. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar: ...
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a ruling stating the mustahabb (recommended) time for giving Sadaqat al-Fitr. The matn clearly states that it is mustahabb to give on the day of Eid before heading to the prayer ground. Two proofs are offered: (1) the Prophet's practice – he used to give before going out; (2) the purpose of the obligation is to make the poor self-sufficient so they do not need to beg during the Eid prayer. This purpose is best achieved by giving earlier, allowing the poor to have the money before the prayer. The commentary adds that the hadith of Ibn Umar supports this. Note that this preferred time does not affect the validity; giving after the prayer is also valid but less reward.

Key Terms
مستحب (Mustahabb): Recommended act; rewarded but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the mustahabb time to give Sadaqat al-Fitr according to the Hanafi school?
A) After the Eid prayer
B) Before going to the Eid prayer ground
C) During the last ten days of Ramadan
D) At sunset on the night of Eid

Key Takeaway
The mustahabb time to give Sadaqat al-Fitr is before the Eid prayer, based on the Prophet's practice and the wisdom of enabling the poor to pray.

Time of Obligation for Sadaqat al-Fitr: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on time of Sadaqat al-Fitr obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the time of obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the linguistic principle of idafat al-ikhtisas.

Core Idea
The obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr begins at dawn of Eid, not sunset, because 'fir' refers to the day.

This lesson examines a classical inter-madhhab dispute: when exactly does the obligation to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr (fitrah) take effect? The Hanafi school, relying on linguistic analysis, places it at the dawn of Eid al-Fitr, while the Shafi'i school, relying on a hadith, places it at sunset of the last day of Ramadan. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to evaluate proofs in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact moment the Hanafi school claims Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory: the true dawn (fajr sadiq) of Eid al-Fitr.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
State Imam al-Shafi'i's view: obligation attaches to sunset of the last day of Ramadan. Examine his proof: the hadith of Ibn Umar and the literal meaning of 'fir' (breaking fast) occurring at sunset.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi refutation: the idafah (genitive construction) in 'Sadaqat al-Fitr' indicates ikhtisas (specific association) with 'fir', which is the opposite of 'sawm'. Since sawm is associated with day, 'fir' must also refer to day, not night. Thus, obligation begins at dawn.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Apply the two positions to real scenarios: conversion/birth during the night of Eid before dawn, or death of a slave/child during that night. See how the ruling differs.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Note that the Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school, and understand why the linguistic argument is considered stronger.

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ فطرہ کا وجوب عید الفطر کی طلوع فجر کی ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ رمضان کے آخری دن کے غروب آفتاب کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے حتی کہ جو شخص اسلام لایا یا پیدا ہوا عید الفطر کی رات میں ہمارے نزدیک اس پر فطرہ واجب ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک واجب نہیں ہوگا اور اس کے برعکس حکم ہے جو شخص اس کے مملوکوں یا اس کی اولاد میں سے اس رات میں مر گیا امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب فطر کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے اور فطر کا وقت یہی ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اضافت اختصاص کے لئے ہے اور فطر کا اختصاص یوم کے ساتھ ہے نہ کہ رات کے ساتھ۔ تشریح ... ہمارے نزدیک عید الفطر کی صبح صادق سے صدقۃ الفطر کا ادا کرنا واجب ہو جاتا ہے یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ رمضان کے آخری دن آفتاب غروب ہونے کے بعد سے ادا کرنا واجب ہوگا حاصل یہ کہ چاند رات میں شوافع کے نزدیک صدقۃ الفطر کے وجوب ادا کا وقت غروب آفتاب سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک صبح صادق طلوع ہونے پر شروع ہوگا۔ اختلاف کا ثمرہ اس سے ظاہر ہوگا کہ چاند رات میں صبح صادق سے پہلے اگر کافر مسلمان ہو گیا یا بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فطرہ واجب ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر چاند رات میں صبح صادق سے پہلے کسی کا کوئی غلام مر گیا یا اس کا بچہ مر گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فطرہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وقت ادا شروع ہونے سے پہلے مر گیا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک وقت ادا شروع ہونے کے بعد مرا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب فطر کے ساتھ مختص ہے کیونکہ ابن عمرؓ نے فرمایا ہے فرض رسول اللہ صلی اللہ عليه وسلم زكوة الفطر اور فطر یعنی افطار کا وقت غروب سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب ادار مضان کے آخری دن کے غروب کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ کہے صدقۃ الفطر میں صدقہ کی اضافت فطر کی طرف اختصاص کے لئے ہے یعنی صدقہ فطر کے ساتھ مختص ہے اور فطر سے مراد صوم کی ضد ہے اور صوم کا تعلق دن سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ رات سے اللہذا فطر کا تعلق بھی دن سے ہوگا نہ کہ رات سے اور یہ معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ صدقہ فطر کیسا تھ مخصوص ہے اور فطر سے مراد دن ہے لہذا صدقہ دن کے ساتھ مختص دن صبح صادق سے شروع ہوتا ہے اس لئے صدقۃ الفطر کا وجوب ادا چاند رات کی صبح صادق کے ساتھ متعلق ہو گا۔
Translation: Quduri said: The obligation of fitrah is attached to the dawn of Eid al-Fitr. Imam Shafi'i said: It is attached to the sunset of the last day of Ramadan. So if a person converts to Islam or is born on the night of Eid, according to us fitrah is obligatory, but according to Shafi'i it is not. And the opposite ruling applies if a person among his slaves or children dies that night. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is specific to 'fir' (breaking fast) and the time of fir is this (sunset). Our proof is that the idafah (genitive construction) is for ikhtisas (specific association), and fir is specifically associated with day, not night. Explanation: ... According to us, it becomes obligatory to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr from the true dawn of Eid day. This is also the view of Imam Malik. Imam Shafi'i says it becomes obligatory from sunset of the last day of Ramadan. So on the night of Eid, for Shafi'is the time of obligation begins at sunset; for us it begins at dawn. The practical consequence: If on the night of Eid before dawn a disbeliever accepts Islam or a child is born, according to us fitrah is obligatory; according to Shafi'i it is not. If a slave or child of someone dies before dawn that night, according to us fitrah is not obligatory (since the time of performance had not started); according to Shafi'i it is obligatory (since their time starts at sunset). Imam Shafi'i's proof: The obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is specific to 'fir' because Ibn Umar said: 'The Messenger of Allah made Zakat al-Fitr obligatory' and fir (breaking fast) begins at sunset. So it is said the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is attached to the sunset of the last day. Our proof: The idafah of sadaqah to fir is for ikhtisas, i.e., sadaqah is specific to fir. And fir is the opposite of sawm (fasting). Sawm is associated with day, not night; therefore fir is also associated with day, not night. It is known that sadaqah is specific to fir, and fir means day. So sadaqah is specific to day, and day begins at true dawn; therefore the obligation of paying Sadaqat al-Fitr is attached to the dawn of the night of Eid.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute regarding the exact moment when Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory. According to the Hanafi school (following Imam Abu Hanifa and also Imam Malik), the obligation is tied to the true dawn (fajr sadiq) of the day of Eid al-Fitr. Imam Shafi'i, however, links the obligation to the sunset (maghrib) of the last day of Ramadan. The practical consequence (thamarat al-khilaf) is illustrated by two scenarios: (1) If a person accepts Islam or a child is born during the night of Eid before dawn, Hanafis consider fitrah obligatory (because the time of obligation has started at dawn, and they are alive at that moment), while Shafi'is do not (because their time of obligation began at the previous sunset before they existed). (2) If a slave or child dies during the night of Eid before dawn, Hanafis do not consider fitrah obligatory for the deceased (since the obligation had not yet arisen), while Shafi'is do (since it arose at sunset before death). The Shafi'i proof relies on the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (PBUH) prescribed 'Zakat al-Fitr', interpreting 'fir' as the breaking of the fast which occurs at sunset. The Hanafi proof counters by analyzing the linguistic construction: 'Sadaqat al-Fitr' uses an idafa (genitive) that indicates ikhtisas (exclusive association). The term 'fir' here means the opposite of 'sawm', and sawm pertains specifically to the daytime, not the night. Therefore, 'fir' refers to the day, which begins at dawn, not the night. Thus, the obligation is connected to the dawn of Eid day.

Key Terms
فطرہ (fitrah): The alms given at the end of Ramadan, also called Sadaqat al-Fitr.
اضافت اختصاص (idafat al-ikhtisas): A genitive construction (idafa) that indicates exclusive association or specification.
فطر (fiṭr): Breaking the fast; the opposite of sawm. Here interpreted as the day because sawm is daytime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does Sadaqat al-Fitr become obligatory?
A) At sunset of the last day of Ramadan
B) At the true dawn of Eid al-Fitr
C) At the time of the Eid prayer
D) At the sighting of the Eid moon

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the linguistic principle of idafat al-ikhtisas to place the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr at dawn of Eid, not sunset.

Mustahabb Time and Permissibility of Early Payment of Sadaqat al-Fitr
Rulings on the best time and early payment of Sadaqat al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for giving Sadaqat al-Fitr and explain why early payment is permissible according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Give fitr on Eid morning before prayer; paying earlier is permissible anytime after the cause exists.

The timing of Sadaqat al-Fitr involves two distinct rulings: the mustahabb (recommended) time and the permissibility of paying before Eid day. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the underlying purpose, then addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about how early one may pay. Understanding these rulings helps ensure the act is performed optimally and validly.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two issues
First, separate the mustahabb timing (Eid day before prayer) from the permissibility of paying early (before Eid day). The text begins with the mustahabb, then moves to the ruling on taqdeem.
These are separate: one is recommended, the other merely permissible.
2
Extract evidence for the mustahabb time
Identify the hadith of Ibn Umar and the hikmah (making the poor independent) used to support giving on Eid morning before prayer. Note the wording: 'He used to command us...'.
The hadith is ahad but sufficient for mustahabb.
3
Analyze the qiyas for early payment
The text analogizes early fitr to ta'jil al-zakat (paying zakat before the year ends). The cause (sabab) – existence of the person for whom fitrah is due – is already present. Thus, payment is valid after the cause is established.
Compare to udhiyyah, where the cause is the day itself, so early payment is invalid.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and identify the mufta bihi
Several earlier scholars restricted early payment to various periods. The text declares the correct view (al-sahih) to be unrestricted permissibility, supported by the practice of the Companions and the principle of qiyas.
The mufta bihi is the unrestricted view.

مستحب وقت
وَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ أنْ يُخْرِجَ النَّاسُ الْفِطْرَةَ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ قَبْلَ الْخُرُوجِ إِلَى الْمُصْلى لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَانَ يُخْرِجُ قَبْلَ أن يَخْرجَ وَلِأَنَّ الأَمَرَ بِالْإِغْنَاء كَى لَا يَتَشَاعَلُ الْفَقِيرِ بِالْمَسْأَلَةِ عَنِ الصَّلوةِ وَ ذُلِكَ بِالتَّقْدِيم ترجمہ اور مستحب یہ ہے کہ لوگ عید الفطر کے دن عید گاہ کی طرف نکلنے سے پہلے فطرہ ادا کر دیں کیونکہ حضور نکلنے سے پہلے نکال دیا کرتے تھے اور اس لئے کہ مستغنی کر دینے کا حکم اس مقصد سے ہے کہ فقیر سوال کرنے کی وجہ سے نماز سے مشغول نہ ہو جائے اور یہ مقصد صدقہ کو پہلے دینے سے حاصل ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرنے میں مستحب عمل یہ ہے کہ لوگ عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے ادا کریں ۔ دلیل حدیث ابن عمر ہے حدیث یہ  كَان يَأْمُرُنَا أَنْ نُخْرِجَهَا قَبْلَ الصَّلوةِ وَكَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يُقسِمُهَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يُنْصَرِفَ إِلَى المُصلى وَيَقُولُ اغْنُوهُمْ عَنِ الطَّوَافِ فِى هذا اليوم، یعنی رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہم کو حکم فرماتے تھے کہ ہم نماز عید سے پہلے پہلے صدقہ ادا کر دیں۔ اور خود آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے پہلے صدقہ تقسیم فرمادیا کرتے تھے اور فرماتے کہ فقراء کو اس دن در در پھرنی سے بے نیاز کرد و یعنی بغیر مانگے نماز سے پہلے ہی ان کو صدقہ دیدو۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فقراء کومستغنی کر دینے کا حکم اس مقصد کے لئے ہے کہ وہ بھیک مانگنے کی وجہ سے نماز عید سے نہ رہ جائیں ۔ اور یہ مقصد اسی صورت میں پورا ہو گا جبکہ صدقہ نماز سے پہلے دیدیا جائے ۔ اسی وجہ سے تقدیم کو مستحب اور مندوب قرار دیا گیا۔ صدقہ فطر کو وقت پر مقدم کرنے کا حکم
فَإِنْ قَدِّمُوهَا عَلَى يَوْمِ الْفِطْرِ جَازَ لِأَنَّهُ أَدَى بَعْدَ تَقَرُّرِ السَّبَبِ فَاشْبَهَ التَّعْجِيلَ فِي الزَّكَوةِ وَ لَا تَفْصِيل بَيْنَ مُدَّةٍ وَ مُدَّة هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ
ترجمہ اور اگر لوگوں نے صدقۃ الفطر کو عید کے دن پر مقدم کر دیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ سبب ثابت ہونے کے بعد ادا کیا ہے پس پیشگی زکوۃ ادا کرنے کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ایک مدت اور دوسری مدت کے درمیان کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عید کے دن سے پہلے صدقہ ادا کر دیا تو جائز ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کے سبب کے متحقق ہونے کے بعد ادا کیا ہے اور سبب وہ راس ہے جس کی مونت برداشت کرتا ہے اور اس پر ولایت حاصل ہے پس جب سبب متحقق ہونے کے بعد ادا کیا تو ادا ہو جائے گا اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے حولان حول سے پہلے پیشگی زکوۃ دیدی جائے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ نصاب جو سبب ہے وہ پایا گیا اور ابن عمر کی حدیث میں ہے وَكَانُوا يُعْطُونَ قَبْلَ الْفِطْرِ بَيوم أو يَوْمَيِّنِ یعنی صحابہ عید الفطر سے ایک دن یا دو دن پہلے فطر و دید یا کرتے تھے اور اس کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں کہ کتنی مدت پہلے صدقہ دینا جائز ہے اور کتنی مدت پہلے جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ مطلقاً پیشگی دینا جائز ہی اور یہی صحیح قول ہے اگر چہ حسن بن زیاد کہتے ہیں کہ پیشگی صدقۃ الفطر کا دینا قطعا جائز نہیں ہے جیسے قربانی کا ایام الضحیہ پر مقدم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور خلف ابن ایوب کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان شروع ہونے کے بعد عید پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے لیکن رمضان سے پہلے دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نوح بن ابی مریم کہتے ہیں کہ نصف رمضان کے بعد مقعد دینا جائز ہے اس سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے اور بعض کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان کے آخری عشرہ میں دینا جائز ہے اس سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے۔ (عنایہ )
The mustahabb time: And it is mustahabb for people to give the fitrah on the day of Eid before going out to the musalla because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to give it before going out, and because the command to make the poor independent is so that the poor person is not distracted from the prayer by begging, and that is achieved by giving in advance. Translation: And it is mustahabb for people to give the fitrah on the day of Eid before going to the Eid prayer because the Prophet used to give it before going out, and because the purpose of making them independent is that the poor person is not engaged in begging and thus miss the prayer, and this purpose is achieved by giving earlier. Explanation: The mustahabb act in giving Sadaqat al-Fitr is that people give it before going to the Eid prayer. Evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'He used to command us to give it before the prayer, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to distribute it before going to the musalla, and he would say: Make them independent of going around on this day.' That is, the Prophet would command us to give sadaqah before the Eid prayer, and he himself would distribute it before going to the Eid prayer, saying: Make the poor independent of begging on this day. A second evidence is that the command to make them independent is so that they are not occupied with begging and thus miss the Eid prayer, and this purpose is only fulfilled if sadaqah is given before the prayer. Hence, giving in advance is considered mustahabb and recommended. The ruling on giving fitr in advance of its time: If they give it before the day of Eid, it is permissible because one pays after the cause is established, and it resembles hastening in zakat. And there is no distinction between one period and another; this is the correct view. Translation: And if people give Sadaqat al-Fitr before the day of Eid, it is permissible because it is paid after the cause is established, so it resembles hastening in zakat. And there is no detail between one duration and another; this is the correct view. Explanation: If someone gives sadaqah before Eid day, it is permissible. The evidence is that it is paid after the cause of obligation is realized. The cause is the head (ra's) whose maintenance one bears and over whom one has guardianship. So when paid after the cause is realized, it is valid. This is like giving zakat in advance before the year passes: it is valid because the cause (nisab) exists. And in the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'They used to give before Fitr by a day or two days.' Meaning the Companions used to give fitr one or two days before Eid. There is no specification as to how long before it is allowed; rather, giving in advance is absolutely permissible, and this is the correct view. Even though Hasan ibn Ziyad says giving fitr in advance is absolutely not permissible, like advancing the sacrifice before the days of sacrifice. And Khalaf ibn Ayyub says it is permissible to give in advance after Ramadan begins but not before Ramadan. Nuh ibn Abi Maryam says it is permissible after the middle of Ramadan, not before. Some say it is permissible in the last ten days of Ramadan, not before. (Uinayah)
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues regarding the timing of Sadaqat al-Fitr: the mustahabb (recommended) time and the permissibility of paying before Eid day. First, it is mustahabb to give the fitrah on the day of Eid itself before going to the Eid prayer. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (PBUH) as narrated by Ibn Umar, and also on the underlying purpose (hikmah) of making the poor independent so they can attend the Eid prayer without needing to beg. The second issue: it is permissible to give Sadaqat al-Fitr before the day of Eid, once the cause (sabab) of obligation is established. The cause is the existence of the person for whom fitrah is due (oneself, one's dependent, one's slave) and the capacity to provide. This is analogous to giving zakat before the year completes (ta'jil al-zakat) which is valid in the Hanafi school if the nisab exists. The text mentions that the correct view (sahih) is that there is no specific limit; it is permissible absolutely before Eid. However, there are minority opinions: Hasan ibn Ziyad forbids it entirely, comparing it to udhiyyah (sacrifice) which cannot be offered before its time; Khalaf ibn Ayyub allows it only after Ramadan begins; Nuh ibn Abi Maryam allows it only after mid-Ramadan; some restrict it to the last ten days. The relied-upon Hanafi position (as stated in the Uinayah and supported by the practice of the Companions) is that it is permissible without restriction, as long as it is given before Eid.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act that is rewarded but not sinful to omit.
تقدیم (taqdeem): Giving Sadaqat al-Fitr before the day of Eid.
سبب (sabab): The cause or reason for obligation; here it is the existence of a person for whom fitrah is due (e.g., being a free Muslim with means).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence for the mustahabb time of giving fitr before the Eid prayer?
A) Qiyas to zakat
B) The hadith of Ibn Umar and the purpose of making the poor independent
C) The opinion of Hasan ibn Ziyad
D) The general principle of istihsan

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends giving Sadaqat al-Fitr on Eid morning before prayer, but allows it any time before Eid once the cause is established.

Delaying Fitr Beyond Eid Day Does Not Waive It
Ruling that fitr remains obligatory even if delayed past Eid day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delayed fitr and explain why it differs from udhiyyah using the concept of qurbah ma'qulah.

Core Idea
If you delay Sadaqat al-Fitr past Eid, it remains wajib — not waived like the sacrifice.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common concern: what if fitr is not paid on time? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that it remains a debt. The key distinction is that fitr is a rationally understood act of worship (qurbah ma'qulah), unlike the udhiyyah which has a fixed time window.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? What is the hukm level? The passage rules on Sadaqat al-Fitr when delayed beyond Eid day: it is not waived (lam tasqut) and must still be paid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is that the qurbah (nearness to Allah) in this act is 'ma'qul' (rationally understood). This means its benefit (supporting the poor) is perpetual, not tied to a specific moment.
This is a qiyas jaliy with zakat as the asl.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Because the purpose is rationally understood, the time for fulfillment is not restricted to a specific day. The obligation continues until paid.
In contrast, udhiyyah is purely devotional (ta'abbudi) and has a fixed time.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with udhiyyah
Udhiyyah sacrifice has a specific time slot (days of Nahr). If missed, it is not made up; the animal is given as sadaqah instead. Fitr is different.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: fitr must be paid later, udhiyyah is not made up.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
If someone delays fitr, it becomes a debt on them. They must pay it whenever they can, even years later.
This is the mufta bihi position in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ اَخِرُوهَا عَنْ يَوْمِ الْفِطْرِ لَمْ تَسْقُطُ وَكَانَ عَلَيْهِمْ إِخْرَاجُهَا لِأَنَّ وَجَدَ الْقُرْبَةِ فِيهَا مَعْقُولُ فَلَا يَتَقَدَّرُ وَقْتُ الْآدَاءِ فِيهَا بِخِلَافِ الأَضْحِيَّةِ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ
ترجمہ اور اگر لوگوں نے صدقۃ الفطر کو عید کے دن سے مؤخر کر دیا تو ساقط نہ ہوگی بلکہ ان پر اس کا ادا کرنا لازم ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں قربت (اللہ کی نزدیکی) کا حاصل ہونا معقول (عقل سے سمجھا جاتا) ہے لہذا اس کا وقت متعین نہیں ہے برخلاف قربانی کے اور اللہ تعالیٰ زیادہ جانتا ہے۔ تشریح اگر عید کے دن سے پہلے یا عید کے دن صدقہ نہ دیا گیا تو یہ ساقط نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس کا ادا کرنا واجب رہے گا کیونکہ یہ ایک ایسی عبادت ہے جس میں قربت کا پہلو عقل سے سمجھا جاتا ہے (یعنی اس کا تعلق فقراء کی مدد سے ہے) اس لئے اس کا وقت متعین نہیں ہے جیسا کہ زکوٰۃ کا نہیں ہوتا بلکہ جب بھی دیا جائے گا مقصود حاصل ہو جائے گا۔ بخلاف قربانی کے کہ اس کا وقت متعین ہے یعنی ایام نحر میں، اگر ان دنوں میں نہ کی گئی تو قضاء نہیں ہوگی بلکہ اس کا جانور صدقہ کر دیا جائے گا۔
And if they delay it beyond the day of Eid, it does not become waived, and they must still pay it, because the attainment of closeness (qurbah) in it is rationally understood, so its time of performance is not specific, unlike the udhiyyah (sacrifice). And Allah knows best. Translation: And if people delay Sadaqat al-Fitr beyond the day of Eid, it is not waived; rather, they are obligated to pay it, because the attainment of closeness to Allah in it is rationally understood, so its time is not fixed, unlike the udhiyyah. Explanation: If fitr was not given before or on the day of Eid, it does not become waived; it remains obligatory to pay. This is because it is an act of worship whose aspect of closeness is rationally understood (i.e., it relates to helping the poor), so its time is not limited, unlike zakat? Actually the text says it is like zakat? No, it says unlike udhiyyah. The explanation clarifies that if not given on time, it must still be given as a debt. In contrast, the udhiyyah sacrifice has a specific time (the days of Nahr); if missed, it is not made up; the animal is given as sadaqah instead.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when Sadaqat al-Fitr is delayed beyond the day of Eid. The Hanafi position is clear: delaying does not cause the obligation to be waived; one must still pay it later. The reason given is that the attainment of qurbah (nearness to Allah) in this act of worship is 'ma'qul' (rationally understood) – meaning its benefit (supporting the poor) is perpetual and not tied to a specific moment. Therefore, the time for fulfilling it is not strictly limited like the udhiyyah (sacrifice) which has a specific window (the days of Nahr). If someone fails to sacrifice in those days, the obligation is not made up; the animal is simply given as charity. But for fitr, it must be paid eventually. This ruling is also analogous to zakat: if the year passes without paying, it remains a debt. The passage emphasizes that fitr is not nullified by delay; it remains a liability upon the person until paid.

Key Terms
قربت (qurbah): Act of drawing near to Allah; worship with a rational benefit.
تاخیر (ta'khir): Delaying the payment of fitr beyond the day of Eid.
اضحیہ (udhiyyah): The sacrificial animal offered on the days of Nahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if someone delays Sadaqat al-Fitr beyond the day of Eid?
A) It is waived and no longer required
B) It remains obligatory and must be paid later
C) It becomes a recommended act but not obligatory
D) It must be given as udhiyyah instead

Key Takeaway
Delaying Sadaqat al-Fitr does not cancel its obligation; it remains wajib until paid, unlike udhiyyah.

Advancing Sadaqat al-Fitr Before Eid Day
Ruling and proofs for advancing fitrana before Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on advancing Sadaqat al-Fitr before Eid, identify the key proofs (qiyas and hadith), and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement and the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Once the cause for Sadaqat al-Fitr exists, advancing its payment before Eid is absolutely permissible — like paying zakat early.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, we examine the permissibility of paying Sadaqat al-Fitr (Fitrana) before the day of Eid. The author presents the ruling as valid (ja'iz) and supports it with an analogy to zakat and the practice of the Companions. Several opposing opinions within the Hanafi school are discussed, but the relied-upon position (al-sahih) is that advancement is allowed without any time restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is advancing Sadaqat al-Fitr before Eid. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz), provided the cause (sabab) is established.
The cause is the existence of a head that one supports and for which he is responsible.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: (1) Qiyas to zakat: just as zakat may be paid early once nisab is possessed, so may Fitrana be paid early once the cause exists. (2) Hadith of Ibn Umar showing Companions gave a day or two before Eid.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
In qiyas: both are financial obligations where the cause (sabab) triggers the duty; early payment fulfills the duty once the cause is realized. In the hadith: the Companions' practice indicates implicit approval from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Hasan bin Ziyad forbids any advancement. Others allow only after Ramadan begins, after mid-Ramadan, or in the last ten days. The author declares the absolute permission as al-sahih (the correct view).
These are positions from the Nawadir; the Zahir al-Riwayah supports absolute permissibility.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that there is no time limit; as long as the cause is established, Fitrana may be paid well before Eid. This is the majority Hanafi view.
The text says 'la tafsila bayna muddatin wa mudda' — no distinction between any periods.

فَإِنْ قَدِّمُوهَا عَلَى يَوْمِ الْفِطْرِ جَازَ لِأَنَّهُ أَدَى بَعْدَ تَقَرُّرِ السَّبَبِ فَاشْبَهَ التَّعْجِيلَ فِي الزَّكَوةِ وَ لَا تَفْصِيل بَيْنَ مُدَّةٍ وَ مُدَّة هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ ترجمہ اور اگر لوگوں نے صدقۃ الفطر کو عید کے دن پر مقدم کر دیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ سبب ثابت ہونے کے بعد ادا کیا ہے پس پیشگی زکوۃ ادا کرنے کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ایک مدت اور دوسری مدت کے درمیان کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عید کے دن سے پہلے صدقہ ادا کر دیا تو جائز ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہونے کے سبب کے متحقق ہونے کے بعد ادا کیا ہے اور سبب وہ راس ہے جس کی مونت برداشت کرتا ہے اور اس پر ولایت حاصل ہے پس جب سبب متحقق ہونے کے بعد ادا کیا تو ادا ہو جائے گا اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے حولان حول سے پہلے پیشگی زکوۃ دیدی جائے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ نصاب جو سبب ہے وہ پایا گیا اور ابن عمر کی حدیث میں ہے وَكَانُوا يُعْطُونَ قَبْلَ الْفِطْرِ بِيَوْمٍ أَوْ يَوْمَيْنِ یعنی صحابہ عید الفطر سے ایک دن یا دو دن پہلے فطرہ دیا کرتے تھے اور اس کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں کہ کتنی مدت پہلے صدقہ دینا جائز ہے اور کتنی مدت پہلے جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ مطلقاً پیشگی دینا جائز ہے اور یہی صحیح قول ہے اگر چہ حسن بن زیاد کہتے ہیں کہ پیشگی صدقۃ الفطر کا دینا قطعا جائز نہیں ہے جیسے قربانی کا ایام الضحیہ پر مقدم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور خلف ابن ایوب کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان شروع ہونے کے بعد عید پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے لیکن رمضان سے پہلے دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نوح بن ابی مریم کہتے ہیں کہ نصف رمضان کے بعد مقدم دینا جائز ہے اس سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے اور بعض کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان کے آخری عشرہ میں دینا جائز ہے اس سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے۔ (عنایہ)
If they advance it before the day of Fitr, it is permissible, because he performed it after the cause was established, so it resembles hastening in zakat. There is no distinction between one period and another; that is correct. Translation: And if people advance Sadaqat al-Fitr before the day of Eid, it is permissible, because it is performed after the cause is established, so it resembles paying zakat in advance. There is no distinction between one period and another; that is correct. Explanation: The issue is that if someone pays the sadaqah before the day of Eid, it is permissible. The evidence is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is paid after the cause of obligation is realized. The cause is the head that one supports and over which one has guardianship. So when it is paid after the cause is realized, it is valid. It is like giving zakat in advance before the passing of a year, because the nisab, which is the cause, exists. And in the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'They used to give it a day or two before Fitr.' That is, the Companions used to give Fitrana a day or two before Eid al-Fitr. There is no specification of how long before it is permissible; rather, it is absolutely permissible to give in advance, and this is the correct statement. Although Hasan bin Ziyad says that giving Sadaqat al-Fitr in advance is absolutely impermissible, like advancing the sacrifice before the days of Adha. And Khalaf bin Ayyub says that advancing it after Ramadan begins is permissible, but before Ramadan it is not permissible. Nuh bin Abi Maryam says that advancing it after the middle of Ramadan is permissible, before that it is not. Some say that giving it in the last ten days of Ramadan is permissible, before that it is not. (Inayah)
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs on the permissibility of paying Sadaqat al-Fitr before the day of Eid. The author states that it is permissible to advance payment because the cause of obligation—ownership of a head that one supports—has been established. This is analogous to paying zakat before the end of the year once the nisab is possessed. The text then cites the practice of the Companions (via Ibn Umar) who would give a day or two before Eid, indicating no strict time limit. Several intra-Hanafi opinions are mentioned: Hasan bin Ziyad forbids all advancement; Khalaf bin Ayyub allows it only after Ramadan begins; Nuh bin Abi Maryam allows after mid-Ramadan; and some restrict it to the last ten days. The author declares the absolute permission as the correct position (al-sahih). This reflects the Hanafi position that once the cause is established, the obligation can be fulfilled in advance without restriction.

Key Terms
صدقۃ الفطر (Sadaqat al-Fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan per head of supported persons.
تقديم (taqdim): To pay the obligation before its designated time (Eid day).
سبب (sabab): The cause that makes the obligation due; here, possession of a head that one supports on the last day of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling regarding advancing Sadaqat al-Fitr before Eid?
A) It is not permissible at all.
B) It is permissible only after Ramadan begins.
C) It is permissible absolutely, with no time limit.
D) It is permissible only in the last ten days of Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows Sadaqat al-Fitr to be paid at any time before Eid once the cause is established, based on analogy to zakat and the practice of the Companions.
