Delaying Sadaqat al-Fitr After Eid Does Not Fall Off
Ruling with proof on delaying Fitrana

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Sadaqat al-Fitr and explain why it remains wajib, using the distinction between rational and non-rational acts of worship.

Core Idea
A financial obligation with a rational purpose never expires with time.

Many people assume that Sadaqat al-Fitr (Fitrana) must be given on Eid day or else it is no longer required. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on delaying Fitrana and the proof behind it. We will see that the obligation remains until paid because it serves a continuous rational objective—meeting the needs of the poor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act under discussion (Sadaqat al-Fitr) and the Hanafi ruling: it remains wajib even if delayed after Eid day.
The act is a financial obligation; the dispute is about time restriction.
2
Recognize the dispute
Note that Hasan bin Ziyad held that it falls off after Eid day. Understand his proof: analogy with sacrifice (udhiyah), which is a non-rational worship tied to specific days.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the relied-upon position is that it does not fall off.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof distinguishes Sadaqat al-Fitr as ma'qulat al-ma'na (rational), like zakat, because its purpose (feeding the poor) is comprehensible and continuous. Therefore, it is not confined to a specific time.
Rational financial obligations do not become invalid when the preferred time passes.
4
Contrast with the opposing view
Compare with sacrifice, which is ghayr ma'qul (non-rational). The sacrifice's purpose (shedding blood for closeness) is not comprehensible to reason, so it is confined to its specific occasion.
This contrast shows how the nature of the act determines its time flexibility.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that if someone delays Fitrana, it remains a debt on them. They must pay it as soon as possible, no matter how late.
Practical consequence: Fitrana does not become qada like a prayer; it is simply delayed performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ اَخِرُوهَا عَنْ يَوْمِ الْفِطْرِ لَمْ تَسْقُطُ وَكَانَ عَلَيْهِمْ إِخْرَاجُهَا لِأَنَّ وَجَدَ الْقُرْبَةِ فِيهَا مَعْقُولُ فَلَا يَتَقَدَّرُ وَقْتُ الْآدَاءِ فِيهَا بِخِلَافِ الأَضْحِيَّةِ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ ترجمہ اور اگر لوگوں نے صدقہ کو عید الفطر سے مؤخر کر دیا تو یہ صدقہ (ان کے ذمہ سے) ساقط نہ ہو گا اور ان پر اس کا نکالنا واجب رہے گا کیونکہ اس صدقہ میں قربت کی وجہ معقول ہے تو اس صدقہ میں ادا کا وقت مقدر نہ ہوگا بر خلاف قربانی کے۔ تشریح اور اگر لوگوں نے عید کے دن فطرہ ادا نہ کیا اور عید کا دن گذر گیا تو صدقہ ان کے ذمہ سے ساقط نہ ہو گا بلکہ ان پر واجب رہے گا اور ان پر اس کا نکالنا لازم ہوگا خواہ کتنی ہی تاخیر ہو جائے اور حسن بن زیاد نے کہا کہ عید کا دن گذرتے ہی ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ صدقہ ایسی عبادت ہے جو عید الفطر کے دن کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے پس قربانی کے مانند ہو گیا کہ جس طرح قربانی ایام الضحیہ گذرنے سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہے اسی طرح صدقہ بھی عید کا دن گزرتے ہی ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صدقۃ الفطر میں عبادت اور قربت کی وجہ معقول ہے کیونکہ یہ مالی صدقہ ہے اور ہر وقت فقراء کی حاجت دور کرنے کے لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے لھذا اس میں ادا کا کوئی وقت متعین نہ ہوگا اور وجوب کے بعد زکوۃ کی طرح بغیر ادا کے ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ برخلاف قربانی کے کہ اس میں قربت خون بہانا ہے اور خون کا بہانا عبادت غیر معقولہ ہے جیسا کہ اردو شاعر نے کہا ہے عجیب ماجرا بروز عید قرباں ی قتل بھی کرے ہے وہی لے ثواب الٹا پس جب یہ عبادت غیر معقولہ اور خلاف قیاس ہے تو اپنے مورد پر منحصر رہے گا اور حدیث کے مطابق قربانی صرف ایام اضحیہ میں ہو سکتی ہے اس لئے اگر کسی نے ایام اضحیہ میں قربانی نہیں کی اور یہ دن گزر گئے تو اس کے ذمہ سے قربانی ساقط ہو جائے گی البتہ اس جانور کا صدقہ کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
If they delay it after the day of Fitr, it does not fall off, and they must still give it, because the aspect of seeking closeness in it is rational (ma'qul), so the time of performance is not fixed, unlike the sacrifice. Translation: And if people delay the sadaqah after the day of Eid al-Fitr, this sadaqah will not fall from their liability, and they remain obligated to give it; because the aspect of closeness in this sadaqah is rational, therefore the time of performance is not fixed, unlike the sacrifice. Explanation: If people do not pay Fitrana on the day of Eid and the day passes, the sadaqah does not fall off; rather it remains obligatory and must be given no matter how long the delay. Hasan bin Ziyad said that it falls off as soon as the day of Eid passes, because this sadaqah is an act of worship specific to the day of Eid, thus resembling the sacrifice, which falls off after the days of Adha pass. Our proof is that in Sadaqat al-Fitr, the worship and aspect of closeness is rational, because it is a financial charity prescribed at all times to fulfill the needs of the poor; therefore the time of performance is not fixed, and like zakat, it does not fall off without performance. Unlike sacrifice, where the act of closeness is shedding blood, and shedding blood is an act of worship that is non-rational (ghayr ma'qul), as a poet said: 'A strange event on Eid day: the sacrifice kills and still gets reward upside down.' So when this worship is non-rational and contrary to analogy, it is confined to its specific occasion, and according to hadith, sacrifice can only be in the days of Adha; therefore if someone does not sacrifice in those days and they pass, the sacrifice falls from liability, but he must give the animal in charity. And Allah knows best. Jameel Ahmad 'Afiy 'anhu.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the effect of delaying Sadaqat al-Fitr after Eid. The author asserts that delaying does not remove the obligation; it remains a debt. The reasoning is that Sadaqat al-Fitr is a rational act of worship (ma'qulat al-ma'na) because it is a financial charity serving a rational purpose (feeding the poor). Therefore, its time is not fixed, just like zakat. The opposite view of Hasan bin Ziyad is presented: he analogizes it to sacrifice (udhiyah), which is a non-rational worship (ghayr ma'qulat al-ma'na), restricted to specific days. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the two: sacrifice is a bodily ritual with a fixed time, while Sadaqat al-Fitr is financial and ongoing. If one delays after Eid, the obligation persists. The text also notes that if sacrifice is missed, the animal must be given in charity. The poetic couplet illustrates the paradoxical nature of sacrifice (killing an animal for reward) showing it is non-rational.

Key Terms
مؤخر (mu'akhkhar): Delayed payment of an obligation beyond its preferred time.
معقول المعنى (ma'qulat al-ma'na): An act of worship whose underlying rationale is comprehensible by reason (e.g., charity for the poor).
ساقط (saqit): Falling off, i.e., the obligation is no longer due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what happens if someone fails to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr on Eid day?
A) It falls off because the specific time has passed.
B) It remains wajib and must be paid later.
C) It becomes makruh but is still valid if given later.
D) It must be given as a sacrifice instead.

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr, being a rational financial obligation, does not fall off if delayed; it must be paid whenever possible.

Sadaqat al-Fitr Not Voided by Delay Beyond Eid
Ruling on fitra when delayed after Eid, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delayed Sadaqat al-Fitr and explain why the majority rejects Hasan ibn Ziyad's analogy with Udhiyah.

Core Idea
Fitrah remains wajib after Eid because it is a rational worship (ma'qul al-ma'na), unlike Udhiyah which is non-rational.

This passage addresses a common question: what happens if one fails to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr (Fitrah) on the day of Eid? Does the obligation fall off, or does it remain? The Hanafi school's majority holds that it remains, but a minority view from Hasan ibn Ziyad claims it becomes void. Understanding the reasoning behind this difference is essential for applying the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi ruling on delayed Fitrah
Identify the main ruling: the Fitrah does not become void if delayed; it remains wajib until paid.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Recognize the opposing view and its basis
Note that Hasan ibn Ziyad argues that Fitrah becomes void after Eid, analogizing it to Udhiyah (sacrifice).
His view is a Nawadir transmission, not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Identify the key distinction: rational vs. non-rational worship
Understand that the majority rejects the analogy because Fitrah is a financial worship with a rational cause (meeting the needs of the poor), while Udhiyah is a non-rational worship (bloodshed) confined to its specific time.
Rational acts (ma'qul al-ma'na) are not time-bound; non-rational acts (ghayr ma'qul) are.
4
Apply the principle to the dispute
Since Fitrah has a rational cause, it is not restricted to Eid day. Obligation continues until performance, like Zakat.
The text also mentions that if Udhiyah is missed, the animal must be given as charity, not that the obligation is completely dropped.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The majority view from Zahir al-Riwayah is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Thus, delayed Fitrah must still be paid.

Kitab al-Zakat. Translation. 121. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume. And if people delay the charity (Sadaqat al-Fitr) after Eid al-Fitr, then this charity will not be voided from their responsibility, and extracting it remains obligatory upon them, because in this charity the cause of closeness (to Allah) is rational, so in this charity the time of performance is not predetermined, unlike sacrifice. Commentary: And if people do not pay Fitrah on the day of Eid and the day of Eid passes, then the charity will not be voided from their responsibility; rather it remains obligatory upon them and it is necessary for them to pay it, no matter how much delay occurs. And Hasan ibn Ziyad said that as soon as the day of Eid passes, it becomes void, because charity is a worship specific to the day of Eid al-Fitr, so it becomes like sacrifice; just as sacrifice becomes void with the passing of the days of sacrifice, similarly charity will become void as soon as the day of Eid passes. Our evidence is that in Sadaqat al-Fitr, the reason for worship and closeness is rational, because it is financial charity and was legislated to fulfill the needs of the poor at all times, therefore no specific time of performance is determined for it, and after obligation it will not be voided without performance, like zakat. Contrary to sacrifice, because in it, closeness is through shedding blood, and shedding blood is a non-rational worship, as an Urdu poet said: 'A strange affair on the day of Eid: sacrifice, even killing, and he receives reward in reverse.' So when this worship is non-rational and contrary to analogy, it remains confined to its specific context, and according to hadith, sacrifice can only be performed during the days of sacrifice. Therefore, if someone did not sacrifice during the days of sacrifice and those days passed, then sacrifice is voided from his responsibility; however, it is obligatory for him to give that animal in charity. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, forgiven.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of Sadaqat al-Fitr (Fitrah) when it is delayed past Eid al-Fitr. The author first states the ruling: the Fitrah does not become void if delayed; it remains obligatory. He then provides a more detailed commentary, noting that even if the day of Eid passes, the obligation remains. He then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Hasan ibn Ziyad held that the Fitrah becomes void after Eid, analogizing it to Udhiyah (sacrificial animal) because both are specific to a particular day. The majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) reject this analogy. The evidence provided is that Fitrah is a financial charity with a rational cause (ma'qul al-ma'na): it addresses the ongoing needs of the poor, so it is not time-bound. It is analogous to Zakat, which does not become void if delayed. In contrast, sacrifice (Udhiyah) is a non-rational worship (ghayr ma'qul) involving bloodshed, which is not intrinsically understood by reason; hence it is confined to its specific time. The passage also quotes an Urdu poet's verse to emphasize the peculiar nature of sacrifice. The conclusion: if one fails to sacrifice during the appointed days, the obligation of sacrifice is dropped, but one must still give the animal in charity. This distinction is based on the principle that acts with rational causes are not confined to specific times, while acts with non-rational causes are. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the majority: Fitrah is not voided by delay.

Key Terms
صدقہ فطر (Sadaqat al-Fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, before Eid al-Fitr prayer.
قربانی (Qurbani / Udhiyah): The sacrificial animal offered during the days of Eid al-Adha.
عبادت غیر معقولہ (Ibadah ghayr ma'qulah): A worship whose rationale is not comprehensible by human reason; it is performed solely due to divine command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the Hanafi school, what happens if a person delays paying Sadaqat al-Fitr until after the day of Eid?
A) The obligation is voided and no payment is needed.
B) The obligation remains and must be fulfilled later.
C) It becomes a sin but no longer requires payment.
D) It is converted to a different type of charity.

Key Takeaway
Fitrah is not voided by delay; it remains wajib until paid because it is a rational worship (ma'qul al-ma'na) unlike the non-rational act of sacrifice.
